### `admin/automations/` — automation editor + test-send (Phase 5 · Cluster 3 · Session B)

> **Architectural note — the editor lives at `/automations/[id]`** inside the shared `/automations` route tree (Next won't allow it inside `(admin)` simultaneously). The page is a `'use client'` dispatcher that role-gates internally: admin renders the editor; client falls back through `router.replace('/automations')` since there's no client editor. The `[id]` slug is decorative for the stub layer — the single canonical FreshHome 24h follow-up renders regardless of id. Admin Screen 10's `AutomationFlowMini` rows already carry `href` values pointing here from Session A.

- **`AutomationEditorLayout`** (`automations/AutomationEditorLayout.tsx`) — `1fr 340px` two-column wizard shell (canvas + sticky right rail). Canvas is wrapped in a white card surface (`rounded-xl border border-rule bg-card px-7 py-6.5`); the rail is a plain `sticky top-[100px]` flex-col. **3rd `1fr + fixed-rail` detail layout** alongside `TicketDetailLayout` + the inline lead-detail shape — see parked decisions for layout-shell consolidation.
- **`AutomationTriggerBox`** (`automations/AutomationTriggerBox.tsx`) — ink-bg trigger row with the rust ⚡ icon + `// TRIGGER` mono label + the trigger name + a rust-light "Change trigger →" affordance. `1fr` middle column holds the trigger summary.
- **`AutomationStepConnector`** (`automations/AutomationStepConnector.tsx`) — small 2px rule-coloured vertical line, centred between the trigger and each step. Pure decorative, `aria-hidden`.
- **`AutomationEditorStep`** (`automations/AutomationEditorStep.tsx`) — `'use client'` editable step. Header is a 6-col grid: numbered ink circle (rust-light digit) + channel pill (`sms` = good, `email` = info) + delay pill (mono with ◷ glyph) + editable name input + ↕ reorder + × delete (icon buttons via the inner `StepIconBtn`). Body: optional subject input (email only) + the message body in a tinted card with `[data-slot=var]` highlighting. `isEditing: true` flips the header bg to rust-soft, the body border to rust + rust-glow shadow, and tints the footerMeta rust. Footer: the meta string + the variable chip row (always leads with a "+ Insert variable" rust-soft chip). Inputs are local state — wire to backend when real save lands.
- **`AutomationAddStep`** (`automations/AutomationAddStep.tsx`) — dashed-border `+ Add another step (SMS / Email / Wait)` affordance. Hover-flips to rust border + rust-soft fill. **Superseded by `AutomationAddActionMenu` in Phase 8 · Session 3** for the live editor — `AutomationAddStep` stays as an inert visual primitive only.
- **`AutomationActionCard`** (`automations/AutomationActionCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` Phase 8 · Session 3. The canonical editable action card backing the `/automations/[id]` editor — replaces the comm-only `AutomationEditorStep` with a per-action-type body discriminator. Header: position circle + type pill (`sms` good, `email` info, `wait` quiet, `operator` amber, `update` plum, `task` rust) + "pauses on client reply" hint + up/down/× icon buttons. Body switches on `actionType`: comm actions → inline textarea + (email) subject input + a `Insert variable:` chip row (click splices `{{variable}}` at the cursor via `lib/editor/insert-at-cursor.ts`); `wait_for_duration` → minutes number input; `update_lead_field` → field + value selects; `create_followup_task` → optional hint input; `send_operator_notification` → variant label. All edits flow up through `onChange` (discriminated `{ kind: 'body' | 'config' }`) — parent owns the React-Query mutation.
- **`AutomationAddActionMenu`** (`automations/AutomationAddActionMenu.tsx`) — `'use client'` Phase 8 · Session 3. Dashed-border "+ Add another action" button + Dialog-based type picker listing all six closed `action_type` enum values with per-type tone pill + description. Picks one → `onPick(actionType)` → parent appends a fresh action via `useAddAction`. Replaces the inert `AutomationAddStep` on the live editor.
- **`AutomationVariableList`** (`automations/AutomationVariableList.tsx`) — right-rail card listing the 7 available variables. Each row: mono rust `{code}` + ink-quiet description + rust "+" affordance. Hover-tinted rust-soft.
- **`AutomationTestSendCard`** (`automations/AutomationTestSendCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` right-rail card that owns the modal `open` state. Heading + description + full-width ink button (hover-flips to rust). Mounts `AutomationTestSendModal` underneath.
- **`AutomationPerformanceCard`** (`automations/AutomationPerformanceCard.tsx`) — right-rail card with N rows of `label : value`. Per-row value tint: `accent` = rust, `good` = good-green, `default` = ink-bold. Dotted bottom rules between rows.

### `shared/automations/` — test-send modal (Phase 5 · Cluster 3 · Session B)

### `shared/` — editor-mode footer actions (Phase 5 · Cluster 3 · Session B)

- **`EditorFooterActions`** (`EditorFooterActions.tsx`) — sibling to `BuilderFooterActions` (the wizard footer). Built separately because the interaction model differs: editor footers carry an "auto-saved" mono progress indicator + a 3-button action set (Back / Disable / Save) rather than the wizard's 2-button Back/Continue. No top border by default — the canvas above already carries its own card border; centred `mt-7` gap separates the rows. Used by the automation editor today; future editors (e.g. page builder) should reuse it. See parked decisions for the "revisit when a third footer-actions variant appears" rule.

### `shared/search/` — global search (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · Session 2)

> **Architectural note — `/search` is a shared route.** `app/search/` has its own `layout.tsx` ('use client', `useRole()`, picks sidebar, mounts `DevRoleSwitcher`). `page.tsx` is a `'use client'` dispatcher that picks the role-scoped stub and renders the shared `SearchResultsView` — no `_admin-content` / `_client-content` siblings, because the two role bodies are structurally identical (same view, different data). Operators search across every client (admin Screen 35); a client searches their own account. `page.tsx` wraps the body in `<Suspense>` because it reads `?q=` via `useSearchParams`.

- **`GlobalSearchInput`** (`search/GlobalSearchInput.tsx`) — `'use client'` rounded-pill search field (⌕ icon + input + decorative `⌘K` hint). Enter routes to `/search?q=…`. As of Session 7 the `Topbar` auto-renders it for every operator-role page (the rollout is complete — see the `Topbar` entry); pages pass it explicitly only to seed a value (`/search` seeds the current query), or set `hideSearch` to suppress it (admin leads + tickets inboxes, which carry their own in-body search).
- **`SearchResultRow`** (`search/SearchResultRow.tsx`) — single result row, a `next/link`: kind-tinted 40px avatar tile (initials for people, glyph otherwise) + title + meta (both run through `highlightMatch`) + `→`. `KIND_TILE` maps the six `SearchResultKind`s to tone classes.
- **`SearchResultGroup`** (`search/SearchResultGroup.tsx`) — one per-kind group: mono label + ink count chip header, then a bordered card of `SearchResultRow`s.
- **`SearchResultsView`** (`search/SearchResultsView.tsx`) — the shared `/search` body: an ink result-count summary strip + the per-kind groups. Role-agnostic — operator and client pass their own `SearchResults`.

### `lib/search/` — global search data + types

- **`types.ts`** — `SearchResultKind` (`lead | booking | review | conversation | customer | client`), `SearchResult` (`{ id, kind, avatar, title, meta, href }` — each result a typed entity with a real detail `href`), `SearchResultGroup`, `SearchResults`.
- **`highlight.tsx`** — `highlightMatch(text, query)` → ReactNode, wrapping case-insensitive query matches in a rust `<mark>`.

### `shared/` — rail-card primitives (Phase 6 · Cluster 6)

> The canonical white-card side-rail pattern. Extracted in Cluster 6 (mechanical rename) from the previously-separate `TicketSideCard` / `TicketPropertyRow` (tickets + bookings) and `LeadRailCard` / `LeadRailRowItem` (leads) — all four deleted, no re-export shims. Used by the tickets, leads, and bookings detail rails, and the single-client overview hub.

- **`RailCard`** (`RailCard.tsx`) — right-rail card wrapper. Props: `heading` (mono uppercase string, e.g. `// Status`), `tone: 'light' | 'dark'` (default light = white card with `border-ink/8`; dark = ink-bg paper-text — used by `TicketStatusCard`), optional `rows: RailRow[]` shorthand (each row renders as a mono-labelled `RailPropertyRow`), `children` (for bespoke bodies — status pickers, action lists). `rounded-[14px] px-5 py-[18px]`. `RailRow` (`{ label, value, accent?, tone? }`) is structurally compatible with `lib/leads/types.ts` `LeadRailRow` — feature types stay put (same pattern as `FilterChips`).
- **`RailPropertyRow`** (`RailPropertyRow.tsx`) — single label/value row inside a `RailCard`. Props: `label` (string) + `value` (ReactNode) + `editable` (boolean — appends a mono `✎` glyph) + `tone: 'good' | 'quiet' | 'default'` (value colour) + `accent` (boolean — rust value, overrides `tone`) + `labelStyle: 'plain' | 'mono'` (default `plain` — quiet sentence-case label for tickets/bookings; `mono` — mono uppercase label, used by the leads rail rows). `space-between` flex, dotted bottom rule between rows, suppressed on the last. Tighter than `SettingsFieldRow` because the 320px side panel can't carry settings' 220px label column.

### `shared/` — activity feed (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · Session 1a)

> The canonical flat activity-log card. Extracted at the third-surface trigger (the single-client overview hub) from the previously-sibling `CampaignActivityCard`. **`LeadTimeline` is deliberately NOT consolidated here** — a timeline (dot-spine, scheduled-future pending events, tinted snippet quotes, gapped rows) is a different structural concern from a flat feed; folding it in would re-create the optional-slot grab-bag. The two coexist by design.

- **`ActivityRow`** (`ActivityRow.tsx`) — one feed row. `row: ActivityRowData` does the work; `ActivityRowData` is **event-shaped** per vision §7 — `{ id, icon, tone, actor?, body, detail?, time, href? }`, a typed attributable event, not rendered prose. `tone: ActivityTone` is a colour-keyed vocabulary (`info | amber | good | rust`) — consumers map their own domain categories onto these slots. `grid-cols-[32px_1fr_auto]`: tone-tinted 32px icon tile + body (rust-bold `actor` + `body` + quiet `detail` block) + right-aligned mono `time`. Dotted bottom rule between rows. Renders as a `next/link` when `href` is set.
- **`ActivityFeed`** (`ActivityFeed.tsx`) — white-card wrapper: `title` (ReactNode, `<em>` = rust) + optional `sub` (`<strong>` = ink-bold) + optional `action` (header-right ReactNode, e.g. an "All →" link — added Cluster 6 · 1b) + a stack of `ActivityRow`s from `items: ActivityRowData[]`. `rounded-xl border border-rule bg-card px-6 py-5.5`. Used by client `/campaigns` (via the `CampaignActivityCard` adapter) and the single-client overview hub.

### `shared/reviews/` + `client/reviews/` — `/reviews` page (Phase 5 · Cluster 4 · Session A)

> **Architectural note — reviews lives outside the role route groups**, same reason as settings / tickets / leads / calendar / automations / dashboard. Single shared route `app/reviews/` with `'use client'` layout (reads `useRole()`, picks `ClientSidebar` vs `AdminSidebar`, mounts `DevRoleSwitcher`) + `'use client'` dispatcher `page.tsx` + `_client-content.tsx` / `_admin-content.tsx` siblings. Client renders a single-business reviews surface (client Screen 6) + the negative-review intercept modal (prototype admin Screen 24 — relocated to client side, see prototype-disagreement note below); admin renders a cross-client per-client-card grid (admin Screen 12). The two role bodies share `ReviewSummaryHeader` (sized down inside the per-client card) and `ReviewItem` (with `variant: 'full' | 'compact'`) — single canonical components, no role-specific duplicates.
>
> **Prototype-disagreement note — negative-review alert is client-side, not admin.** The platform prototype mounts the 2★ alert modal on admin Screen 24 ("Call Jamie immediately to apologise" framed as the operator's action). In practice the business owner is the one with the customer relationship and the one who'd actually call back; the operator's role here is to be informed and to adjust ad copy if a pattern emerges. The modal lives in `shared/reviews/` (reusable shape) but its only mount today is on client `/reviews` via `client/reviews/NegativeReviewAlertButton`. If a future operator-facing "FreshHome just got a 2★" surfacing lands in Cluster 6, build that as a sibling — don't shoehorn it into this modal.

- **`ReviewSummaryHeader`** (`reviews/ReviewSummaryHeader.tsx`) — big rating block (Inter Tight rating value with `<em>` rust on the ★ glyph + stars-row + mono meta line). `size: 'lg' | 'sm'` controls scale (56px headline on client Screen 6; 26px headline inside admin per-client cards). `align: 'left' | 'right'` so the same component can sit left-aligned in the client summary and right-aligned in the admin per-client card header. Single canonical — don't sibling per-surface.
- **`ReviewDistributionBars`** (`reviews/ReviewDistributionBars.tsx`) — 5★→1★ horizontal bar chart driven by `ReviewDistributionRow[]` (stars / count / pct). Rust-fill on paper-2 track, mono labels. Used by client `/reviews` today; lives in `shared/` so admin can reuse if a future single-client admin drill-down appears.
- **`ReviewCallout`** (`reviews/ReviewCallout.tsx`) — ink-bg "Asked, not begged." motivational card on the right of the client summary row. ReactNode `headline` (`<em>` = rust-light on ink) + sub line + a rust-light mono link.
- **`ReviewItem`** (`reviews/ReviewItem.tsx`) — single canonical Google review entry, discriminated by `variant`. **`full`** (client Screen 6) = `44px avatar + 1fr body + 100px stars + 80px age` grid with name + job + quote + filled-star row + mono age. **`compact`** (admin per-client cards) = `1fr text + auto right-aligned stars-and-age` with `<strong>Name</strong> · "quote"` and right-aligned `★★★ · age`. Same data shape, two layouts.
- **`ReviewMiniStat`** (`reviews/ReviewMiniStat.tsx`) — small stat tile inside admin per-client cards (NEW · 7D / 5-STAR / REQUEST → REVIEW). 20px Inter Tight value + mono uppercase label. Smaller than `StatCard`, intentionally — sits inside a 3-up grid inside an already-bordered card.
- **`ReviewClientCard`** (`reviews/ReviewClientCard.tsx`) — admin per-client card. White card composing logo + name+meta header row + right-aligned `ReviewSummaryHeader` (size `sm` + align `right`) + 3-up `ReviewMiniStat` grid + `// RECENT` block of `ReviewItem` (compact). Discriminated by `card.kind` — `connected` renders the full content; `empty` (Voltline pre-launch) renders an opacity-dimmed card with description + "Connect Google Business" CTA.
- **`NegativeReviewActionRow`** (`shared/reviews/NegativeReviewActionRow.tsx`) — numbered suggested-action row inside the negative-review modal. 3-column grid: 24px ink/rust-light digit circle + 1fr title+sub body + auto right-aligned "Recommended" pill. `recommended: true` flips the row to rust-soft bg + rust border + shows the pill. Structurally close to `shared/bookings/ConflictOptionRow` but adds the visible pill column — parked-decision: extract a generic numbered-option-row shared primitive on the third instance.
- **`NegativeReviewModal`** (`shared/reviews/NegativeReviewModal.tsx`) — `'use client'` Dialog (size `default` = 560px). Same viewport-safe header / scrollable body / footer rhythm as `NewBookingModal` (`p-0 gap-0` on `DialogContent`, custom paper-2 close button, paper footer with paper-2 top border). Header: warn-tinted tag (with leading warn dot) + 24px rust-em title + subtitle. Body: centered 56px warn-soft `!` icon + warn-tinted quote block (stars + italic quote + mono meta with `<strong>` ink emphasis) + numbered `NegativeReviewActionRow` list. Footer: muted footer info (`<strong>` = ink) + Dismiss / Call buttons (both close the modal — wire to real call/dismiss when backend lands). Lives in `shared/` (reusable shape); currently only mounted on client `/reviews`.
- **`NegativeReviewAlertButton`** (`client/reviews/NegativeReviewAlertButton.tsx`) — `'use client'` trigger button + modal-open state owner. Stub-only entry point: the real build fires the modal from a low-rating webhook the moment Google surfaces a sub-4★ review, but the stub layer mounts a "⚠ Show 2★ alert" secondary `Button` next to the client `/reviews` `PageHeader`. Delete the button (and the data import) when the webhook trigger lands; keep `NegativeReviewModal` either way.

### `lib/reviews/` — reviews stub data + types

- **`types.ts`** — single source of truth for review shapes: `ReviewItem` (data shape used by both row variants), `ReviewDistributionRow`, `ReviewSummaryData`, `ReviewMiniStat`, `ReviewClientCardData` (discriminated `kind: 'connected' | 'empty'`), `ReviewCalloutData`, `ClientReviewsPage`, `AdminReviewsPage`, and the negative-review modal shapes (`NegativeReviewActionData`, `NegativeReviewQuoteData`, `NegativeReviewModalData`).
- **`client-negative-modal.tsx`** — `voltlineNegativeReview`: Voltline 2★ Jamie K. stub (reframed from the prototype's KeyHero/admin-side copy — see prototype-disagreement note above). Quote + 4 suggested actions (action 1 recommended; action 4 = "Flag to Craig at Webnua for ad messaging review") + footer "first negative review in your first 14 days" reassurance. **Still a stub** — the negative-review alert modal is a stub interaction (`NegativeReviewAlertButton` demo trigger), not wired to live data.
- **`queries.tsx`** — **Phase 3 · the `/reviews` read surfaces are wired to live Supabase data.** `useClientReviews()` — the signed-in client's `ClientReviewsPage` (reads `clients` + `reviews`, both RLS-bounded; a client with zero reviews still resolves via the single `clients` row). `useAdminReviews()` — the operator `AdminReviewsPage`: one `ReviewClientCardData` per accessible client (`connected` when the client has reviews, `empty` otherwise) + the 4-up workspace stat row. **Phase 9b** added `useSubAccountReviews(clientSlug)` — the operator drilled into one client; renders the same single-business shape `useClientReviews` does, scoped to the active sub-account. The rating headline, the 5★→1★ distribution, the per-client mini-stats, the workspace stats and the relative age labels are all computed here from `reviews.stars` / `reviews.reviewed_at` per design §5. Hero copy is composed in the query (the client eyebrow carries the client name). The `client-reviews.tsx` / `admin-reviews.tsx` stub files were removed in the Phase 3 dead-stub cleanup; the `types.ts` shapes stay live.

### `shared/campaigns/` + `admin/campaigns/` — `/campaigns` page (Phase 5 · Cluster 4 · Session B)

> **Architectural note — campaigns lives outside the role route groups**, same reason as reviews / settings / tickets / etc. Single shared route `app/campaigns/` with `'use client'` layout + `'use client'` dispatcher + `_client-content.tsx` / `_admin-content.tsx` siblings. The two role bodies render **different shapes** — client is a single-campaign deep dive (managed band + active hero card + 4-week trend chart + activity log + change CTA); admin is a flat cross-client roster (filter chips + 4 workspace stats + N campaign rows + Meta Ads info bar). Intentionally not converged — they're genuinely different surfaces (single-campaign view vs multi-campaign roster), and forcing a shared shell would only produce a grab-bag of optional slots.

- **`CampaignManagedBand`** (`campaigns/CampaignManagedBand.tsx`) — ink-bg reassurance band at the top of client `/campaigns`. 3-column grid: 56px rust-tinted icon tile + tag/title/sub body (`<em>` = rust-light, `<strong>` = paper-bold) + ghost "Text Craig" CTA on the right. Standalone — distinct from `AutomationInfoBanner` (rust-soft chip) and from `BillingPlanCard` (plan-meta + headline + action). If a second ink-bg "managed by your operator" band lands elsewhere on the client side, revisit extraction.
- **`CampaignMetricTile`** (`campaigns/CampaignMetricTile.tsx`) — single metric tile inside the active-campaign hero. 10px mono uppercase label + 32px Inter Tight value (`<em>` = rust) + sub trend line with `trendTone: 'good' | 'warn' | 'quiet'`. Sized larger than `StatCard` (32px vs 30px) AND lives inside a parent card with no border of its own — the 1px paper-2 gap between tiles comes from the parent's grid background trick.
- **`CampaignPlainEnglish`** (`campaigns/CampaignPlainEnglish.tsx`) — rust-soft tinted "In plain English" explainer card. 2-column grid: 32px rust circle with `i` glyph + ReactNode body (`<em>` = rust bold, `<strong>` = ink-bold). Sits below the metric grid inside the active-campaign hero.
- **`CampaignHeroCard`** (`campaigns/CampaignHeroCard.tsx`) — active-campaign hero on client `/campaigns`. White card composing header row (pulsing-good-dot eyebrow + 22px name with `<em>` rust + meta line + good-soft status pill) + 4-tile `CampaignMetricTile` grid with 1px paper-2 separators + a `CampaignPlainEnglish` block in the footer. Single-campaign surface — admin has no equivalent.
- **`CampaignTrendChart`** (`campaigns/CampaignTrendChart.tsx`) — CSS-only 4-week grouped-bar chart (leads vs spend). Hand-rolled with a 60px y-axis column + a 1fr bars area; each week column renders two stacked-end bars (leads filled rust / spend paper-2 outlined) scaled against `leadsMax` / `spendMax`. Bar labels float above their bars; the "current" week gets a rust glow shadow + rust week label. No chart library — the prototype shape is small enough that hand-rolling is cleaner than pulling in a dep; revisit if a second chart shape lands elsewhere.
- **`CampaignActivityCard`** (`campaigns/CampaignActivityCard.tsx`) — "What Webnua's done lately" activity log on client `/campaigns`. **As of Cluster 6 · Session 1a this is a thin domain adapter** over the shared `ActivityFeed` (see the `shared/` activity-feed entry above): it maps the campaign activity-category vocabulary (`creative`/`audience`/`budget`/`tune`) onto `ActivityFeed`'s colour-keyed tone slots and shapes `CampaignActivityItem` into `ActivityRowData`. Keeps its `{ data, className }` API so `/campaigns` is unchanged; `CampaignActivityItem` stays uncoupled from the row shape.
- **`CampaignChangeCard`** (`campaigns/CampaignChangeCard.tsx`) — bottom "Want to change something?" CTA card on client `/campaigns`. White card + body text + N right-aligned `Button`s. Buttons render through the canonical `Button` primitive (`primary: true` → rust default; otherwise secondary).
- **`CampaignSparkline`** (`campaigns/CampaignSparkline.tsx`) — small inline SVG sparkline used on admin `/campaigns` rows. Rust stroke with a soft rust fill below the line; dashed flat-line when `points` is omitted (pre-launch / pending rows). Lives in `shared/` because it's generic enough to be reusable.
- **`CampaignStatusPill`** (`admin/campaigns/CampaignStatusPill.tsx`) — mono uppercase pill used on admin `/campaigns` rows. `active` = good-green with pulsing dot; `paused` / `pending` = ink-quiet with static dot. `label` overrides the status-keyed default. Distinct vocabulary from the existing tickets/leads status-pill families — kept as its own component; revisit if a third campaign-status surface appears.
- **`CampaignClientRow`** (`admin/campaigns/CampaignClientRow.tsx`) — admin-only cross-client roster row. 7-column grid: 36px ink-bg logo with rust-light glyph + 1.4fr name+meta + 110px `CampaignStatusPill` + three 100/110px metric cells (each with a ReactNode `value` for rust accent + small mono `sub`) + 100px `CampaignSparkline`. `row.dimmed` opacity-fades the whole row (used for Voltline pre-launch).

### `lib/campaigns/` — campaigns stub data + types

- **`types.ts`** — single source of truth for campaign shapes. Client side: `CampaignActivityIconTone` (`creative | audience | budget | tune`), `CampaignMetric`, `CampaignManagedBandData`, `CampaignHeroData`, `CampaignTrendWeek` + `CampaignTrendChartData`, `CampaignActivityItem` + `CampaignActivityData`, `CampaignChangeCardData`, top-level `ClientCampaignsPage`. Admin side: `AdminCampaignStatus` (`active | paused | pending`), `AdminCampaignRow`, top-level `AdminCampaignsPage` (hero + filters + stats + rows + footer info bar).
- **`queries.tsx`** — **Phase 3 · partial wire — the `/campaigns` pages are wired to live data for what the schema honestly carries.** `useClientCampaigns()` builds the client deep-dive (the running campaign, else most recent); `useAdminCampaigns()` builds the cross-client roster. **Phase 9b** added `useSubAccountCampaigns(clientSlug)` — the operator drilled into one client; renders the single-business deep-dive shape `useClientCampaigns` does, scoped to the active sub-account. **Schema gap (read the module header):** `campaigns` stores only the campaign *record* (name / status / budget / dates) and `campaign_activity_events` the operator activity log — there are **no performance-metric columns and no `campaign_metrics` table**. Leads / spend / CPL / ROAS / the 4-week trend / the row sparklines are Meta Ads integration data, not yet modelled (design §5 #7). So the record + the activity log are wired live (the activity log composes from `campaign_activity_events` joined to actor `users`); every metric renders an honest "Awaiting Meta Ads" placeholder, the client `trend` is omitted (`ClientCampaignsPage.trend` is now optional — the content file renders a placeholder card), and the admin row sparklines fall back to the dashed flatline. When the Meta Ads integration lands, replace the placeholders; the record + activity wiring stays. The `client-campaigns.tsx` / `admin-campaigns.tsx` stub files were removed in the Phase 3 dead-stub cleanup; `types.ts` shapes stay live.

### `lib/editor/` — generic editor helpers (Phase 8 · Session 3)

- **`insert-at-cursor.ts`** — pure splice-at-cursor helper for textarea / input fields used by click-to-insert variable chips. Exports `insertAtCursor(current, selectionStart, selectionEnd, insert) → { value, cursor }` (pure on the tuple — replaces any current selection) and `applyInsertToField(field, setValue, insert)` (the ref-aware wrapper that restores focus + caret on the next animation frame so React's re-render lands first). Used by `AutomationActionCard`'s variable chips and `PlatformTemplateEditor`'s chips. Add new editor surfaces that need click-to-insert via this helper rather than re-implementing the splice — that was the second-use trigger that justified extracting it.

### `lib/email/platform-templates-queries.tsx` — Phase 8 · Session 3

Operator-only data layer for `platform_email_templates` (migration 0079). Exports `PlatformTemplateKey` (`'lead_notification' | 'lead_digest'`), `PlatformEmailTemplate`, `usePlatformTemplates()` (the list read), `useUpdatePlatformTemplate()` (subject + body update — `body_html` is reflowed from the plain text on save), `LEAD_NOTIFICATION_VARIABLES` / `LEAD_DIGEST_VARIABLES` / `variablesForTemplate(key)` (the variable catalogs per template — drives the editor's chip row), and `renderTemplatePreview(template)` (substitutes the curated sample-context map for the preview pane). Backs `/settings/platform-templates`. The supabase client is cast through `as never` for now because `platform_email_templates` is not in the generated `Database` type yet (regen runs after the migration applies).

### `lib/auth/` — user + capability layer (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 1a)

The spine of the cluster 5 builder access model. See `reference/builder-design.md` §1 for full rationale. One editor renders for everyone; capabilities decide which controls are live. Role still drives sidebar shape (which nav set / workspace block); capabilities are the finer-grained layer inside the editor.

- **`capabilities.ts`** — single source of truth for the cap layer. 14 capabilities (`viewBuilder`, `editCopy`, `editMedia`, `editSEO`, `editLayout`, `editSections`, `editForms`, `editTheme`, `editPages`, `useAI`, `publish`, `approve`, `rollback`, `manageDomain`) — `editForms` (lead-capture form editing) was added with the form builder; see `reference/form-builder-design.md`. Exports `ALL_CAPABILITIES`, `ADMIN_DEFAULTS` (= all caps), `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` (= just `viewBuilder`), `CAPABILITY_LABEL` (`Record<Capability, string>` — the affirmative display name per cap, e.g. `editCopy → 'Edit page copy'`; the SoT for labelling a capability in any human-facing UI — added Cluster 6 · team invite), plus `Role`, `CapabilityGrant` (`{ userId, websiteId | '*', capabilities }` — shape stays preset-compatible per design doc §1.4 forward-compat note), and `User` (`{ id, displayName, email, role, clientId: string | null, capabilities: Set<Capability> }` — `clientId` is the user's home client business, null for operators; `capabilities` is **derived** from role defaults + grants every render). Force-publish is **not** a separate cap — break-glass discipline is UI + audit log layered on top of `publish`, gated at the call site by `role === 'admin'`.
- **`explainers.ts`** — `CAP_EXPLAINER: Record<Capability, { short, requestLabel }>` — the per-cap human strings surfaced by `<CapabilityGate>` (tooltip in `disable` mode, affordance label in `request` mode). Empty `requestLabel` opts a cap out of `request` mode entirely (currently `viewBuilder` + `approve`). Hardcoded "your operator" / "your account" — see the parked decision in Open decisions about an `{operatorLabel}` token for multi-operator deploys.
- **`user-stub.tsx`** — **real Supabase Auth** (the filename is misleading and kept only so the ~50 import sites stay untouched — this is NOT a stub). `<UserProvider>` resolves the signed-in user from a real Supabase session: `supabase.auth.getSession()` + `onAuthStateChange` → the `public.users` profile row → `capability_grants` rows → a `User` whose `capabilities` set is derived (`resolveCapabilities(role, grants)` — role defaults ∪ granted caps). Exports `<UserProvider>`, `useUser()` → `User | null`, `useUserContext()` (`{ user, effectiveCapabilities, hydrated, clearUser, refreshUser }`), `useCapabilities()` → `Set<Capability>`, `useCan(cap)` / `useCanAny` / `useCanAll`, a legacy `useRole()` shim (`{ role, hydrated, setRole (no-op), clearRole }` — `setRole` is dead, role comes from the signed-in profile), `<CapabilityOverrideProvider>` (locks the effective cap set to a fixed list for the wizard-frame editor), and `resolveCapabilities`. **No user-switching, no view-as, no localStorage, no stub users** — all removed when real auth landed (`7ceda3c` Phase 2, `341d19f` Phase 5). `clientId` resolves to the client's `slug`. The capability layer (`capabilities.ts` / `explainers.ts` / `resolver.ts`) is product code — it did not move; only how the user is *resolved* changed. **Sign-in:** `app/(auth)/login/page.tsx` is a real `supabase.auth.signInWithPassword` screen.
- **`audit-stub.ts`** — Phase 4: **type-only display module.** Just the `ForcePublishEntry` shape now. The audit log itself is the `force_publish_audit_log` table — entries are written by `lib/website/mutations.ts` (`publishDraft` with `force`) and read by `useForcePublishLog` (`lib/website/queries.tsx`). `/settings/access` consumes the live read via that hook. The previous localStorage overlay (`webnua.dev.audit-log`) + `appendForcePublishEntry` / `getEffectiveAuditLog` / `subscribeAudit` exports are gone.
- **`roster-store.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`** (PR #43). The users-with-grants list that backs the cap grid + the access roster on `/settings/access`. Combines `public.users` rows with their `capability_grants` so the grid can render every operator-known user with the websites they hold caps on. Snapshot-cached for `useSyncExternalStore` stability. The previous localStorage stub vanished with `DevRoleSwitcher`.

### `lib/data/` — auth-driven store hydration (Phase 5 · PR #43)

- **`DataHydrationProvider.tsx`** — mounted in `src/app/layout.tsx` inside `<UserProvider>`. The single point that pulls every Supabase-backed in-memory cache from the DB. On mount and on every `supabase.auth.onAuthStateChange`, calls `hydrateClients()` first (because the slug↔UUID map is the spine every other store depends on), then fires the rest in parallel: agency-policy, policy-overrides, plan-catalog, plan-assignments, client-invites, seat-limit history, team-invites, roster. Each store's `hydrate*()` function reads its table via the anon Supabase client (so RLS bounds the rows). A logged-out page load produces a wall of `401 permission denied` console warnings — the `anon` role correctly refuses; the stores hydrate properly on sign-in. **Two-second knock-on:** every store is a `useSyncExternalStore` snapshot-cached store, so hydration must bump the version counter exactly once at the end of each `hydrate*()` — never mid-loop — or the snapshot stability rule breaks.

### `lib/clients/` (cont'd) — client roster store

- **`clients-store.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider` first** (slug↔UUID is the spine every other store depends on — PR #43). Replaces the previous static `lib/nav/admin-clients.ts` source for the live roster: hydrates from `public.clients`, exposes `getClientUuidBySlug(slug)` / `getClientSlugByUuid(uuid)` / `getAllClients()` / `subscribeClients()`. `lib/clients/queries.tsx` `useClientId(slug)` resolves through this; `lib/clients/seat-limit-stub.ts` uses it too. `create-client.ts` calls `hydrateClients()` after a successful insert so the new client appears in the sidebar picker immediately.

### `lib/team/` (cont'd) — team-invite store (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 + PR #43)

- **`team-invite-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider` (PR #43 — net-new in that PR; there was no localStorage predecessor).** Operator-side team-invite list backed by `team_invites`. `addTeamInvite` writes through; `getAllTeamInvites` (snapshot-cached), `subscribeTeamInvites`. Sibling of `lib/invites/client-invite-stub.ts` — the same Supabase-cache + version-counter + `useSyncExternalStore` shape, different table + different lifecycle.

### `lib/website/` — website data model + section registry (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 2)

The data shape every later session builds against. See `reference/builder-design.md` §2 for the full design. Single-shape versioning (drafts and published share `Version`, distinguished by `status`). Section data is `Record<string, unknown>` at the registry boundary — each section type's actual shape is exported from its own module and asserted at the Fields/Preview component boundary.

- **`types.ts`** — `Website` (`{ id, clientId, name, domain, draftVersionId, publishedVersionId | null, createdAt, updatedAt }` — no `brand`, that lives on the Client now), `Page` (`{ id, websiteId, slug, title, type: PageType, sections[], seo, createdAt, updatedAt }`), `Section` (`{ id, type: SectionType, enabled, data, ai? }`), `Version` (`{ id, websiteId, status, snapshot: { pages, header, footer, nav, pageOrder }, createdBy/At, publishedAt/By?, notes?, parentVersionId? }`), `NavLink` (`{ label, target: { kind: 'page', pageId } | { kind: 'href', href } }`), `BrandObject` + `VoiceTone` (kept here for now — both Funnel and Website consume them; backend pass can hoist to `lib/brand/types.ts`), `WebsiteDomain`, `ContainerKind` (`'page' | 'funnelStep' | 'websiteHeader' | 'websiteFooter'` — drives the registry's singleton constraint). **11 section types**: `hero | offer | trust | services | reviews | faq | cta | schedulePicker | thanksConfirmation | header | footer` — the last two are website-level singletons (see registry). **5 page types**: `home | about | services | contact | generic` (funnel page types removed — those live in `lib/funnel/types.ts`). `MAX_NAV_LINKS = 6` const exports the V1 forcing-function cap (design doc §2.5).

- **`registry.ts`** — `SectionTypeDefinition<TData>` (`{ type, label, description, defaultData, Fields, Preview, capabilityHints?, allowedContainers, allowedPageTypes?, implemented }`). `allowedContainers: readonly ContainerKind[]` enforces singleton vs stackable semantics: `'header'`/`'footer'` have `allowedContainers: ['websiteHeader' | 'websiteFooter']` and are not stackable in `Page.sections[]`; stackable types use `['page', 'funnelStep']`; funnel-only types (`schedulePicker`, `thanksConfirmation`) use `['funnelStep']`. `defineSection<TData>(def)` is a type-preserving helper for registrations.

- **`sections/index.ts`** — the canonical const array `SECTION_REGISTRY` (no mutable registry; immutable list at module load). Order: stackable types first (hero / offer / trust / services / reviews / faq / cta), then funnel-only (schedulePicker / thanksConfirmation), then website-level singletons (header / footer). Accessors: `getSectionDefinition(type)`, `getImplementedSections()`, `getPlaceholderSections()`, `getSectionsForContainer(container: ContainerKind)`. Re-exports every section's `*Data` type for typed consumers. **Client-only consumers (the editor) read this.** Server-side consumers (the generation route's prompt builder + validation pipeline) MUST read `registry-meta.ts` instead — see the next entry.

- **`sections/registry-meta.ts`** — server-safe SSOT for section metadata. The section `*.tsx` modules carry `'use client'` because they ship React Fields/Preview components; Next's RSC bundler replaces every `'use client'` export with a `registerClientReference` stub in the server bundle. That made server reads of `SECTION_REGISTRY` crash with `TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'includes')` on `def.allowedContainers`. This module — no `'use client'`, type imports only — exports `SectionMeta` plus one `*Meta` const per section (`heroMeta`, `offerMeta`, …) and the `SECTION_REGISTRY_META` array. Each entry carries the metadata fields the generation server needs (`type`, `label`, `description`, `allowedContainers`, `allowedPageTypes?`, `implemented`, `capabilityHints?`, `elementLabels?`, plus `defaultDataKeys` — a server-safe stand-in for `Object.keys(defaultData())`). Section modules import their `*Meta` entry and spread it into the `defineSection({...})` call, so the metadata lives here exactly once. **`SECTION_REGISTRY_META` and `SECTION_REGISTRY` in `index.ts` MUST stay aligned** — adding a section type means adding it in both arrays (and adding its `defaultDataKeys` here when fields change).

- **`sections/_shared/CopyField.tsx`** (Session 4) — text/textarea field wired with per-field capability gating + AI controls. Wraps `BuilderField`/`BuilderInput`/`BuilderTextarea` in `<CapabilityGate capability="editCopy" mode="request">` so view-only users see the request-change affordance on hover. When `useAI` is held, renders inline rust-soft `✦ Regen` and `↶ Original` buttons in the field's `hint` slot — `Regen` cycles through a hardcoded `alternatives: readonly string[]` (stub-layer; Session 6 wires real AI), `Original` reverts to the `originalValue` prop. The `capability` prop defaults to `'editCopy'` but accepts `'editSEO'` for SEO-bound text. Every implemented section's Fields component uses this helper instead of raw `BuilderInput`.

- **`sections/_shared/MediaField.tsx`** (Session 4) — image-URL field gated on `editMedia`. Sibling to `CopyField`. Stub-layer is URL text input; real upload + crop UI lands when asset management ships.

- **`sections/hero.tsx`** (Session 2 → Session 4 → **Phase 6 uplift**) — first section on the **element-inspector model**: its preview regions (`eyebrow` / `headline` / `subheadline` / `ctaPrimary` / `ctaSecondary`) are individually selectable; `Fields` switches on `selectedElement` and renders only that element's settings (text + that element's colour), or section-level settings (theme preset + background colour + layout/image-side cycles + image) when no element is selected. `HeroData`: `layout` (`split` | `overlay`), `theme` (`SectionTheme`), `imageSide`, eyebrow, two-line headline, sub, 2 CTAs, image. Preview renders full-bleed through `SectionShell`; the overlay scrim derives from the theme background so the theme drives both layouts. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/offer.tsx`** (Session 2 → Session 4) — `OfferData`: tag + title + price label/caption + newline-separated inclusions + scarcity copy + CTA. AI alts on title + scarcity. Preview: single-offer card with brand-tinted price + bulleted inclusions + warn-tinted scarcity + CTA. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/services.tsx`** (Session 2 → Session 4) — `ServicesData`: title + intro + `services: ServiceItem[]` (id/name/priceFrom/durationLabel/description). Add/remove buttons are `editLayout`-gated (`hide` mode on Remove, `disable` mode on the Add row). Per-item text fields use `CopyField` without alternatives (too item-specific to canonicalise). Preview: 2-col grid of service cards. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/trust.tsx`** (Session 4) — `TrustData`: eyebrow + rating value/max + rating source + years label + licence label + guarantee label. Preview: wrap-flex of trust pills, rating tile uses brand colour. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/reviews.tsx`** (Session 4) — `ReviewsData`: title + intro + `reviews: ReviewItem[]` (author/rating/body/age). Add/remove gated like services. Preview: 3-col grid of review cards with brand-coloured star strings. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`. Real GBP auto-pull arrives when the GBP integration wires in.

- **`sections/faq.tsx`** (Session 4) — `FAQData`: title + intro + `items: FAQItem[]` (id/question/answer). Preview shows all Q/A pairs open (no accordion in the editor preview for scannability — real frontend renders the accordion). Add/remove gated. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/cta.tsx`** (Session 4) — `CTAData`: tag + headline + sub + button label/href. AI alts on headline + sub. Preview: centred dark `bg-ink` callout block with brand-coloured tag, large headline, and a glowing brand-coloured CTA button. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.

- **`sections/schedulePicker.tsx`** (Session 4) — `SchedulePickerData`: title + intro + duration label + earliest-slot caption. **Funnel-only** (`allowedContainers: ['funnelStep']`). Preview renders a 4-col mockup of available time slots with a "Mockup · real availability pulls from the calendar integration" footer. Real picker wires in when bookings backend is ready.

- **`sections/thanksConfirmation.tsx`** (Session 4) — `ThanksConfirmationData`: title + body + detail line + referral title/body/CTA. **Funnel-only** (`allowedContainers: ['funnelStep']`). Preview: centred success ✓ + body + optional referral block. Leaving `referralTitle` blank hides the entire referral block in the preview.

- **`sections/header.tsx`** (Session 4) — `HeaderData`: logo text + logo image URL + CTA label/href + `showCta` flag. **Website-level singleton** (`allowedContainers: ['websiteHeader']`). Preview: horizontal bar with brand-coloured logo + dashed-border `[ site nav · from Website.nav ]` placeholder + brand-coloured CTA. **Important:** nav data lives on `Website.nav` (NOT in `HeaderData`); the Session 4 Header editor does NOT wire nav editing — that requires extending the singleton editor's API to thread `Website`-level context into Fields, which is a deliberate punt for a future polish pass. The preview's nav placeholder communicates the boundary.

- **`sections/footer.tsx`** (Session 4) — `FooterData`: brand line + phone/email/address + 3 socials + legal copy. **Website-level singleton** (`allowedContainers: ['websiteFooter']`). Preview: 3-col footer on `bg-ink`, brand-coloured section labels, legal copy under a separator. Empty social handles hide rather than render.

- **`sections/placeholders.tsx`** (Session 4) — **empty in Session 4** (all eight previously-stubbed types graduated). The file remains as the canonical home for any FUTURE V2 placeholder types — `makePlaceholderSection` factory + `PlaceholderFields` + `makePlaceholderPreview` are still exported for that case.

- **`data-stub.tsx`** — three stub websites demonstrating the publish lifecycle, plus the brand-by-client store (brand lives on the Client now per design doc §2.3; no `brand` field on `Website`). **Voltline**: 3 pages (Home + About + Contact populated, Services page exists with empty sections — partial-build state), published. **FreshHome**: 4 pages fully published (Home / About / Services / Contact), draft ahead of published with hero copy edits on Home — demonstrates the Lane B submit-for-review flow when Session 5 lands. **KeyHero**: 1 home page, draft only, never published — first-publish state for Session 8. NeatWorks has no website (empty state in the agency-mode roster). Exports `STUB_WEBSITES`, `STUB_VERSIONS`, `DEFAULT_PREVIEW_BRAND`, plus accessors `findWebsite`, `findWebsiteByClient`, `getWebsitesForClient`, `findVersion`, `getDraftForWebsite`, `getPublishedForWebsite`, and the brand resolver `getBrandForClient(clientId)`. **Distinct from `lib/funnel/data-stub.tsx`** — that file holds the section-registry-backed funnel content; this one is the website data.

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — section-library uplift foundations (Phase 6 · library uplift · Phase 0)

> Phase 0 of the section-library uplift program. The library is being reworked so generated pages render like real websites, not editor schematics: each section type gains layout **variants** + a tonal **surface**, and the AI picks both. Phase 0 lays the shared foundations only — it does NOT retrofit the existing 11 sections (each adopts these when uplifted). New section types `about / features / gallery / contact` were added to the `SectionType` union + the `section_type` Postgres enum (migration `0026`); their registry modules land in later phases.

- **`section-theme.ts`** — the per-section colour model with **brand-default inheritance**. `SectionTheme` = three *optional* colour overrides (`background` / `heading` / `body`); `resolveTheme(overrides, brandDefaults, hardcoded)` resolves each colour down the chain `override ?? brand default ?? section hardcoded ?? platform fallback`, then derives `muted` / `border` / `card` / `cardBorder` / `isDark` via `mixHex`. `brandThemeDefaults(brand)` builds the brand-default layer from a brand's colour fields. `THEME_PRESETS` = 6 starter themes shown as circle swatches; `matchPresetId()` tells the picker which is active. So a brand default (set via "apply to all", or by the AI builder picking a palette) flows into every section that hasn't overridden the colour. Deliberately NOT global `@theme` tokens — a section-library concern; plain hex.
- **`google-fonts.ts`** — `CURATED_FONTS` (10 sans + serif display fonts) + `getFont(id)` + `googleFontsHref(ids)`. Brand stores a font *id* (`BrandObject.headingFont` / `bodyFont`, both optional → fall back to `inter-tight`). `next/font` is build-time so brand-chosen fonts load via the css2 API. Phase 0 ships a curated list; the browse-all-Google-Fonts picker lands later with a brand-editing surface.
- **`sections/_shared/SectionShell.tsx`** — the shared full-bleed wrapper every uplifted section's `Preview` renders inside. Owns the section bg + base text colour (from the section's `theme`), the brand body font, Google-Font loading. Marks the section as a `@container` so section responsive classes use **container queries** (`@2xl:` etc.) — they track the device-preview width, not the browser viewport. Props: `theme` (`ResolvedTheme`), `pad` (`none` | `tight` | `default` | `roomy`), `inset` (`band` = centred max-width column; `flush` = section self-manages its insets, for bleeding-image layouts), `maxWidth`, `backgroundLayer` (ReactNode rendered absolutely behind content — overlay-hero scrims, image-backed CTAs). Replaces the old per-section `rounded-xl border bg-card` editor-card framing. `children` is a render-prop receiving `{ theme: ResolvedTheme, headingFont, bodyFont, accent }`.
- **`sections/_shared/GoogleFontLoader.tsx`** — injects the css2 stylesheet `<link>` for a set of curated font ids. Rendered by `SectionShell`.
- **`sections/_shared/VariantField.tsx`** — left/right cycle picker for a section's structural choices (layout / image-side). Sibling to `CopyField` / `MediaField`; gates on `editLayout` by default via `CapabilityGate mode="request"`.
- **`sections/_shared/ThemeField.tsx`** — two theme controls: `ThemePresetField` (6 preset circles applying a whole `SectionTheme` — a section-level quick start) and `ColorField` (a single labelled colour picker, placed under whichever element owns that colour). `ColorField` shows whether the colour is inherited from the brand default or locally overridden (with a Reset), and — when `applyToAll` is set — opens `ApplyToAllModal` after a change to offer promoting the colour to a brand default. Both gated on `editTheme`. `components/shared/website/ApplyToAllModal.tsx` is the modal ("Apply everywhere" = set brand default + drop the local override; "don't ask again" persists per-browser).
- **`sections/_shared/SelectableElement.tsx`** — wraps a region of a section `Preview` so it is clickable to select in the editor (element-inspector model). Inert when given no `onSelect` (Preview rendered outside the editor / a non-selected section); otherwise clickable with a selection outline. `display: 'block' | 'inline-block'` for inline regions (CTA buttons).
- **`brand-style.ts`** — write a brand-level style default (font / colour) to the `brands` row. **Replaces the sunset `brand-style-stub.ts` (localStorage overlay).** `setBrandStyleValue(clientSlug, key, value)` is a fire-and-forget async write — same signature the stub had, so the 15 call sites (SiteFontsMenu + 13 section files' "apply colour to all" path) didn't change. Optimistic cache update lands first (`queryClient.setQueryData` on `['website','brand', slug]` via the module-level `getQueryClient` singleton), then the Supabase update + a `notifyBuilder()` fan-out so every `useBuilderQuery` reader (sections inheriting brand defaults, the brand editor) refetches. The brand editor's own query key (`['settings','brand']`) is invalidated on the same path so both surfaces stay in lockstep. RLS on `brands` (migration 0088) is the real authorisation — UI call sites are inside `<CapabilityGate capability="editTheme">` already. Slug→UUID resolution is cached on a `Map` for the session. Failed writes invalidate the brand query so the optimistic update gets reverted. **`useBrandStyle` is GONE** — `SectionEditor` now reads `brandQuery.data` directly, no merge layer.
- **`apply-to-all-dismissal.ts`** — per-browser "don't ask again" preference for `ApplyToAllModal`, kept in localStorage under `webnua.apply-to-all-dismissed`. A real UX preference, NOT brand data — survived the brand-style sunset because it belongs per-browser, not in the database.
- **`brand-style-legacy-migrate.ts`** — one-shot migration of any leftover `webnua.dev.brand-style` localStorage data into the `brands` row. Called from `SectionEditor` on mount; per-tab memoised in `sessionStorage` so it doesn't re-attempt; per-client (multi-tenant safe); logs to console for operator visibility. Delete this module + the `SectionEditor` call site when telemetry says the legacy key is gone in the wild.
- **`lib/query/getQueryClient.ts`** — promoted the TanStack `QueryClient` to the standard TanStack-recommended singleton pattern (server: fresh per request; browser: memoised module-level). `QueryProvider` now reads through this helper instead of holding the client in `useState`, so module-level callers (the new `brand-style.ts` write path is the first) can update the cache without threading a hook handle through props.

### `lib/funnel/` — funnel data model + publish lane (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 3.5 types; Session 7 stub; A3 publish + approval lane)

> **Architectural note.** Funnel types were locked shape-only in Session 3.5; Session 7 added the first stub data + editor wiring; **A3 wired the publish + approval lanes** (`mutations.ts` / `queries.tsx` / `approval.ts` / `preflight.ts`). The funnel data layer lives alongside the website data layer (same `Section` model, separate top-level type). See design doc §2.0 for the funnel-vs-website distinction.
>
> **Naming overlap** with `lib/funnels/` (plural, Cluster 4) is intentional: `lib/funnel/` (singular) is the editable build model; `lib/funnels/` (plural) is the analytics-detail stub for `/funnels/[id]`. Different shape, different concern. The two coexist for the same Voltline funnel — id `emergency-call-out` resolves in both stores. If a third domain joins, consider hoisting to `lib/funnel/{builder,analytics}/`.

- **`types.ts`** — `Funnel` (`{ id, clientId, name, domain, draftVersionId, publishedVersionId, createdAt, updatedAt }` — no `brand`, resolves through Client like Website does), `FunnelStep` (`{ id, funnelId, slug, title, type: FunnelStepType, sections[], seo, createdAt, updatedAt }`), `FunnelStepType` (`'landing' | 'schedule' | 'thanks' | 'optin' | 'upsell'` — distinct from website's `PageType`; design doc §2.0 spells out why), `FunnelVersion` + `FunnelVersionSnapshot` (`{ steps, stepOrder }`), `FunnelVersionStatus` (mirrors `VersionStatus`). Imports `Section` and `WebsiteDomain` from `lib/website/types.ts` — sections and domain shape are shared, everything else is funnel-specific.

- **`data-stub.tsx`** (Session 7) — Voltline's "$99 emergency call-out" funnel built against the section registry. Three steps: `landing` (hero + offer + trust + services + cta), `schedule` (schedulePicker), `thanks` (thanksConfirmation). Section content built against the section registry — seed content for the funnel editor and the funnel queries' stub fallback. One published version + one draft (identical for now). Exports `STUB_FUNNELS`, `STUB_FUNNEL_VERSIONS`, plus accessors `findFunnel`, `getFunnelsForClient`, `findFunnelVersion`, `getDraftForFunnel`, `findStep`, `findStepBySlug`. FreshHome / KeyHero / NeatWorks ship without funnels — the agency-mode roster on `/funnels` renders empty rows for them. When real backend lands, this stub is replaced by Supabase reads against `funnels` / `funnel_steps` / `funnel_versions` tables; the accessor surface stays the same.
- **`generation-stub.ts`** — `generateFunnelStub(brief, options?)`, the funnel-generation handler. **Wired to real Claude** via `/api/generate-funnel` (Opus 4.7, ONE call for the EIGHT-section landing step in the Sultanic / Suby + FAQ order: `hero → offer → reviews → features → trust → faq → reviews → form` — C3 V1 inserted FAQ between trust and reviews #2 to handle objections; see the parked decision "C3 V1 — FAQ section added to funnel step 1"); the schedule + thanks steps are built deterministically by the route + this module's `scheduleStepSections` / `thanksStepSections` helpers (chrome-only). Same fallback shape as `site-generation-stub.ts`: `503` (key unset) → silently fall back to the synchronous `generateFunnelSync` (deterministic passthrough through the website page generator); `500` → throw `AppError` so `CreateClientModal` surfaces the error; network throw (non-abort) → fallback. The legacy no-brief call still resolves to the registry-backed Voltline funnel (back-compat). The route assembles its `FunnelGenerationResult` by calling `buildFunnelSkeleton(brief, { landing, schedule, thanks })` — exported here so the live + fallback paths produce identical shapes. Consumed by the create-client flow (`site-generation-stub.ts` / `lib/clients/create-client.ts`).
- **`mutations.ts`** — the funnel publish + approval write path (A3 — the funnel-shaped sibling of `lib/website/mutations.ts`). `publishFunnelDraft` (Lane A — promote draft → published `funnel_version`, archive prior, move the funnel pointer, re-base the draft, clear `content_drafts`, and resolve any in-flight pending submission). `submitFunnelForApproval` (Lane B — insert a `pending_approval` `funnel_version` + a `funnel_approval_submissions` row with the step-diff). `approveFunnelSubmission` / `rejectFunnelSubmission` / `recallFunnelSubmission` mirror the website operations. Also `updateFunnelSlug` + `saveSeoForSteps`. Each fires `notifyBuilder()` on success. **A funnel publishes as a unit** — the whole step sequence ships together; no partial-step publish.
- **`queries.tsx`** — funnel reads (`useFunnelsForClient` / `useAllFunnels` / `useFunnelVersions` / `useFunnelWithDraft`) **plus the A3 approval-lane hooks**: `useUserPendingFunnelSubmission(funnelId, userId)` (the submitter's pending submission — drives the editor Lane B lock) and `useAllPendingFunnelApprovals()` (the operator `/tickets` queue). Both subscribe to `BUILDER_EVENT` so a publish / approve anywhere refetches.
- **`approval.ts`** (A3) — `FunnelApprovalSubmission` + `FunnelApprovalStatus` display shapes (sibling of `lib/tickets/website-approval-stub.ts`; the submission state itself is the `funnel_approval_submissions` table, pre-aligned in migration 0015). `diffFunnelSnapshots` is the pure step-field diff producing the `{ pagesChanged, sectionsChanged, fieldsChanged }` approval summary (`FunnelApprovalDiff` reuses `WebsiteApprovalDiff` — "pages" reads as "steps").
- **`preflight.ts`** (A3) — the funnel-shaped preflight rule engine, sibling of `lib/website/preflight.ts`. Six rules over a `FunnelVersionSnapshot` (`{ steps, stepOrder }`, no header/footer chrome): step-has-sections + hero-content + cta-content + form-fields are `fail`; lead-capture-present + seo-title are `warn`. `runFunnelPreflight(snapshot, funnelId)` returns the same `PreflightReport` shape the website engine does, so `/funnels/[id]/review` reuses the shared `PreflightChecklist`.

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — autosave + publish lanes + approval store (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 5; **Phase 4: Supabase-wired** — PR #41 / merge `534de96`)

The save → publish → approval pipeline behind the editor. **PR #41 deleted the localStorage `publish-stub.ts` / `draft-stub.ts` / `audit-stub.ts` modules and replaced them with Supabase reads + writes** against `website_versions` / `website_approval_submissions` / `force_publish_audit_log` / `content_drafts` / `brands` / `websites`. The reactive bus is the platform-standard event-bus pattern (`BUILDER_EVENT`) instead of the previous per-store custom events. Consumer hook surface (`useAutosave`, `useWebsitePublishState`, `useUserPendingSubmission`, `useAllPendingApprovals`) is unchanged.

- **`queries.tsx`** — Phase 4 read path. Live Supabase reads over `websites` / `website_versions` / `content_drafts` / `website_approval_submissions` / `force_publish_audit_log` / `brands`. `useBuilderQuery` subscribes to `BUILDER_EVENT` and refetches, so every publish / approve / autosave anywhere refreshes every dependent surface. Exports the three reactive hooks (`useWebsitePublishState` / `useUserPendingSubmission` / `useAllPendingApprovals`) keeping their old return shapes — `use-publish-state.ts` is now a re-export shim so existing consumers (`SectionEditor`, `VersionHistoryCard`, the `/tickets` approvals tab) are unchanged.
- **`mutations.ts`** — Phase 4 write path. Async functions over Supabase, each firing `BUILDER_EVENT` on success. Operations (design doc §3.3):
  - **`publishDraft(websiteId, actor, options?)`** — Lane A. `mergeDraftsIntoSnapshot` overlays `content_drafts` onto the draft baseline, inserts a new `published` `website_versions` row, archives prior published, updates the website's `published_version_id` pointer, clears the website's `content_drafts` rows, resolves any in-flight pending submission to `approved`, and — when `options.force` is set — inserts a `force_publish_audit_log` row.
  - **`submitForApproval(websiteId, submitter, note?)`** — Lane B. Same snapshot construction; inserts a `pending_approval` version + a `website_approval_submissions` row. Does NOT clear `content_drafts` — submitter retains the draft so recall / reject puts them back in business. `diffSnapshots` (in `snapshot.ts`) computes the `{ pagesChanged, sectionsChanged, fieldsChanged }` summary stored on the submission.
  - **`approveSubmission(submissionId, approver)`** — promotes the pending version → `published`, archives prior, updates pointer, clears drafts, marks submission `approved`.
  - **`rejectSubmission(submissionId, approver, reason)`** — archives the pending version, marks submission `rejected` with the reason. Drafts untouched.
  - **`recallSubmission(submissionId)`** — submitter recall; same end-state as reject but no reason recorded; status `recalled`.
  - **`restoreVersionAsDraft(websiteId, sourceVersionId, actor)`** — Session 8 rollback (design §7). Deep-copies a prior version's snapshot into a fresh `draft` version, archives any existing draft, wipes the website's `content_drafts` rows so the editor rehydrates from the restored snapshot. **Refuses while a pending submission is in flight** (would silently overwrite the submitter's diff). Returns `{ newDraftId }` or null.
- **`content-drafts.ts`** — Phase 4 autosave write-buffer (replaces `draft-stub.ts`). A transient per-page / per-singleton / per-funnel-step buffer in the `content_drafts` table that overlays the draft version's baseline snapshot. One row per editable scope, keyed by the `(scope_kind, website_id, funnel_id, page_key)` unique constraint (NULLS NOT DISTINCT — so the null funnel_id / null page_key collapse). `updated_by` must equal the signed-in user (RLS) — the buffer is the user's own unsaved work; publish / approve clears the website's whole buffer. `DraftSlot` type kept from the stub layer: `{ kind: 'page', websiteId, pageId } | { kind: 'header', websiteId } | { kind: 'footer', websiteId } | { kind: 'funnelStep', funnelId, stepId }`. Public API: `loadDraft(slot)`, `loadDraftSections(slot)`, `saveDraftSections(slot, sections)` (upsert), `clearDraft(slot)`, `clearDraftsForWebsite(websiteId)`, `clearDraftsForFunnel(funnelId)`.
- **`snapshot.ts`** — Phase 4 pure helpers (no I/O). `mergeDraftsIntoSnapshot(baseline, draftRows)` overlays the `content_drafts` buffer onto a draft version's baseline snapshot (slot wins where present, preserving `page.seo` — the SEO panel writes straight to the draft version snapshot, not the per-section buffer). `diffSnapshots(prev, next)` produces the `{ pagesChanged, sectionsChanged, fieldsChanged }` approval summary — lifted verbatim from the old `publish-stub` so the publish lanes keep identical behaviour.
- **`builder-events.ts`** — Phase 4 reactivity bus. `BUILDER_EVENT = 'webnua:builder-change'` + `notifyBuilder()` + a subscriber helper. Replaces the previous `APPROVAL_EVENT` / `webnua:draft-change` custom events with one bus. Every mutation in `mutations.ts` and `content-drafts.ts` fires it; every reactive hook in `queries.tsx` subscribes.
- **`use-autosave.ts`** — Session 5 (A) · Phase 4 wiring. The hook driving section persistence. `useAutosave({ slot, sections, disabled? })` → `{ status: AutosaveStatus, lastSavedAt: number | null, retry }`. Statuses: `idle | pending | saving | synced | failed`. Behaviour (design doc §3.2): every change to `sections` schedules a 500ms debounced flush; on flush, `saveDraftSections(slot, sections)` upserts the `content_drafts` row; status moves `saving → synced` (or `failed` on RLS / network error, with `retry()` to reattempt). First-render is skipped. `disabled: true` cancels any pending flush and parks at `idle` (used by the Lane B editor lock — locked submitters mustn't keep writing). Submit-mid-edit edge case (§3.1) is docced — server-snapshot defines the pending version's contents; in-flight 500ms edits stay in operator's local React state and fold forward on the next flush.
- **`use-publish-state.ts`** — Phase 4 re-export shim. The three hooks (`useWebsitePublishState`, `useUserPendingSubmission`, `useAllPendingApprovals`) moved into `queries.tsx`; this module re-exports them so existing consumers' import paths are unchanged.
- **`preflight.ts`** — Session 8 (design doc §7). Declarative preflight rule engine. `PreflightRule` is `{ id, title, run(snapshot, context) → PreflightResult[] }` — each rule is a pure function over a `VersionSnapshot` that emits zero-or-more results (one per affected page / section). `PreflightResult` carries `{ ruleId, status: 'pass' | 'warn' | 'fail', title, message, pageId?, sectionId?, fixHref? }`. `PREFLIGHT_RULES` is the const array (13 rules: page-has-sections, SEO title/description, hero content + CTA, offer content, CTA section, trust evidence, reviews/FAQ populated, header logo, footer contact, nav targets). `runPreflight(snapshot, context)` → `PreflightReport` (`{ results, counts, canPublish, allClear }`); `canPublish` is true when there are zero `fail`s, `allClear` adds zero `warn`s. `groupResultsByPage(results)` buckets results by `pageId` (with a `__site` bucket for header/footer/nav rules) for the per-page review cards. **Integration-prerequisite rules** (GBP for reviews, calendar for schedule) are deferred until the integrations data layer can answer "is X connected for this client" — add a composable integration-aware rule set then. **B16 added `reviews-ai-placeholder`** — a `warn` rule (one result per offending page) flagging reviews sections that still carry unedited AI-drafted placeholder testimonials; it reads `uneditedPlaceholderCount` from `placeholder-testimonials.ts`.
- **`placeholder-testimonials.ts`** — **B16.** Detection layer for AI-invented testimonials. The website generator emits `reviews` sections with plausible-but-fake quotes + author names; shipping them live is a credibility risk. `toSection` (`generation-stub.ts`) snapshots the AI-drafted items onto `section.ai.placeholderSnapshot.reviews` (a `{ quote, authorName, authorRole }[]` — added to `SectionAIMeta` in `types.ts`). **The detection heuristic is an EXACT content match:** a live review item is an "unedited placeholder" when its `quote` + `authorName` + `authorRole` still exactly equal a snapshot entry; the moment the operator edits any of that text it counts as a real review. **This is why the heuristic survives changes to the AI generator — the snapshot is whatever was generated for THAT section, not a fixed string set.** Future edits to the generation prompts therefore need no change here; what MUST stay in lockstep is the snapshot shape — if `toSection` ever stops writing `placeholderSnapshot`, or the reviews section renames `quote`/`authorName`/`authorRole`, detection silently returns 0 (fails open: no false warnings, but no nudge either). Exports `uneditedPlaceholderCount(section)` and `countUneditedPlaceholderTestimonials(snapshot)` (whole-site total, enabled sections only). Consumed by the `reviews-ai-placeholder` preflight rule, the `PlaceholderTestimonialBanner` editor nudge, and the `/website/review` publish-confirm copy. Funnel-generated reviews are NOT covered — the funnel generator (`generate-funnel-live.ts`) is a separate path that does not call `toSection`, so funnel reviews never carry the snapshot and `uneditedPlaceholderCount` returns 0 for them (a safe no-op; CLAUDE.md's parked decision already says funnels never AI-generate testimonials).
- **`PlaceholderTestimonialBanner`** (`components/shared/website/PlaceholderTestimonialBanner.tsx`) — **B16.** `'use client'` editor nudge shown at the top of `SectionFieldsPanel` when the open reviews section still has unedited AI placeholders. Amber-tinted; states the count and tells the operator to replace the placeholders with real reviews. Self-gates (renders null otherwise) so the mount site is unconditional. Dismissable per-section via a localStorage key (`webnua:testimonial-placeholder-ack:{sectionId}`) so an acknowledged section stops nagging on reopen. The banner clears automatically as the operator edits the last placeholder (count → 0).

### `lib/tickets/` (cont'd) — website-approval submission shapes (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 5)

- **`website-approval-stub.ts`** — Session 5 (B+C) · Phase 4: **type-only display module.** The submission state is now the `website_approval_submissions` table — written by `lib/website/mutations.ts`, read by the publish-state hooks in `lib/website/queries.tsx`. This module keeps only the display shapes the "Website approvals" tab and the Lane B editor-lock banner consume. `WebsiteApprovalSubmission` (`{ id, websiteId, pendingVersionId, submitterId, submitterName, submittedAt, status: 'pending' | 'approved' | 'rejected' | 'recalled', note?, diff: WebsiteApprovalDiff, snapshot, rejectionReason?, resolvedAt?, resolvedByName? }`). `WebsiteApprovalDiff` (`{ pagesChanged, sectionsChanged, fieldsChanged }`) — shallow JSON-string compare counts, good for the V1 "X fields in Y sections" summary; per §3.4 there's no field-level diff view V1.
- **`types.ts`** — Session 5 added `'website-approval'` as a new `TicketCategory` enum value with `CATEGORY_LABEL['website-approval'] = 'Website approval'`. `pills.tsx` (`CategoryPill`) and `CategoryTile` got their record entries — both render in rust on rust-soft to distinguish from the default `website` tone. The pills are wired but currently unused by the inbox row paths (the approvals tab uses `WebsiteApprovalRow` directly, not `TicketRow`); they're available if a future surface lists website-approvals alongside regular tickets.

### `admin/tickets/` (cont'd) — website-approval row (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 5)

- **`WebsiteApprovalRow`** (`tickets/WebsiteApprovalRow.tsx`) — Session 5 (E). Single pending-website-submission row inside the "Approvals" tab on `/tickets`. Admin-only. 4-cell grid: 36px rust-tinted client-initial avatar + `1fr` body (client name + diff summary + submitter / submitted-at / pages-touched meta) + 90px right-aligned relative age + actions row (Approve & publish ✓ / Open in editor → / Reject ✗). Reject expands inline (decision 3 in the Session 5 plan message): the actions row swaps for a warn-tinted reason `Textarea` + Cancel / Submit-rejection ↩ row. Submit button stays gated on non-empty reason. Approve calls `approveSubmission`; reject calls `rejectSubmission`. "Open in editor" routes to `/website` (per-page deep-link wasn't in the brief — submissions are website-level since any of their pages could have changed).

### `admin/funnels/` — funnel-approval row (A3 · funnel publish + approval lane)

- **`FunnelApprovalRow`** (`funnels/FunnelApprovalRow.tsx`) — the funnel-shaped sibling of `WebsiteApprovalRow`, rendered in the shared `/tickets` "Approvals" tab. Admin-only. Same 4-cell grid + inline-reject pattern; carries a rust `Funnel` pill to distinguish it from a website row, and a `Funnel: {name}` meta line. Approve calls `approveFunnelSubmission`, reject `rejectFunnelSubmission`. "Open in editor →" routes to `/funnels/[id]` (the funnel detail page carries the editor deep-link — funnel submissions are funnel-level since the whole step sequence publishes as a unit).
- **Unpublish / Publish toggle lives inside `FunnelSlugEditor`** (Phase 8 · Session 4 follow-up — UX consolidation). Operator-only contextual button on the right side of the Public URL row: "Unpublish" (warn-outline, opens a destructive `ConfirmDialog` that fires `unpublishFunnel`) when the funnel has a `publishedVersionId`, "Publish →" (rust, links to `/funnels/[id]/review`) when draft-only. Gated on `role === 'admin'` + `publish` cap. Lives inside `FunnelSlugEditor` rather than as a standalone card so the publish state sits with the URL — operators reason about "this URL is live / not live" as one concern. The previous standalone `FunnelPublicationControls` card was removed.

### `app/tickets/_admin-content.tsx` — augmented in Session 5 (E); A3

Now `'use client'`. Tab list is the static `adminTicketTabs` with a live `{ id: 'approvals', label: 'Approvals', count }` tab spliced in as the second entry. The count is `useAllPendingApprovals().length + useAllPendingFunnelApprovals().length` (website + funnel pending). `TicketTabsBar` runs in controlled mode (`value` + `onChange`). When the approvals tab is active the regular ticket table + filter bar both hide; `ApprovalsList` renders the `WebsiteApprovalRow`s then the `FunnelApprovalRow`s (one shared queue, empty-state card when both are clear).

### `lib/workspace/` — agency vs sub-account context (Phase 6 · Cluster 5)

The two-tier GoHighLevel-style workspace model. Operator's default view is **agency** (cross-client birds-eye, where triage/oversight happens). Drilling into a client via `AdminClientPicker` switches the context to **sub-account** mode for that client (where the actual managing/changes happen). Surfaces that exist in both modes (currently just `/settings/access`) dispatch on the context. Cross-client-only surfaces (`/tickets`, `/leads`, `/calendar`, `/automations`, `/campaigns`, the `/settings/integrations` matrix) stay agency-only for now; per-client sub-account variants land as each surface gets touched in future clusters. URL stays clean — context is state-driven, not URL-driven.

- **`workspace-stub.tsx`** — **STUB.** localStorage-backed React provider + hooks. Active client id lives in `webnua.dev.active-client-id`; absent = agency mode; populated = sub-account mode for that client. Exports `<WorkspaceProvider>` (mounted in `src/app/layout.tsx` inside `<UserProvider>`), `useWorkspace()` → `{ activeClientId, activeClient, hydrated, setActiveClientId, clearActiveClient }`, `useActiveClient()` (sugar), `useIsAgencyMode()` (sugar — true when `activeClientId` is null). Defaults to agency mode (no key) on fresh load. Client-role users never see the picker (hidden in `ClientSidebar`), so the context has no effect for them. Two deletion points when real auth ships: this file, and the `<WorkspaceProvider>` mount.

### `lib/agency/` — policy resolution layer (Phase 6 · Cluster 8 · Session 2)

> The three-layer model's spine (see the `## Agency / sub-account model` section near the top). Layer 2 (agency policy) + Layer 3 (sub-account overrides) + the resolver that merges them. Six policy keys, three wired to UI in Cluster 8, three typed + resolver-ready but deferred. **Supabase-backed caches**, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider` (PR #43); writes go straight to the policy tables and the in-memory caches update locally for snapshot stability. The resolver + hooks are unchanged from the stub-layer shape.

- **`types.ts`** — the closed `PolicyKey` union (6 keys) + `POLICY_KEYS` / `LIVE_POLICY_KEYS` arrays + `POLICY_KEY_LABEL`. Per-key value types: `IntegrationDefaults`, `BrandDefaults`, `AutomationDefaults`, `PricingDefaults`. `PolicyValueMap` maps each key to its value type — the resolver is typed to this, never `Record<string, unknown>`. `PolicyResolution<K>` (`{ effectiveValue, source: 'agency' | 'plan' | 'override', agencyValue, planValue }` — Cluster 9 · Session 1 added `'plan'` + `planValue`) + `AllPolicyResolutions`. **Adding a policy key means amending this union AND the CLAUDE.md policy-key table — don't widen it ad hoc.**
- **`agency-policy-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`** (filename is misleading; kept for import stability — same trick as `auth/user-stub.tsx`). Layer-2 store. `AGENCY_POLICY_SEED` (frozen, derived from `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` + `adminDefaults*`) is the pre-hydration fallback; `hydrateAgencyPolicy()` overlays the real `agency_policy` table rows. `getAgencyPolicy(key)`, `getAllAgencyPolicy()`, `setAgencyPolicy(key, value)` (writes through to Supabase), `resetAgencyPolicy(key | '*')`, `subscribeAgencyPolicy(cb)`. Snapshot-cached per the CLAUDE.md stability rule.
- **`override-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`.** Layer-3 store backed by `policy_overrides` table (`Record<clientId, Partial<PolicyValueMap>>`). A key absent from a client's entry = inherit. Carries `SUB_ACCOUNT_OVERRIDE_SEED` (Session 4b) — the per-client overrides that exist at platform start (the migrated former `AdminClient.seatLimit` values: Voltline `3`, KeyHero/NeatWorks `null`; FreshHome inherits). `hasOverride`, `getOverride`, `getOverridesForClient`, `setOverride`, `clearOverride`, `clearOverridesForClient`, `subscribeOverrides`.
- **`resolver.ts`** — pure functions over the policy stores **and** (Cluster 9 · Session 1) the `lib/billing/` plan stores. `resolvePolicy(key, clientId)` → `PolicyResolution<K>`, walking `override → assigned-plan bundle → agency` (clientId null = agency mode, no plan layer). The first agency ↔ billing link: resolver imports `getAssignedPlanId` / `getPlan` (value) from `lib/billing/`; `lib/billing/` imports `PolicyValueMap` (type-only) back — no runtime cycle. `resolveAllPolicies(clientId)`.
- **`use-policy.ts`** — `'use client'`. `usePolicy(key)` resolves against the active workspace (`useWorkspace`), reactive to the policy stores **and** the plan stores (catalog edits + reassignment move resolved values); `useAgencyPolicy(key)` is the raw Layer-2 value. Resolution snapshots cached per `(key, clientId)` against a JSON key (snapshot-stability rule).
- **`integration-providers.ts`** — `INTEGRATION_PROVIDERS` — display metadata (id / name / description) for the providers tracked by the `integrationDefaults` key. The ids must match the `sharedProviders` keys in `AGENCY_POLICY_SEED`. Shared by the `/settings/integrations` agency-mode connection-policy section + the sub-account integrations view.
- Verified by `/dev/agency-policy` (see `app/dev/` convention) — the resolution matrix: every key × agency + each sub-account, with source flags + per-cell test-override toggle. Cluster 9 · Session 1 added per-plan columns (each plan's bundle value per key) so the plan layer reads straight against the resolved client cells.
- **Consuming surfaces:** the `/settings/integrations` agency-mode connection-policy section + `/settings/seats` (Session 3 — agency-level, set Layer 2 via `useAgencyPolicy`/`setAgencyPolicy`). Session 4b — sub-account override UI: `/settings/integrations` sub-account mode (`_sub-account-content.tsx`, per-provider `integrationDefaults` inherit/override via `usePolicy` + `setOverride`/`clearOverride`) and `ClientSeatLimitCard` (the seat limit resolves through `resolvePolicy('defaultSeatLimit', clientId)` — see `lib/clients/seat-limit-stub.ts`).

> **Known follow-up (Cluster 9 · Session 1) — RESOLVED (Session 7).** `/settings/integrations` sub-account mode (`_sub-account-content.tsx`) used to derive per-provider inherited-vs-overridden by comparing the *resolved* `integrationDefaults` against the *agency* value — so a client on a plan whose integration bundle differed from the agency default showed every provider as "overridden". The design call: per-provider "revert" targets the **inherited** value — the assigned plan's bundle when the client is on a plan, otherwise the agency default — which is the value the client resolves to with no override. The view now computes `inherited = planValue ?? agencyValue` and compares against that; the source hint reads `plan ·` vs `agency ·` accordingly. A scan of the other resolver consumers (`/settings/billing` sub-account, `seat-limit-stub.ts`) confirmed neither carried the same pre-plan-layer shape.

### `lib/billing/` — plan layer (Phase 6 · Cluster 9)

> The billing plan layer — Layer 2.5 of the policy resolution stack (see the `## Agency / sub-account model` section). A plan packages a `Partial<PolicyValueMap>` bundle the agency offers as a tier; the resolver inserts it between the agency default and a per-sub-account override. **Supabase-backed caches**, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider` against `plan_catalog` + `plan_assignments` (PR #43 + migration `0025`). Real payment/Stripe is deliberately out of scope — invoices stay display stubs.
