- **`types.ts`** — `Plan` (`{ id, name, description, price, currency, billingCycle, policy: Partial<PolicyValueMap> }`), `PlanAssignment` (`{ clientId, planId }`), `BillingCycle` (`'monthly' | 'yearly'`) + `BILLING_CYCLE_LABEL`. Imports `PolicyValueMap` from `lib/agency/` type-only (the agency ↔ billing link — no runtime cycle).
- **`plan-catalog-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`.** The catalog. `PLAN_CATALOG_SEED` (frozen — Basic / Pro / Enterprise, each with a real seat-limit + capability-floor + integration-defaults bundle) is the pre-hydration fallback; the real catalog lives in `plan_catalog` (migration `0025`). `getPlanCatalog()`, `getPlan(id)`, `upsertPlan(plan)`, `removePlan(id)`, `resetPlanCatalog()`, `subscribePlanCatalog(cb)`. Snapshot-cached per the CLAUDE.md stability rule.
- **`plan-assignment-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`.** `Record<clientId, planId>` backed by `plan_assignments`. `PLAN_ASSIGNMENT_SEED` assigns voltline→basic, freshhome→pro, keyhero→pro (NeatWorks unassigned — exercises the no-plan path). `getAssignedPlanId(clientId)`, `getAssignedPlan(clientId)`, `getAllPlanAssignments()`, `setPlanAssignment`, `clearPlanAssignment`, `subscribePlanAssignments`.
- **`hooks.ts`** — `'use client'`. `usePlanCatalog()`, `usePlan(id)`, `useAssignedPlanId(clientId)`, `useAssignedPlan(clientId)` — all `useSyncExternalStore` over the reference-stable stores.
- **Consuming surfaces:** `/settings/plans` (Session 2 — agency-mode catalog editor). The resolver (`lib/agency/resolver.ts`) reads `getAssignedPlanId` + `getPlan`. **The sub-account `/settings/billing` plan-assignment UI was removed** (Phase 7 Stripe billing) — sub-account billing now shows only the Stripe subscription; per-client plan assignment + the resolved-bundle view will return with the later-phase integrated upgrade path (plan tiers tied to access restrictions). The catalog + resolver are unchanged and still drive agency defaults.

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — form-to-page generation (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 6)

The Q&A-to-Page pipeline that backs `/website/new`. Spec lives in `reference/builder-generation-design.md`. Five locked questions (page type → primary intent → audience → specifics → avoid); stub generator deterministic on `(pageType, intent, audience)` with synthetic 4–8s delay; validation pipeline + fallback log graduates straight to backend.

- **`generation-context.ts`** — `GenerationContext` + the discriminated `PrimaryIntent` (including `'other'` with free-text fallback) + `Audience` + `ExistingPageSnapshot`. Chip-row data tables (`PAGE_TYPE_CHIPS`, `PRIMARY_INTENT_CHIPS`, `AUDIENCE_CHIPS`) + label helpers (`describeIntent`/`describeAudience`/`describePageType`) live here so the Q&A flow + review surface + dev preview share one source of truth.
- **`generation-prompt.ts`** — pure prompt-block construction. Six blocks (`system | brand | page-questions | existing-pages | registry-catalog | example` — the `example` block carries a fully-populated Voltline Electrical home page, see parked decision "Worked examples"). `buildPromptBlocks(ctx)` for the dev surface; `composePrompt(ctx)` glues them with `---` separators. The existing-pages block is omitted for first-page-of-website generation (empty `existingPages[]`). The registry-catalog block filters `SECTION_REGISTRY` by `allowedContainers.includes('page')` + `allowedPageTypes` (if set). Voice tone numeric axes → prose translation via `voiceToneToProse()`. Side-effect-free + no React; this is the piece that graduates to the real backend. **Per-section shape catalog** (`SECTION_SHAPE_CATALOG`): for every page-eligible section type, lists the variant key enum values (`layout`, `theme`, `imageSide`, `contentAlign`, `headerAlign`, `headlineSize`, `subSize`, `stackStyle`, `columns`, `mediaStyle`, `iconStyle`, `aspect`, `ctaStyle`, `nav`, `extra`, `mediaMode`, `mediaShape`, `overlay`, `footer`, `display`, `align`, `overlayOpacity`) with optional one-line picker guidance, and the per-array element object shape for `items` / `inclusions` / `signals` / `features` / `stats` / `badges`. **`SHARED_FIELD_NOTES`** (exported) is the appendix block both the website registry catalog AND the funnel field-keys block include: explains the `headlineAccent` / `titleAccent` semantic (an optional SECOND LINE in the accent colour, NOT a substring of the headline), lists the 74 curated icon ids, declares the item-`id` rule, and explains the `theme` object shape. **`formatSectionShape(type)`** (exported) is the helper the funnel prompt uses to emit a single section's catalog entry in the same shape as the website registry catalog. When the section module's TypeScript shape changes, update the matching `SECTION_SHAPE_CATALOG` entry — these annotations are inline, not generated.
- **`generation-stub.ts`** — handler + recipes + per-section copy library + validation pipeline (§4.4) + fallback log (§4.4a). `generatePageStub(ctx)` runs the synthetic delay then returns `{ generationId, page, fallbackLog, droppedSections }`; `generateSync(ctx)` is the no-delay variant for the dev preview. Per-page-type recipes (`home | services | about | contact | generic`) pick which sections appear and in what order. Three voice variants (`cold-ad-urgent | existing-calm | search-plain`) selected from `audience`. `GENERATION_PHASES` exports the three phase strings the status card cycles through. The free-text `specifics` + `avoid` answers are **received but not consumed** by the deterministic stub — but the real generator (`generate-live.ts`) does consume them, since `composePrompt` feeds them to the model. **`assembleResult(ctx, rawSections, generationId, overrides?)`** is exported here — it runs the §4.4 validation pipeline + Page assembly and is shared by `generateSync` (the recipe path) and `generate-live.ts` (the real LLM path).
- **`generated-pages-stub.ts`** — **STUB.** localStorage-backed overlay store. Key shape `webnua.dev.generated-pages.{websiteId}` → `Page[]`. `addGeneratedPage(websiteId, page)` writes; `mergeGeneratedPages(websiteId, seed)` returns seed-first list with the overlay appended (seed wins on id collision). Both the `/website` hub and the `/website/[pageId]` editor merge in at read time so the new page is visible and editable immediately. When real backend ships, replaced by a normal INSERT against the `pages` table; the merge helper goes away (seed = backend reads).

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — section library uplift (Phase 6 · library uplift · PR #45)

> PR #45 expanded the section library: four net-new section types (`about`, `features`, `gallery`, `contact`) and significant rewrites of the existing eight to add per-variant layouts + element inspectors. Migration `0026` extends the `section_type` Postgres enum to match. `services.tsx` was demoted to `implemented: false` in this pass (kept in the registry so seed pages still parse; new sections can't be added).

- **`sections/about.tsx`** (~1,060 lines) — `about` section type. Variant set + element-inspector model + `CopyField` / `MediaField` per element. `allowedContainers: ['page']`; `allowedPageTypes: ['home', 'about', 'generic']`.
- **`sections/contact.tsx`** (~909 lines) — `contact` section type. Variants with form / map / hours / address blocks; element inspector covers each region. `allowedContainers: ['page']`. **Bundle C1 default-shape change**: new contact sections render a single primary CTA (default label "Send us a message", default href `POPUP_HREF` → opens the section's popup form modal via the platform-standard `Section.popup` envelope + `PopupHost`). The CTA destination is editable via `LinkField` in the new `cta` element inspector — pick a page, popup, `tel:`, `mailto:`, or custom URL. `showInlineForm: true` (configurable from the section settings AND the form element inspector) flips the section back to the legacy two-column "details + inline form" shape. **Back-compat**: a pre-C1 stored contact section (no `ctaLabel`/`ctaHref`/`showInlineForm` keys) is detected by `withDefaults` and forced to `showInlineForm: true`, so existing customer pages don't silently flip to a CTA they never asked for. `SectionEditor`'s `handleAddSection` seeds `Section.popup = defaultPopupConfig()` on a freshly-added contact so the popup form is workable immediately (sibling pattern to the `form` section's auto-attached form envelope).
- **`sections/features.tsx`** (~956 lines) — `features` section type. Variant set with N-column feature grids; per-feature `IconField` + `CopyField`s. Add/remove gated on `editLayout`. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`.
- **`sections/gallery.tsx`** (~821 lines) — `gallery` section type. Variants for grid / carousel / masonry; per-image `MediaField`. `allowedContainers: ['page']`.
- **`sections/_shared/IconField.tsx`** — capability-gated icon picker over `section-icons.ts`'s curated set. Gated on `editLayout`.
- **`sections/_shared/ColumnsField.tsx`** — variant cycle for N-column layouts (used by `features`, `gallery`, etc.). Gated on `editLayout`.
- **`sections/_shared/BundleButton.tsx`** (Bundle C2b-3) — customer-facing CTA primitive that reads the SectionShell-injected `--bundle-radius-button` / `--bundle-button-style` / `--bundle-shadow-elevation` CSS custom properties and renders the correct bundle treatment. Variants: `primary` (filled by default; the `outlined-or-text` bundle reframes as outlined) + `secondary` (outlined by default; reframed as a text link). Built on `SurfaceLink` so editor click-to-select still works. The `big-bold-arrow` bundle promotes the trailing glyph to a permanent `→` when absent. Adopted in `about` (extra='button') + `features` (bottom CTA) as the C2b-3 reference implementations; the other 7 customer-facing CTA sections (hero / offer / gallery / reviews / contact / cta / faq) keep their inline-styled `SurfaceLink` chains pending a follow-up migration — see the C2b-3 parked-decision entry for the migration recipe.
- **`sections/_shared/SocialGlyph.tsx`** — small inline social-icon glyph used by `footer.tsx` + `contact.tsx`.
- **`sections/_shared/StarRow.tsx`** — N-star row used by `reviews.tsx` + `trust.tsx` previews; brand-coloured.
- **`sections/_shared/section-icons.ts`** (~214 lines) — the curated icon library `IconField` chooses from. Closed set + label + the icon SVG path.
- **`sections/_shared/grid.ts`** — grid maths helpers (column-count → Tailwind classes, etc.) for the variant layouts.

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — lead-capture form builder (Phase 6 · form builder · PR #46)

> PR #46 added the entire form-builder feature — see `reference/form-builder-design.md` for the retroactive design doc. New `editForms` capability + new `form` section type + the `Section.form?: FormConfig` envelope. Migration `0029` adds `editforms` to the `capability` Postgres enum; `0030` adds `form` to the `section_type` enum; `0031` adds the `lead_attachments` Storage bucket + RLS. The `form_submitted` `lead_events` kind carries the captured submission.

- **`form-config.ts`** (~176 lines) — the form's field shape + per-field config. Field types: `text | email | phone | textarea | select | checkbox | image | date`. `date` was added with the funnel qualification step (native `<input type="date">`, no calendar-availability lookup — kept simple for V1; the funnel's qualification form pairs it with a Morning/Afternoon/Evening `select` to ask for the request, not pick a confirmed slot). `FormConfig = { fields: FormField[]; submitLabel: string; successMessage: string }`. Field-level config: `required`, `placeholder`, `options` (for `select`), `accept` (for `image`).
- **`sections/form.tsx`** (~196 lines) — registers the `form` section type. `allowedContainers: ['page', 'funnelStep']`. Preview renders the form via `FormBlock`; editor renders the form-controls panel via `SectionFormControls`. Distinct concern from a section's `Section.form` envelope — the section type IS-a form; the envelope ATTACHES-a form to another section (currently `hero`).
- **`section-form-slot.ts`** — declares which section types may host a `Section.form` envelope (currently `hero` only — see the form-builder design doc). One source of truth for "can this section type carry a form?".
- **`components/shared/website/FormBlock.tsx`** (~399 lines) — the rendered form. Used inside the `form` section's preview AND inside any envelope-hosting section's preview. Validates required fields client-side; submission lands in `leads` + `lead_events` (`form_submitted`).
- **`components/shared/website/SectionFormControls.tsx`** (~714 lines) — the per-field editor surface. Add / remove / reorder fields (each gated on `editForms` via `CapabilityGate`); per-field name / label / required / options / etc. Lives in the editor's fields panel.
- **`components/shared/website/FormFieldTypePicker.tsx`** (~60 lines) — small picker `Dialog` invoked by the `+ Add field` button. Shows the seven field types + an icon glyph + description; picking one appends a fresh field at the registry's default config.
- **`lib/leads/upload-attachment.ts`** (~47 lines) — image-attachment upload helper for the `image`-typed form field. Uploads to the `lead_attachments` Storage bucket (migration `0031`); returns the public URL the form-submit then stores on the `lead_events.payload`. RLS on the bucket: anonymous read of objects under `{client_slug}/{lead_id}/`; writes from the public-submit flow only.

### `lib/website/` (cont'd) — real Claude generator (Phase 6 · PR #47 · this PR)

The Phase 6 generator pair, called via the `/api/generate-site` route. See the parked decision "Phase 6 generation fallback policy" for the silent-vs-thrown contract. `generation_log` writes documented inline in the API-routes section below.

- **`generate-live.ts`** — server-only. `generatePageLive(ctx, generationId?)` — the real Claude call: `composePrompt(ctx)` → `claude-opus-4-7` (adaptive thinking, streamed, `max_tokens: 64000`, cached system prompt) → defensively-parsed JSON → `assembleResult` (same §4.4 validation pipeline the deterministic stub uses). Optional `generationId` lets the route share one uuid across all per-page calls so `generation_log` rows group cleanly; defaults to `crypto.randomUUID()` standalone. Imported only by the route handler so `@anthropic-ai/sdk` stays out of the client bundle. `SYSTEM_PROMPT` is the conversion-copywriter persona + the strict JSON output contract.
- **`site-generation-stub.ts`** — browser-side caller. `generateSiteStub(brief, options?)` POSTs the brief (plus the optional `clientId` for `generation_log` attribution) to `/api/generate-site` and returns the `SiteGenerationResult`. **Fallback policy:** `503` (key not configured) → silent fallback to `generateSiteSync` for dev; `500` (real failure) → throw `AppError` with the server's `{ name, status, detail }` body so `CreateClientModal` surfaces the actual error; network throw (non-abort) → fallback with `console.warn`. `generateSiteSync(brief)` is the deterministic no-I/O variant (dev / test).

### `app/api/` — server routes

- **`generate-site/route.ts`** — see the entry in `admin/` create-client flow above for the full contract. Real Claude website generator with `generation_log` observability.
- **`generate-seo/route.ts`** — server-only Claude-backed SEO drafter. Called by `lib/website/seo-generate.ts` via `fetch('/api/generate-seo')`; runs an Anthropic message per target (page or funnel step) and returns `{ title, description }` per id. Returns `503` when `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` is unset (the client's caller falls back to the deterministic generator), `500` on failure. Server-only — the SDK stays out of the client bundle. Same fallback shape as the website generator.
- **`generate-offer/route.ts`** — server-only Sonnet-backed funnel-offer drafter (the four-field offer the wizard captures: `{ headline, promise, riskReversal, ctaText }`). Called by `lib/website/offer-generate.ts` via `fetch('/api/generate-offer')`. **Sonnet 4.6, not Opus** — short structured copy doesn't need Opus pricing; thinking enabled (`budget_tokens: 2000`, `max_tokens: 4000` — Anthropic requires `max_tokens > thinking.budget_tokens`, hence the 4000-token envelope ahead of a ~150-token output). System prompt is a Suby/Sultanic direct-response brief with concrete examples per field, a hard ban list of AI corporate-speak ("comprehensive", "leverage", "elevate", etc.), and length caps (headline ≤12 words, promise ≤25, risk-reversal ≤15, CTA ≤6). Returns `503` (key unset → caller throws `AppError.validation` so the wizard surfaces "configure ANTHROPIC_API_KEY" rather than degrading silently — a stub offer at this step would be misleading), `400` (missing required brief fields), `500` (real failure with `{ name, status, detail }` body, PR #58 pattern). **No `generation_log` write** — the wizard runs offer generation BEFORE the client row exists, and `generation_log.client_id` is NOT NULL; failures land in console + the 500 detail. Matches the `generate-seo` precedent.
- **`enhance-offer/route.ts`** — server-only Sonnet-backed offer-text polish. Called by `lib/website/offer-generate.ts` `enhanceFunnelOfferText` from the wizard's brief step "✦ Enhance with AI" button. Takes a rough offer paragraph the operator typed + light context (industry / business name / service area) and returns a tighter polished version (`{ text: string }`) — same voice, more concrete, no invented facts, same banned-corporate-speak list as `/api/generate-offer`. **Sonnet 4.6** (matches the offer-generation model choice); `thinking: { type: 'enabled', budget_tokens: 2000 }`, `max_tokens: 4000`. Returns `503` (key unset → caller throws `AppError.validation`), `400` (missing `rawText` or bad body), `500` (real failure with `{ name, status, detail }` body, PR #58 pattern). **No `generation_log` write** — the wizard runs this BEFORE the client row exists, same as `/api/generate-offer`. Replaces the previous `enhanceOffer` deterministic stub in `CreateClientModal.tsx` (4-rule text rewriter that did nothing when the input already passed all rules — the cause of the "Enhance with AI not working" report). Sibling of `/api/generate-offer`, distinct concern (polish a free-form paragraph vs draft the four-field structured offer).
- **`enhance-field/route.ts`** — server-only generic Sonnet-backed freeform-field enhancer. Sibling of `/api/enhance-offer` but with a different framing: research-grade copywriter who interviews the operator to draw out specificity, vs offer-route's direct-response conversion-copy framing. Body: `{ fieldName, currentValue, briefContext?: { businessName, industry, serviceArea, funnelService } }`. Response: `{ enhanced: string }`. **Sonnet 4.6**, `thinking: { type: 'enabled', budget_tokens: 2000 }`, `max_tokens: 4000` (Anthropic requires `max_tokens > budget_tokens`). Same fallback contract as `enhance-offer`: `503` (key unset → caller throws `AppError.validation`), `400` (missing `fieldName` or `currentValue`), `500` (real failure with `{ name, status, detail }` body, PR #58 pattern). **No `generation_log` write** — same precedent as `enhance-offer` / `generate-offer` / `generate-seo`: wizard runs before client row exists, `generation_log.client_id` is NOT NULL. Browser caller is `lib/website/field-enhance.ts` `enhanceField`. UI is `components/shared/EnhanceableTextarea` (accept/reject preview, see parked decision below). Used today by the wizard's `funnel_customer_pain` field. The offer field keeps `/api/enhance-offer` — different system prompt fits direct-response copy better than the generic specificity-drawing-out framing. Add new freeform brief-step fields to this route as the wizard grows; use `enhance-offer` only for offer-shaped copy.
- **`generate-funnel/route.ts`** — server-only Claude-backed funnel generator. **Two parallel Opus 4.7 calls** — one per non-deterministic step. Step 1 (lead-capture landing) = 8 sections in Sultanic / Suby + FAQ order (`hero → offer → reviews → features → trust → faq → reviews → form`); the form is restricted to **name + email only** and the same form is attached to the hero via the `Section.form` envelope so the visitor can convert above the fold OR at the bottom. The FAQ section between trust and reviews #2 handles 4–6 industry-specific objections (the prompt block already emits the industry template's `objectionHandlers` — see `industry-templates.ts` `renderIndustryPromptBlock`). Step 2 (qualification) = 4 sections (`hero → reviews → features → form`) reinforcing the booking decision and qualifying the lead — phone, service address, preferred date (`date` field), preferred time of day (`select`: Morning / Afternoon / Evening), budget (`select` with trade-typical bands). Step 3 (thanks) is deterministic chrome from `funnel/generation-stub.ts` reading the thanks-section defaults from `registry-meta.ts`'s `defaultDataValues` snapshot — the `schedulePicker` section type is no longer used. Both Claude calls share one `generation_id` so their combined fallback log writes as one group. Same fallback contract as `/api/generate-site`: `503` (key unset), `400` (bad body), `500` (real failure with `{ name, status, detail }` body). `maxDuration = 300`. **Lead-link across steps — WIRED.** The public `/api/forms/submit` route accepts an optional `existingLeadId`; when present and the lead belongs to the same `clientId`, the route appends a second `form_submitted` `lead_events` row to that lead instead of inserting a new one (mirrors the editor-side `submitLead(existingLeadId)` branch in `lib/leads/queries.tsx`). `FormBlock` reads `?lead=` from `window.location.search` on mount and posts it as `existingLeadId`; after a step-1 submission with `afterSubmit.kind === 'nextStep'`, it appends `?lead=<createdLeadId>` to the next-step URL. Step 1 + step 2 from one visitor therefore land as a single lead with two timeline events. See the parked decision "Funnel lead threading uses ?lead=<id> URL parameter" below for the trigger to revisit. Called by `lib/funnel/generation-stub.ts` `generateFunnelStub` via `fetch('/api/generate-funnel')`. **ONE Opus 4.7 call** generates the eight-section funnel-landing step in the locked Suby/Sultanic + FAQ order (`hero → offer → reviews → features → trust → faq → reviews → form`); the schedule + thanks steps stay deterministic (chrome-only, no inputs an LLM would need to differentiate them). Body is a `ClientBrief` + optional `clientId`. Returns a `FunnelGenerationResult` — same shape `generateFunnelSync` returns, so the client swaps stub for live transparently. Same fallback contract as `/api/generate-site`: `503` (key unset, caller silently falls back), `400` (bad body), `500` (real failure with `{ name, status, detail }` body — surfaced in `CreateClientModal` via `AppError`). Writes `generation_log` rows for every missing-field fallback via the service-role client, gated on `clientId`. Server-only — `@anthropic-ai/sdk` stays out of the browser bundle. `maxDuration = 300`. See the parked decision "Funnel vs offer generator model choice" for the Opus-here / Sonnet-on-offer split.

- **`lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts`** — server-only counterpart to `generate-live.ts`. Exports two functions: `generateFunnelLandingLive` (Step 1 — 7 sections) and `generateFunnelQualificationLive` (Step 2 — 4 sections). Both run Opus 4.7 with `thinking: { type: 'adaptive' }` (`max_tokens: 16000`, streamed, cached system prompt). Two separate system prompts: the lead-capture prompt enforces the Sultanic / Suby section order and frames the form as name+email-only minimum-friction; the qualification prompt frames the page as homestretch reassurance ("you're almost booked") and frames the features section as a concrete what-happens-next sequence. Both consume the same brand + funnel-brief + offer + testimonial set; the chosen offer's headline / promise / risk-reversal / CTA flow into Step 1 verbatim and are not re-pitched in Step 2. Defensive JSON parsing tolerant of code fences. The output runs through a funnelStep-typed validation pipeline (mirror of `runValidationPipeline` in `generation-stub.ts` — the website version is page-typed, so we duplicate that slice rather than refactor the registry pipeline). **Form-config builders live here**: Step 1's `buildLeadCaptureFormConfig` returns `{ name, email }` (submit label from the offer's CTA text), Step 2's `buildQualificationFormConfig` returns `{ phone, service-address, preferred-date (date), time-of-day (select Morning/Afternoon/Evening), budget (select with trade bands) }`. Both forms use `afterSubmit: { kind: 'nextStep' }` so the public renderer's step-router moves the visitor forward. On Step 1 the same form is also attached to the `hero` section via `Section.form` envelope (so the form appears above-the-fold AND at the bottom — both feed the same lead when leadId threading lands). Imported only by `/api/generate-funnel` so the Anthropic SDK never reaches the client bundle.

### `shared/website/` (cont'd) — form-to-page UI primitives (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 6)

- **`QuestionCard`** (`website/QuestionCard.tsx`) — single Q&A step inside `/website/new`. Composes `BuilderStepHeader` + body slot + `BuilderFooterActions`. Discriminates Continue vs Skip via `required` + `isAnswered`: required & empty disables Continue; optional & empty shows both "Skip →" and "Continue →". Body slot is open — chip rows, textareas, or the chip-or-free-text dual mode used by Q2's "Other" option.
- **`GenerationStatusCard`** (`website/GenerationStatusCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` ink-bg "// GENERATING ✦" card. Rotating ✦ glyph + "Drafting your page…" + phase copy cycling on a 1.6s interval (`GENERATION_PHASES`). When Q4 or Q5 had content, the card mounts a separate "// RECEIVED" footer block with ✓-prefixed lines reading "Got your specifics — will shape the final draft." / "Got your avoid notes — will be honoured." **Framing rule locked in the design doc §1:** never echo Q4/Q5 inline with phase copy as the AI consuming them in real time — that would mislead users into thinking the stub-output ignoring those answers is a bug.
- **`NewPageEntry`** (`website/NewPageEntry.tsx`) — the "+ New page" / "✦ New page" CTA on `/website`. Encapsulates the two-cap gating story (`editPages` + `useAI`): both → rust `Link` to `/website/new`; `editPages` only → hidden (V2 manual-new-page modal lands here later); missing `editPages` → `<CapabilityGate mode="request">` reveals the request-change affordance. Inlining this on the hub would force every reader to re-derive the three-state gating from the JSX; the wrapper keeps the hub readable.

### `app/website/new/` — Q&A generation flow (Phase 6 · Cluster 5 · Session 6)

- **`page.tsx`** — `'use client'` flow root. State lives in URL search params (`?step=N&pageType=...&intent=...&intentOther=...&audience=...&specifics=...&avoid=...`), no localStorage — refresh + back/forward work natively; 90-second form doesn't warrant cross-tab merge complexity. Six logical steps: 1-5 questions (each via `QuestionCard`) → 6 review summary with inline "Edit ✎" links bouncing back to the relevant question while preserving the rest. On Generate, mounts `GenerationStatusCard` with `specifics`/`avoid` passed through, calls `generatePageStub(ctx)`, writes via `addGeneratedPage`, routes to `/website/[newPageId]`. The route doesn't re-check caps (the gated `NewPageEntry` already filtered); the review-card Generate button is disabled with a fallback explainer if the user somehow lacks `editPages + useAI` on this workspace.

### `app/dev/generation-preview/` — Session 6 dev surface

- **`page.tsx`** — Off-nav dev utility per the `app/dev/` convention (deletion-point: same lifecycle as `/dev/capabilities` + `/dev/sections`). Three-column layout: inputs (page-type chips / intent chips + Other input / audience chips / specifics + avoid textareas) → prompt blocks (expandable per-block details) → stub output (Generated page summary + validation log + full JSON). All three columns re-render on every input change — no Generate button, the live linkage is the whole point. Validates the prompt-construction layer (which graduates to real backend) in isolation from the stub recipes (which don't).

### `admin/team/` — team-invite flow (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · team invite)

> **Architectural note — `/settings/team` is a shared-slug dispatcher (Cluster 6 · client invite).** Both roles now reach a "Team" tab from their own nav, so `app/settings/team/page.tsx` is a `'use client'` role dispatcher (same pattern as `/settings/integrations`): operator → `_admin-content.tsx` (the workspace team-invite flow below); client → `_client-content.tsx` (the client's own-account teammate list — see `app/settings/team/` entry). The 3-step operator modal stays admin-only by virtue of mounting only inside `_admin-content.tsx`.

> The first real management UI for the capability layer. A 3-step `Dialog`-based modal launched from the operator `/settings/team`. Screens 37-39 in the platform prototype. The flow captures org-structure decisions (who / what role / which clients) as a discrete attributable `TeamInvite` record (vision §7). Built as pure composition over `Dialog` / `Button` / `Input` / `Textarea` + the capability layer.
>
> **Prototype disagreements converged:** (1) the prototype's Step 2 allow/deny bullets ("Edit Meta ad campaigns", "See revenue/billing") are off the 13-cap builder model — the preview is driven **purely from the 13 real capabilities** instead (see the parked decision below). (2) The prototype shows a pre-filled readonly demo; the real modal is an empty interactive form. (3) The prototype sizes Step 3 narrower than Steps 1-2 — a single step-switching `Dialog` can't resize per step, so the flow uses one `size="lg"` (920px) throughout.

- **`TeamInviteModal`** (`team/TeamInviteModal.tsx`) — `'use client'` orchestrator. Owns step state (`1 | 2 | 3`) + the `TeamInviteDraft` form state + the committed `TeamInvite` once sent. Modal chrome comes from `shared/invite/InviteModalChrome` (extracted at the second use — see that entry). Step 1 = invite form (email / full name / role pick / client-access selection / personal note); Step 2 = invitee ink card + `PermissionPreview` + "what happens after" box; Step 3 = success state + copyable magic link + "what happens next". Step 1→2 is gated on a non-empty email and (for junior) ≥1 assigned client. On send, builds one `TeamInvite` record and (stub) `console.log`s it. Step-2 invitee card + Step-1 client-access row stay local subcomponents (operator-specific, single-use).
- **`InviteTeamButton`** (`team/InviteTeamButton.tsx`) — `'use client'` trigger: a `size="sm"` "+ Invite member" `Button` + `TeamInviteModal` open-state owner. Mounted on `/settings/team`. Same pattern as `AddBookingButton` / `NegativeReviewAlertButton`.
- **`InviteStepper`** (`team/InviteStepper.tsx`) — generic N-dot progress indicator. Props: `steps` + `current` (1-indexed). Steps before `current` render done (good check), `current` renders rust with a soft ring, the rest paper-2. First stepper primitive in the codebase — kept in `admin/team/` (only consumer); move to `shared/` if a second flow needs it.
- **`RoleSelectCard`** (`team/RoleSelectCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` selectable role card (icon tile + name + description), used 3-up in Step 1. Borrows `ReframeOptionCard`'s `data-selected` + rust-border-on-active idiom but is its own shape (compact icon-tile card vs `ReframeOptionCard`'s 22px display-headline card — reuse would have fought both).
- **`PermissionPreview`** (`team/PermissionPreview.tsx`) — **the cap-wired component.** Iterates `ALL_CAPABILITIES`, partitions allow/deny by membership in `TEAM_ROLE_CAPABILITIES[role]`, labels each with `CAPABILITY_LABEL`, and uses `CAP_EXPLAINER[cap].short` as the deny-line hover title. Never a hand-written list — role → permissions is computed. Renders a one-line note for owner/operator explaining they look identical here because they only diverge on billing/governance (outside the cap model).

### `shared/invite/` — invite-modal chrome (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · client invite)

> Extracted at the second use (operator `TeamInviteModal` + client `ClientTeamInviteModal`). Deliberately the **intersection** of what both modals need — the structural rhythm + the two in-body form primitives — not the union. Anything one modal needs and the other never does (operator role-pick, client seat-meter) stays composed in that modal, never bolted on here as an optional prop.

- **`InviteModalChrome`** (`invite/InviteModalChrome.tsx`) — exports: `INVITE_DIALOG_CONTENT_CLASS` (the shared `DialogContent` className — each modal still composes its own `Dialog`/`DialogContent size="lg"`), `InviteModalHeader` (rust/good mono tag + `<em>`-rust title + subtitle + close), `InviteModalFooter` (mono info line + action-button slot), `InviteSection` (labelled form section with `last` rhythm flag), `InviteFieldLabel` (mono uppercase field label + optional `required` asterisk), `InviteCopyLinkRow` (the dashed-border magic-link + copy button on both confirmation steps), and the `inviteInitials(fullName, email)` helper.

### `client/team/` — client-side teammate invite (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · client invite)

> The client-role counterpart to the operator team-invite. A client business owner invites a user into their **own** client account — fixed client (no picker), flat access (no role pick): every invitee resolves to the `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` floor (`viewBuilder` only); per-website edit grants stay an operator concern via `/settings/access`. With no role/access decision to review, the flow is **2 steps, not 3** — inventing a review step for a flat invite would be drift (same logic as Session 3's Step-2 call). The access reality is communicated inline on Step 1. Net-new — the client prototype has no team surface.

- **`ClientTeamInviteModal`** (`team/ClientTeamInviteModal.tsx`) — `'use client'` 2-step `Dialog` modal. Composes `shared/invite/InviteModalChrome`. Step 1 = form (email required / optional full name / default-access explainer / `SeatUsageMeter` + seat-blocked warn block / optional note); Step 2 = success state + `InviteCopyLinkRow` + "what happens next". The send is seat-gated — `canInviteToClient(clientId)` disables the Send button AND re-guards inside `handleSend` (the count can move while the modal is open). On send, commits one attributable `ClientUserInvite` via `addClientInvite`.
- **`InviteTeammateButton`** (`team/InviteTeammateButton.tsx`) — `'use client'` "+ Invite teammate" trigger + modal open-state owner. Resolves the inviter's own `clientId` from `useUser()`; renders null for a user with no client. Sibling of `admin/team/InviteTeamButton`.
- **`SeatUsageMeter`** (`team/SeatUsageMeter.tsx`) — presentational "N of M seats used" indicator (bar + count, or uncapped variant when `limit` is null). Takes a resolved `SeatUsage` — the caller fetches it reactively via `useClientSeatUsage`. Used on the client Team tab, inside `ClientTeamInviteModal`, and inside the operator `ClientSeatLimitCard`.

### `shared/settings/` (cont'd) — client seat-limit control (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · client invite)

- **`ClientSeatLimitCard`** (`settings/ClientSeatLimitCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` operator control for one client's seat limit, mounted on `/settings/access` in **sub-account mode** as a visually-distinct `SettingsSection` separate from the capability grid (the seat limit is a contract/plan axis — how many users — not the capability axis — what users can do). Number input + "No limit" checkbox + Save (disabled until dirty); shows the live `SeatUsageMeter` and the most-recent `SeatLimitChange`. **Cluster 8 · Session 4b** — resolver-backed: the limit resolves through `resolvePolicy('defaultSeatLimit', clientId)`, so the card shows a `PolicySourceBadge` (inherited vs a per-account override) and a "Revert to agency" affordance (`inheritSeatLimit`) when overridden. **Cluster 9 · Session 1** — the inherited-source hint distinguishes "from plan" vs "from agency" via `getInheritedSeatLimit` (the plan layer can supply the inherited seat limit). Admin-only — placed in `shared/settings/` following the `CapabilityToggleGrid` precedent. Calls `setSeatLimit` with the operator's id for attribution.
- **`PlanEditorCard`** (`settings/PlanEditorCard.tsx`) — `'use client'` Cluster 9 · Session 2. Operator editor for one billing plan, mounted on `/settings/plans` (agency mode). Edits the plan's identity (name / description / price / currency / billing cycle) and its policy bundle — seat limit, capability floor (`Switch` per `ALL_CAPABILITIES`), integration defaults (`Switch` per `INTEGRATION_PROVIDERS`). Local draft state with a previous-render re-sync; Save writes through `upsertPlan`, Delete (confirm) through `removePlan`. Admin-only — in `shared/settings/` following the `CapabilityToggleGrid` / `ClientSeatLimitCard` precedent.
- **`PolicyOverrideRow`** (`settings/PolicyOverrideRow.tsx`) — `'use client'` Cluster 8 · Session 4b. The canonical "inherited from agency / overridden here" affordance for sub-account settings: a label + an inherited/overridden source badge + the agency value hint when inherited + a "Revert to agency" action when overridden; the control is `children` (the parent owns what "override" means for its policy key). Sibling export **`PolicySourceBadge`** is the standalone pill (used by `ClientSeatLimitCard`). Consumed today by the sub-account integrations view.

### `app/settings/team/` — shared-slug Team tab (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · client invite)

- **`page.tsx`** — `'use client'` role dispatcher (operator → `_admin-content`, client → `_client-content`).
- **`_admin-content.tsx`** — the operator workspace team page (`AdminSettingsTeamContent`) — team members + role-permission matrix + the `InviteTeamButton`.
- **`_client-content.tsx`** — the client's own-account view (`ClientSettingsTeamContent`) — `SeatUsageMeter` + `InviteTeammateButton`, the current-users list + pending invites (both via the shared `TeamRow`), and a "what teammates can do" explainer. Reactive to the client-invite store so a freshly-sent invite appears immediately.

### `lib/team/` — team-invite data shapes + roles

- **`types.ts`** — `TeamInviteStatus` (now a re-alias of `InviteStatus` from `lib/invites/shared-types` — single-sourced so the operator + client invite siblings can't drift), `TeamInviteDraft` (mutable form state — `{ email, fullName, role, assignedClientIds, personalNote }`), and the committed `TeamInvite` (draft + `id`, `invitedBy` (operator user id — an invite without it is unattributable, vision §7), `invitedAt` / `expiresAt` (ISO strings), `magicLink`, `status`). Stub-becomes-schema-contract: every field is producible from real DB rows + lookups with no narrative interpretation.
- **`roles.ts`** — `TeamRole` (`'owner' | 'operator' | 'junior'` — the operator-tier org role, distinct from `Role` in `capabilities.ts`), `TEAM_ROLES` (the 3 role defs: id / name / icon glyph / description), and `TEAM_ROLE_CAPABILITIES: Record<TeamRole, readonly Capability[]>` — **derived** from the cap layer: owner + operator inherit `ADMIN_DEFAULTS` verbatim; junior is a deliberate subset (`viewBuilder`, `editCopy`, `editMedia`, `editSEO`, `useAI` — `editSEO` is deliberately in, since SEO drafts ≠ SEO publishes and the `publish` gate still requires operator). `getTeamRoleDef(role)` helper.

### `lib/invites/` — invite primitives + client teammate invite (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · client invite)

> `ClientUserInvite` is a **sibling** of `lib/team/types.ts` `TeamInvite`, NOT a generalization — the dimensions genuinely differ (no Webnua-org role; a single fixed `clientId` not `assignedClientIds[]`; a client-user inviter; different RLS/lifecycle). Two clean siblings beat one record with conditional optional fields. Only the genuinely-common primitives are shared.

- **`shared-types.ts`** — `InviteStatus` (`'pending' | 'accepted' | 'expired' | 'revoked'` — the lifecycle union both invite siblings use; `lib/team` `TeamInviteStatus` re-aliases it), `IsoTimestamp` / `MagicLink` (convention-carrying string aliases), `INVITE_TTL_DAYS` (= 7).
- **`client-invite.ts`** — `ClientUserInviteDraft` (mutable form state — `{ email, fullName, personalNote }`) + the committed `ClientUserInvite` (`id`, `email`, `fullName`, fixed `clientId`, `invitedBy` (client user id — attributable, vision §7), `invitedAt` / `expiresAt`, `magicLink`, `status: InviteStatus`, `personalNote: string | null`). Stub-becomes-schema-contract.
- **`client-invite-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`.** Invite list backed by `client_user_invites`. `addClientInvite` writes through; `getInvitesForClient` (pending only), `getAllClientInvites` (snapshot-cached for `useSyncExternalStore` stability), `subscribeClientInvites`.
- **`seats.ts`** — seat accounting. `getClientSeatUsage(clientId)` → `SeatUsage` (`usedByUsers` + `usedByInvites` + `total` + `limit`); usage is **derived** (existing client users + pending invites — pending counts so the limit can't be gamed by bulk-inviting). `canInviteToClient(clientId)` → `{ allowed, reason? }` (`reason: InviteBlockReason` — `'seat_limit_reached'` today, union kept open) — backs both the modal's Continue gate and the send guard.
- **`use-seat-usage.ts`** — `useClientSeatUsage(clientId)` hook — `useSyncExternalStore` over both feeder stores (client invites + seat limits), snapshot-cached against a derived key so the reference only changes when the counts change.

### `lib/clients/` — per-client seat limit + identity tones (Phase 6 · Cluster 6–7)

- **`tones.ts`** (Session 7) — the canonical **solid per-client identity colour** map: `ClientTone` (the superset union — `voltline | freshhome | keyhero | neatworks | flowline | generic`) + `CLIENT_TONE_BG` / `CLIENT_TONE_BORDER_L` (pre-composed Tailwind class records, because arbitrary-value classes can't be built from runtime strings). Consumed by `BookingPill`, `CalendarLegend`, `CalendarTodayPanel`, `AdminBookingHero`, and `AutomationFlowMini`. Promoted out of `lib/calendar/tones.ts` in Session 7 once automations became the fourth consumer (calendar was the wrong home for a cross-domain map). Feature modules keep their narrower tone unions (`CalendarClientTone`, `AutomationClientTone`) and index the wider record. The muted pill-tint vocabularies (`LeadClientTone` / `AdminTicketClientTone`) are a separate concern — not here (see the resolved parked decision).
- **`seat-limit.ts`** — `SeatLimitChange` (`{ changedBy, changedAt, clientId, previousLimit, newLimit }`, limits `number | null`) — every limit change is an attributable event (vision §7); history is an array of these, not a single overwritten value.
- **`seat-limit-stub.ts`** — **Supabase-backed cache, hydrated by `DataHydrationProvider`.** **Cluster 8 · Session 4b — a facade over the agency policy resolver**, not a standalone store. The seat limit is the `defaultSeatLimit` policy key: the effective limit resolves down the layers (`resolvePolicy('defaultSeatLimit', clientId)`) — agency default (Layer 2) → per-account override (Layer 3, `override-stub`). This module keeps the seat-limit export surface (`getSeatLimit`, `getAgencySeatLimit`, `isSeatLimitOverridden`, `setSeatLimit` = set an override, `inheritSeatLimit` = clear it, `subscribeSeatLimits`) and owns the change-history log (Supabase `seat_limit_changes` table — `getSeatLimitHistory`, `subscribeSeatLimitHistory`), which the generic override store doesn't track. `getSeatLimit`/`subscribeSeatLimits` keep their old names so `lib/invites/seats.ts` + `use-seat-usage.ts` are unchanged.

> Note: `AdminClient` (`lib/nav/admin-clients.ts`) carried a `seatLimit` field through Cluster 6; **Cluster 8 · Session 4b retired it** — the per-client seed values moved into `SUB_ACCOUNT_OVERRIDE_SEED` (`lib/agency/override-stub.ts`) and the seat limit now resolves through the `defaultSeatLimit` policy key.

### `lib/onboarding/` + `app/onboarding/` — Pattern B onboarding wizard (Session C)

> The 7-step wizard that captures industry / business / target / brand / testimonials / integrations / done for a freshly-signed-up Pattern B client. Mounted at `/onboarding`, gated by the dashboard's lifecycle redirect (preview + null `wizard_completed_at` → /onboarding). Persists state to `clients.wizard_state` (jsonb, migration 0091) on every step transition so a refresh resumes exactly where the customer left off. **Fires background website + funnel generation on step 4** so the site is ready by step 7.
>
> **Operators don't see this surface** — the wizard route redirects an admin-role user to /dashboard, where the concierge `IntegrationOnboarding` surface (with the manual "Mark active" affordance) is the right tool.

- **`lib/onboarding/types.ts`** — `WizardState` (`{ current_step, completed_steps[], step_data }`) + per-step `Step1Data`…`Step6Data` shapes. Step 7 has no data (the "done" surface). `WizardStepId = 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | 6 | 7`. `INITIAL_WIZARD_STATE` is the fresh-start value. **Adding a step or a field** means amending this type AND providing a sensible default (the JSON column tolerates extras; readers default-coalesce on absence).
- **`lib/onboarding/industry-colors.ts`** — `INDUSTRY_PRIMARY_COLORS: Record<IndustryKey, string>` — per-industry primary-colour defaults seeded into step 4's colour picker. Emergency-callout trades lean warm + high-contrast (electrician amber, plumber blue), scheduled trades lean soft (cleaner mint, landscaper green), project trades lean neutral. `generic` falls back to Webnua rust. **Trigger to revisit**: the customer overrides via the wizard's colour picker, so this is the SEED only; if the industry templates ever grow their own `defaultPrimaryColor` field, fold this in (see the parked-decision answer locking this in here). `deriveSecondaryColor(primary)` is a pure heuristic (primary * 0.78) for the auto-derived secondary.
- **`lib/onboarding/wizard-state.ts`** — load + save the wizard state via the browser Supabase client. `loadWizardState(clientId)`, `saveWizardState`, `markWizardComplete`, `isWizardComplete`. **Persistence is fire-and-forget** — local React state advances synchronously; a write failure surfaces inline. Resume always re-reads the server state, which is the SoT.
- **`lib/onboarding/derive-brief.ts`** — pure (no I/O). Converts `WizardState` into a `ClientBrief` the generators (`generateSiteStub` / `generateFunnelStub`) consume. **Funnel brief fields are derived from existing wizard data per the locked plan**: `funnel.service ← step1.services[0]`, `funnel.customerPain ← step3.targetCustomer framed via the industry's urgency mode`, `funnel.guarantee ← step3.usp OR template.objectionHandlers[0].response`. Skipped steps fall back to industry-template defaults + signup fallbacks.
- **`app/onboarding/layout.tsx`** — standalone layout (no sidebar / Topbar). Just `BrandMark` + a generous canvas. Mobile-first.
- **`app/onboarding/page.tsx`** — `'use client'` lifecycle gate + state loader. Operators → /dashboard; pending_verification / non-preview lifecycle → /dashboard; already-completed wizard → /dashboard; preview + no wizard yet → mounts `WizardShell` with the persisted state.
- **`app/onboarding/_wizard-shell.tsx`** — the orchestrator. Owns the wizard state, dispatches per-step components, owns the `triggerGeneration` flow (fires the moment step 4 commits with retries 0/1s/3s exponential), owns the persist-on-transition writes. The shell renders a `ProgressIndicator` (one notch per step, rust-filled up to current).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/_step-frame.tsx`** — shared StepFrame chrome: title + description + Back / Skip / Continue actions in a mobile-friendly layout (stacked below md, side-by-side above). Per-step bodies stay focused on their inputs.
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step1Industry.tsx`** — REQUIRED step. Dropdown of the 11 known industries + "Other". The **industry-mirror block** appears the moment the customer picks: shows the template's services + trust signals as toggleable chips, with a custom-entry field. The conversion lever — the customer immediately sees Webnua "gets" their trade. "Other" routes to free-text + manual entry. Drives `clients.industry` AND `brands.industry_category` in lockstep (they're synced at signup; the wizard keeps them aligned).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step2Business.tsx`** — Skippable. Business name + service area + phone + hours + (optional) address. Email is read-only (Pattern B's signup-time email is the auth SoT; changing it via Settings post-publish).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step3Target.tsx`** — Skippable. Target customer (chip-select or free text) + average job value (free text) + optional starting-price framing + optional USP. Drives `audienceLine`, `funnel.customerPain` framing, and `funnel.guarantee`.
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step4Brand.tsx`** — Skippable. Logo upload (Supabase Storage `section-media` bucket via `uploadSectionImage`) + primary colour (seeded from `INDUSTRY_PRIMARY_COLORS`) + secondary colour (auto-derived) + tagline + tone preset (friendly / professional / casual). **Background generation fires on this step's commit** — the wizard advances to step 5 while site + funnel build asynchronously. Writes through to the `brands` row directly via Supabase (the brand-style helper's key set doesn't cover `accent_color` / `logo_url`).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step5Testimonials.tsx`** — Skippable. 0–3 testimonials. Empty array → the funnel renders the "Your customer reviews will appear here" placeholder (per CLAUDE.md — we NEVER invent quotes).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step6Integrations.tsx`** — All individually skippable. Mounts the same `IntegrationConnectionsSection` used everywhere else (returnTo=/onboarding so OAuth callback lands here) for Meta Ads + Google Business Profile. Custom domain shows as a "later" checkbox (the real attach happens post-publish from /settings/domains).
- **`app/onboarding/_steps/Step7Done.tsx`** — The conversion landing. Summary card (industry, services, integrations connected, default automations, site status) + three CTAs: "See your site" (opens preview), "Publish to go live" (links to /dashboard's PublishToGoLiveCTA → Stripe Checkout), "See my dashboard" (primary — marks wizard complete + routes). Generation status card surfaces ready / running / failed-with-retry.
- **`app/api/clients/[id]/wizard-state/route.ts`** — `GET` returns `{ completed, state }` (dashboard's wizard-completion check + the wizard's resume read both go through this). `POST { state, complete? }` upserts the wizard state + optionally stamps `wizard_completed_at`. Auth: `requireClientAccess` — customer for own client, operator concierge.

### `lib/billing/cancellation*` + `app/api/clients/[id]/{cancel,reactivate}` — Pattern B two-stage cancellation (Session C)

> Two-stage soft delete + 30-day grace + 60-day operator recovery + day-83 warning email + day-90 hard delete. Customer-facing cancellation via the Stripe Customer Portal; the webhook drives every lifecycle transition. **Migrations 0090 (enum) + 0091 (columns + cron).**
>
> Stages: Stage 1 (`'cancelled'`, day 0–30): customer can log in, sees the CancellationBanner with a Reactivate CTA. Stage 2 (`'deleted'`, day 30–90): customer locked out, operator-only recovery out-of-band. Stage 3 (day 83): cron sends 7-day-warning email. Stage 4 (day 90): cron HARD-deletes the row via cascade FKs.

- **`lib/billing/cancellation.ts`** — SERVER-ONLY. `applyStripeCancellation(clientId)` (Stripe `subscription.deleted` → set lifecycle 'cancelled' + cancelled_at + data_deletion_scheduled_at = NOW() + 30 days; idempotent, refuses to reset a row already 'cancelled' / terminal). `reactivateClient(clientId)` (Stripe `subscription.created` on a 'cancelled' client → flip to 'active' + clear timestamps; refuses 'deleted' rows — that recovery is operator-only). `daysUntilDeletion(scheduledAt)` is the pure helper the banner consumes. Constants `STAGE_1_GRACE_DAYS = 30` / `STAGE_2_WARNING_DAYS_AFTER_SCHEDULE = 53` / `STAGE_3_HARD_DELETE_DAYS_AFTER_SCHEDULE = 60` — keep in lockstep with migration 0091's cron math.
- **`lib/billing/cancellation-warning-email.ts`** — SERVER-ONLY. Sister of `re-engagement-email.ts` + `welcome-email.ts`. Minimal inline Resend send via `callExternal`. Degrades to 'skipped' when RESEND_API_KEY unset (the handler still stamps `hard_delete_warning_sent_at` so the cron doesn't loop).
- **`lib/billing/cancellation-warning-handler.ts`** — registers the `send_cancellation_warning_email` integration_jobs handler. The daily cron (migration 0091 stage 2) enqueues one job per eligible client on day 83. Handler: load → eligibility re-check → resolve recipient → send → stamp. Failures re-throw (retry); skipped sends still stamp.
- **`app/api/clients/[id]/cancel/route.ts`** — `POST`, `requireClientAccess`. Mints a Stripe Customer Portal session and returns the URL. We deliberately do NOT touch `lifecycle_status` here — Stripe is the SoT; the webhook handles the lifecycle flip when the customer confirms cancellation on Stripe's hosted UI.
- **`app/api/clients/[id]/reactivate/route.ts`** — `POST`, `requireClientAccess`. Refuses for `lifecycle_status !== 'cancelled'` (with explicit `deleted-recovery-operator-only` for the day-30+ case). Mints a Stripe Checkout session for the standard plan; on payment the webhook calls `reactivateClient` which flips 'cancelled' → 'active' and clears the timestamps.
- **`components/shared/CancellationBanner.tsx`** — `'use client'`. High-vis warn-tinted banner mounted on /dashboard when lifecycle is 'cancelled', and on /settings/billing for the same state. Self-fetches `cancelled_at` + `data_deletion_scheduled_at` (keeps the clients-store free of cancellation-specific columns — they're rare). Reactivate button POSTs `/api/clients/[id]/reactivate` and follows the returned Stripe Checkout URL.
- **Webhook extension (`app/api/integrations/stripe/webhook/route.ts`)**: `subscription.created` now ALSO calls `reactivateClient` after the publish-pay path (idempotent — no-op for non-'cancelled' rows). `subscription.deleted` now ALSO calls `applyStripeCancellation` after the existing `applySubscriptionEvent` (sets `lifecycle_status='cancelled'` + the grace timestamps).
- **Dashboard gate (`app/dashboard/page.tsx`)**: routes a client-role + preview-lifecycle + no `wizard_completed_at` user to /onboarding; mounts `CancellationBanner` for 'cancelled' lifecycle; bounces 'deleted' lifecycle to /(auth)/login. The wizard-completion check fires via `/api/clients/[id]/wizard-state` GET — async to keep the clients-store free of an extra column for one redirect.

---

## Migration log (recent)

> One line per migration since the May 2026 audit found inventory drift.
> Older migrations are referenced inline in the relevant inventory entries.

- **`0023_seed_builder_websites_funnels.sql`** — PR #41. Seed rows for the builder family (websites + funnels + their draft versions) so the editor has something to open after a fresh hydration.
- **`0024_brands_capability_rls.sql`** — PR #43. RLS policies for `brands` + `capability_grants` once the auth + cap layer landed.
- **`0025_seed_agency_billing.sql`** — PR #43. Seed rows for the agency policy + plan catalog + plan assignment tables (the Layer-2 / Layer-2.5 of the policy resolver).
- **`0026_section_type_enum_additions.sql`** — PR #45. Adds `features`, `gallery`, `about`, `contact` to the `section_type` Postgres enum to match the section-library uplift.
- **`0027_section_media_bucket.sql`** — PR #45 era. Storage bucket + RLS for the per-section media uploads (`uploadSectionImage`).
- **`0028_fix_clients_select_returning.sql`** — PR #45. Drop / re-add `clients_select` policy so `INSERT … RETURNING *` from `create-client.ts` works.
- **`0029_capability_enum_add_editforms.sql`** — PR #46. Adds `editforms` to the `capability` Postgres enum.
- **`0030_section_type_add_form.sql`** — PR #46. Adds `form` to the `section_type` enum.
- **`0031_lead_attachments_bucket.sql`** — PR #46. Storage bucket + RLS for the form-builder image-attachment uploads.
- **`0032_notification_write_path.sql`** — Phase 9. `AFTER INSERT` triggers fanning notifications + the `supabase_realtime` publication entries (already referenced inline above).
- **`0033_funnel_slug.sql`** — funnel-slug add.
- **`0034_normalise_site_domains.sql`** — domain-host normalisation pass.
- **`0035_analytics_tables.sql`** — visitor-engagement tracking tables (PR #52 era).
- **`0036_funnel_brief_fields.sql`** — adds `funnel_service` / `funnel_customer_pain` / `funnel_guarantee` (text) + `funnel_testimonials` (jsonb, default `[]`) to `public.funnels`. Captured by the wizard's brief step; consumed by the AI funnel offer generator in a later session. No standalone `briefs` table — funnel-specific brief data lives with the funnel, matching the existing pattern where brief data lands on the entity tables it semantically belongs to (business identity on `clients`, brand voice on `brands`).
- **`0037_funnel_offer.sql`** — adds `funnel_offer jsonb` (nullable) to `public.funnels`. Shape: `{ headline, promise, risk_reversal, cta_text }`. Populated by the wizard's funnel-offer step (Sonnet-backed `/api/generate-offer`) when the operator runs offer generation; NULL when the operator skipped the step or the run failed. Single jsonb (not four text columns) because the four fields are one unit of data — always created, edited and rendered together. Matches the `funnel_testimonials` shape.
- **`0038_form_submit_error_enum.sql`** + **`0039_form_submit_error_aggregation.sql`** — analytics-audit §5.2 gap #1. Added `form_submit_error` to `analytics_event_type` and the matching `form_failed` rollup stage so a failed `/api/forms/submit` no longer counts as a success.
- **`0040_form_abandon_aggregation.sql`** — analytics-audit §5.2 gap #2. Added the missing `when event_type = 'form_abandon' then 'form_abandoned'` branch so abandons roll up instead of being pruned at 90d.
- **`0041_scroll_and_click_aggregation.sql`** — closes analytics-audit §3 / §4 website-side gaps. Adds three previously-dropped scroll-depth stages (`scrolled_25`, `scrolled_75`, `scrolled_90`; existing `engaged` keeps the canonical 50% label so prior consumers stay wired). Adds `element_label text not null default ''` to `analytics_funnel_daily` and extends the PK to `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label)`, so per-CTA click rollup rows are queryable. The aggregator populates `element_label` from `payload->>'label'` (truncated 120 chars) for `element_click` events; all other stages write `''`. Surfaced on `/website` via the new `WebsiteEngagementCard` (scroll-depth breakdown + top CTAs + form completion) and per-page `PageGridCard` visit/avg-time stats from a new `fetchPageTotalsByRef` helper. Does NOT touch the funnel rollup's `page_ref` step-granularity (audit §2.2) — that's closed by 0042.
- **`0042_funnel_step_granularity.sql`** — closes analytics-audit §2.2 / §2.6 + the CLAUDE.md parked decision "Funnel analytics gaps that remain after lead threading". Adds `page_ref text not null default ''` to `analytics_funnel_daily` and extends the PK to `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label, page_ref)`; the aggregator's GROUP BY gains `page_ref`. A funnel's step-1 (`page_ref = ''`, served at the funnel root) and step-2 (`page_ref = <step.slug>`) now roll up as distinct rows, so step-by-step drop-off is queryable. Empty-string sentinel matches the `element_label` convention from 0041 — no NULL in PK. Backwards-compatible: website surfaces typically have a single `page_ref` per surface, and the existing `fetchSurfaceFunnelTotals` reads (which sum across all `page_ref` rows) produce the same totals. The new `fetchFunnelStepBreakdown(surfaceId, pageRefs)` consumes the per-step axis; surfaced on `/funnels/[id]` (the prototype Screen 23 detail). The 90-day raw-event window means existing events back-fill on the next aggregator tick — rollup table was empty at apply time so no data preservation concern.
- **`0043_lead_source_kind.sql`** — adds `source_kind text not null default 'website'` to `public.leads`, check-constrained to `'website' | 'funnel' | 'meta'`. Surfaces the categorical surface attribution on the inbox as a Source column / pill (`LeadSourcePill`). Written by `/api/forms/submit` from a new `surfaceKind` body field (`'website' | 'funnel'`) the public renderer + the editor test-submit both populate via `PublicFormSubmit.surfaceKind` and `FormTestSubmitContext.surfaceKind`. `meta` is reserved for the future Meta lead-ads integration — the value is in the constraint now so the enum doesn't churn when it lands. Plain text + check (not a Postgres enum) — cheaper to extend later when new surfaces (e.g. `'gbp'`, `'referral'`) are added.
- **`0044_lead_source_funnel_id.sql`** — adds `source_funnel_id uuid` to `public.leads` (nullable, FK to `public.funnels`, `on delete set null`) + a single-column index on the FK. Pairs with `source_kind` from `0043`: the kind is *categorical* (website / funnel / meta) for the inbox column; this is the *entity FK* a client can run multiple funnels against. NULL = captured outside a funnel (every website-form submission + every lead created before this migration). Written by `/api/forms/submit` (only when `surfaceKind === 'funnel'`, with a cross-tenant guard that the funnel belongs to the posted `clientId`). The public renderer threads it through via a new `funnelId` field on `PublicFormSubmit` + the `PublicSiteRenderer` `funnel`-case prop. Powers `getBookedFromFunnelCount` (`lib/analytics/queries.tsx`) — one count over `leads` filtered by `source_funnel_id` + `status in ('booked', 'completed')` + capture window (`leads.created_at`, default 7 days matching the funnel hero's "Funnel performance · 7 days"). Closes the CLAUDE.md "Funnel-to-lead attribution" parked decision; the `/funnels/[id]` hero "booked from this funnel" tile now renders real numbers instead of `—`. Leads created before this migration carry NULL and are correctly excluded. **Editor test-submit attribution is intentionally NOT wired** — `submitLead` (`lib/leads/queries.tsx`) and `FormTestSubmitContext` (`lib/website/form-config.ts`) don't carry a `funnelId`, so editor test leads from a funnel preview carry `source_kind = 'funnel'` but `source_funnel_id = NULL`. Test leads are vanishingly rare in production analytics; thread `funnelId` through `FormTestSubmitContext` + `submitLead` later if test traffic starts polluting the count.
- **`0045_rls_cross_tenant_fixes.sql`** — closes three cross-tenant RLS holes the Section-A validation pass found (harness: `tests/rls/`, run with `pnpm test:rls`; doc: `reference/rls-test-suite.md`). (1) **`users` privilege escalation** — `users_update`'s `WITH CHECK` only re-asserts row ownership, so a client could `update public.users set role='admin', client_id=null, team_role='owner' where id=auth.uid()` and become an operator (or move `client_id` to another tenant); fixed with a `BEFORE UPDATE` trigger (`private.guard_user_identity_columns`) that makes `role`/`client_id`/`team_role` immutable to non-operators (RLS `WITH CHECK` can't compare OLD vs NEW — a trigger can). (2) **`website_versions_insert`** + (3) **`website_approval_submissions_insert`** gated `INSERT` purely on `private.has_capability()`, which is true for a workspace-wide (`website_id IS NULL`) grant on *any* website — so a client holding such a grant could write versions/approvals into another tenant's website; fixed by ANDing a tenant-membership `EXISTS` clause onto each `WITH CHECK`. All three verified live before + after the fix. The funnel-side equivalents already carried the tenant check and were unaffected.
- **`0046_funnel_publish_realtime.sql`** — A3 (funnel publish + approval lane). Adds the four builder tables — `website_approval_submissions`, `funnel_approval_submissions`, `website_versions`, `funnel_versions` — to the `supabase_realtime` publication so `RealtimeProvider` can subscribe to `postgres_changes` and fan a `BUILDER_EVENT` (a submitter's editor lock clears when an operator resolves; a published version surfaces on the detail / roster). RLS still scopes which change events each user receives. Each `alter publication` is wrapped in a `duplicate_object`-tolerant `DO` block. The `funnel_approval_submissions` *table* already existed (pre-aligned in migration 0015) — this migration adds no tables. **It supersedes B1's separate `0046_realtime_website_approvals.sql`** (which added `website_approval_submissions` only) — that file was a same-numbered duplicate from a parallel branch and was folded into this superset migration during the B1↔A3 merge.
- **`0047_integration_call_log.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. Audit log of every external API call + inbound webhook (provider / operation / direction / redacted request+response shapes / status / latency / error class+message / client_id / correlation_id). Operator-only tenant-scoped RLS; service-role writes. Single table for V1 — monthly-partition path documented in the migration comment.
- **`0048_integration_jobs.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. The async-work queue (status / attempts / run_after / provider / job_type / payload / result / error). Internal infrastructure — RLS on with zero policies, all `authenticated` privileges revoked; service-role only.
- **`0049_integration_jobs_cron.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. `pg_cron` poller (every minute) dispatching due jobs to `/api/internal/job-executor` via `pg_net`; reclaims stale `running` jobs after a 10-min lease. Adds `private.integration_runtime_config` (single-row table holding the executor base URL + shared secret — operator populates once post-deploy; see the table comment).
- **`0050_client_sms_senders.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. Per-client Twilio alphanumeric one-way SMS sender assignment (one per client, ≤11-char, registration-status lifecycle). Operator-only tenant-scoped RLS; service-role writes.
- **`0051_client_email_senders.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. Per-client Resend email sub-address slug (the sending address `[slug]@mail.webnua.com` is composed in app code, not stored). Operator-only RLS; service-role writes.
- **`0052_client_stripe_customers.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. Per-client Stripe Customer mapping (standard scope, no Connect). Operator-only RLS; service-role writes.
- **`0053_notifications_outbound.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 1. Audit log of operator-facing notification emails sent (throttle + audit; carries the Resend message id). Operator-only tenant-scoped RLS.
- **`0054_vault_setup.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 2. Supabase Vault (`supabase_vault`) + four `public` SECURITY DEFINER wrapper functions (`webnua_vault_create_secret` / `_read_secret` / `_update_secret` / `_delete_secret`) so server code can mint/read/rotate/delete encrypted secrets — EXECUTE revoked from `public` / `anon` / `authenticated`, granted to `service_role` only. The `vault` schema is not PostgREST-reachable; the wrappers bridge it. Fallback (pgsodium) documented in the migration comment.
- **`0055_integration_connections.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 2. The per-tenant OAuth connection table — one row per customer account per provider. Generic across providers; supports both token models (`token_model`: `refresh_access` / `long_lived`). The persistent secret lives in Vault (`token_secret_id`); only the short-lived Google access token is plain (`access_token_cached`). Operator-only tenant-scoped RLS; service-role writes; clients get no access.
- **`0056_token_refresh_cron.sql`** — Phase 7 Session 2. Daily `pg_cron` schedule that enqueues a `token_refresh_check` job onto the Session 1 jobs spine — the handler proactively refreshes `long_lived` (Meta) connections before expiry.
- **`0057_stripe_pricing.sql`** — Phase 7 Stripe billing. Extends `client_stripe_customers` (from `0052`) with the subscription posture the Stripe webhook keeps current: `stripe_subscription_id`, `stripe_price_id`, `current_period_end`, `cancel_at_period_end`, `last_payment_at`, `last_payment_status`, `past_due_since`, `updated_at`. Adds `'incomplete'` to the `status` check (a customer record with no subscription yet — the checkout route inserts the row before Checkout completes) and re-defaults `status` to `'incomplete'`. Pricing stays env config — the €299/month Price id lives in `STRIPE_PRICE_ID_STANDARD`, not a table; the migration comment documents the path to a `stripe_prices` table once there is more than one tier. RLS unchanged (`client_stripe_customers` stays operator-SELECT / service-role-write).
- **`0058_client_sms_sender_registration.sql`** — Phase 7 Twilio SMS. Adds `twilio_registration_sid` to `client_sms_senders` (from `0050`) — the Twilio AlphaSender resource SID `registerSenderID()` writes and `getSenderIDStatus()` polls. NULL until the operator submits a sender id. RLS / grants unchanged (the column inherits the table's operator-SELECT / service-role-write policy).
- **`0059_sms_messages.sql`** — Phase 7 Twilio SMS. The SMS send log — one row per outbound send: `client_id`, `sender_id` (the alphanumeric value snapshot), `recipient_phone`, `message_body`, `segments_count` + `encoding` (computed by the SMS validator at send), `twilio_message_sid`, `status` (queued/sent/delivered/failed/undelivered), `error_code`/`error_message`, `related_lead_id`, `cost_eur`. Indexed by client+sent_at and by Twilio SID (the status-webhook lookup). RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()` (operators see their clients' messages, a client sees its own); writes service-role only.
- **`0060_sms_templates.sql`** — Phase 7 Twilio SMS. Per-client SMS templates — `(client_id, template_key)` unique, `body`, `is_default`, `last_edited_at`/`by`. `template_key` check-constrained to the closed 4 (`lead_acknowledgment` / `job_confirmation` / `arrival_notification` / `review_request`). A `private.seed_sms_templates()` helper + an `AFTER INSERT` trigger on `clients` seed the four defaults for every new client (SECURITY DEFINER — a seed is a system event); existing clients are backfilled. The default bodies here must stay in lockstep with `DEFAULT_SMS_TEMPLATES` (`lib/sms/default-templates.ts`). RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; writes service-role only. Editor UI is deferred to the Automations feature — until then the `send_sms` job reads the seeded body straight from the row.
- **`0061_email_messages.sql`** — Phase 7 Resend. The email conversation log — one row per outbound send + per inbound reply, discriminated by `direction`. Columns: `client_id`, `sender_address` / `recipient_address` / `reply_to_address` snapshots, `subject` + `body_text` + `body_html`, `resend_message_id` (status webhook lookup), `in_reply_to_message_id` (RFC 2822 threading), `status` (queued/sent/delivered/bounced/complained/failed/received), `related_lead_id`, `thread_token`, `attachments` jsonb, `is_auto_responder`, `sent_by`. Indexed by `(related_lead_id, occurred_at)` for the conversation read, by `resend_message_id` for the delivery webhook, by `thread_token` for inbound routing debug. RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()` (operators see their clients' messages, a client sees their own); writes service-role only.
- **`0062_email_templates.sql`** — Phase 7 Resend. Per-client email templates — `(client_id, template_key)` unique. `template_key` check-constrained to the closed 5 (`lead_followup` / `review_request` / `quote_followup` / `lead_notification` / `lead_digest`). Each row carries `subject` + `body_html` + `body_text` (Resend sends both; mail clients pick). A `private.seed_email_templates()` helper + AFTER INSERT trigger on `clients` seed all five defaults per client (SECURITY DEFINER, same pattern as 0060); existing clients are backfilled. **Default bodies stay in lockstep with `DEFAULT_EMAIL_TEMPLATES`** (`lib/email/default-templates.ts`) — editing the defaults means BOTH files. Operator template editor is deferred (same precedent as SMS templates).
- **`0063_notification_preferences.sql`** — Phase 7 Resend. Per-client operator notification recipients. `(client_id, operator_email)` unique, with per-event flags (`notify_on_new_lead` / `notify_on_payment_failure` / `notify_on_review_received`, all default true) + `digest_frequency` (`immediate` / `hourly` / `daily`). Adds `leads.notification_pending_at` (timestamptz, NULL when no notification has been deferred — set by the throttle path of `send_lead_notification`, cleared by the digest worker). AFTER INSERT trigger on `leads` enqueues a `send_lead_notification` job. `pg_cron` schedule enqueues `batch_notification_digest` hourly. RLS: operators see their accessible clients' preferences; writes service-role only.
- **`0064_email_attachments_bucket.sql`** — Phase 7 Resend. Supabase Storage bucket for email attachments (outbound: operator-attached files on a reply; inbound: re-uploaded from the inbound MIME so the conversation view can display them). Private bucket; reads gated on `accessible_client_ids()` via the path's first segment (the client slug). Writes service-role only. Path convention: `{client_slug}/{direction}/{email_message_id}/{filename}`.
- **`0066_client_gbp_locations.sql`** — Phase 7 GBP. Per-client Google Business Profile location selection — one row per client (UNIQUE on `client_id`; V1 forcing function — multi-location clients need this loosened + a `primary` flag). Stores the resource-name pair `gbp_account_id` (`accounts/...`) + `gbp_location_id` (`locations/...`), plus cached `location_title` / `address` / `phone` / `website` / `review_link` (the substitution target for `{{review.link}}`), `current_rating` + `review_count` (refreshed by the daily sync), and `last_synced_at`. RLS: operators see their accessible clients' locations; writes service-role only.
- **`0067_gbp_reviews.sql`** — Phase 7 GBP. Local cache of GBP reviews — upserted by the daily `gbp_sync_reviews` job. UNIQUE on `(client_id, gbp_review_id)` so per-client upsert is trivial. Stores reviewer name + photo (may be NULL for anonymous reviews), 1-5 `rating`, comment, Google timestamps (`created_at_google` / `updated_at_google`), and operator `reply_text` + `reply_created_at` once one is published. `is_new_since_last_view` powers the operator dashboard badge — preserved across syncs (the handler's two-pass strategy never touches it for known reviews). `deleted_at_google` marks reviews removed at Google so they drop out of the visible list but stay for audit. RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; writes service-role only.
- **`0068_gbp_review_requests.sql`** — Phase 7 GBP. Audit log of review-request SMS/email sends. One row per send attempt, written by the `gbp_send_review_request` job. Channel-agnostic vocabulary (`channel` = sms|email, `status` = queued/sent/delivered/failed) — per-channel detail (segments, delivery status, Resend message id) is in `sms_messages` / `email_messages`. `resulted_in_review_id` FK is populated by the sync job's 7-day attribution window so the conversion rate is queryable. RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; writes service-role only.
- **`0069_gbp_triggers_and_cron.sql`** — Phase 7 GBP. Four pieces of plumbing: (1) `AFTER UPDATE` trigger on `bookings` that fires `gbp_send_review_request` with a **2-hour `run_after` delay** on the transition to `status='completed'` (matches the "let the customer experience the work first" UX intent). Looks up the customer's phone/email so the job has a payload to act on; skips cleanly when no contact channel exists. Same swallow-errors pattern as `0063`'s lead-notification trigger — an enqueue failure must not fail the booking update. (2) Daily `pg_cron` schedule at 06:00 UTC enqueueing one `gbp_sync_reviews` job per `client_gbp_locations` with an active GBP `integration_connections`. (3) `AFTER INSERT` trigger on `gbp_reviews` that fans an in-app `notification_kind='review'` via `private.notify_client_users` from migration `0032` (operator + client users see the new review notification immediately). (4) Adds `gbp_reviews` + `gbp_review_requests` to the `supabase_realtime` publication so `RealtimeProvider` can keep operator dashboards live.
- **`0070_client_meta_ad_accounts.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads. Per-client mapping of "which Meta ad account does Webnua manage for this client". UNIQUE on `client_id` (V1 forcing function — one ad account per client; the multi-ad-account / agency-of-agency case loosens this + adds a `primary` flag later). Stores Meta's `act_*` ad-account id + business id + cached posture (name / currency / status code / balance / amount spent / timezone) + the operator-confirmed customer-agreement audit snapshot (`customer_agreed_at` / `customer_agreed_by_email`). RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; writes service-role only.
- **`0071_meta_lead_forms.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads. Catalogue of Meta lead-form records. Unique on `meta_form_id`. Stores Page id, form name, the field structure snapshot (so the lead-sync job can map field values to display labels without extra round-trips), and `archived_at` for Meta-side soft-deleted forms (kept for late-arriving leads + audit). RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; service-role writes.
- **`0072_meta_campaigns.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads. The Meta-side record for every campaign Webnua launched (or imported). Unique on both `meta_campaign_id` AND `campaign_id` (each Meta campaign maps 1:1 to one operator-facing `public.campaigns` row). The launch orchestrator inserts both rows in lockstep so the existing `/campaigns` surfaces light up automatically; `campaign_id` CASCADE-deletes keep them aligned. New enums: `meta_campaign_status` (`active | paused | archived | in_review | with_issues`) and `meta_campaign_created_via` (`webnua_month_1 | webnua_ongoing | external`) — the month-1 / ongoing split is what the €200 ad-credit accounting reads.
- **`0073_meta_ads_insights.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads. Daily per-campaign metrics. Unique on `(meta_campaign_id, date_recorded)` so the upsert from the sync job is trivially idempotent. Stores impressions / clicks / leads (extracted from Meta's `actions` array) / spend (minor units) / CPL / CTR (basis points) + the raw `/insights` payload as jsonb for diagnostics + future-metric extraction without a re-pull. RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()`; service-role writes.
- **`0074_meta_ads_cron.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads. Two `pg_cron` schedules + realtime publication. **Daily `04:00 UTC`** enqueues one `meta_sync_insights` job per active campaign on a client with an active Meta `integration_connections`. **Every 15 minutes** enqueues one `meta_sync_leads` job per active campaign that has a wired lead form (polling rather than push because Meta's lead webhooks aren't reliable enough to depend on). Adds `meta_campaigns` + `meta_ads_insights` to the `supabase_realtime` publication so the operator `/campaigns` surface refreshes when a sync completes.
- **`0075_meta_sync_campaigns_cron.sql`** — Phase 7 Meta Ads campaign-ingest cron. Adds an **hourly** `pg_cron` schedule (`7 * * * *`) that enqueues one `meta_sync_campaigns` job per client with an active Meta `integration_connections` AND a `client_meta_ad_accounts` row. The handler (server: `meta-ads/job-handlers.ts`) calls `/act_{id}/campaigns` via `callWithToken()` and upserts both `public.campaigns` + `meta_campaigns` for every campaign on the ad account. The job is also enqueued immediately by the ad-account `select` route so a freshly-connected customer sees their campaigns within seconds; the operator can trigger it manually via the "↻ Sync campaigns" button on `/campaigns`. Closes the V1 follow-up flagged on the previous Meta migration set — campaigns built in Meta Ads Manager now flow into Webnua's `/campaigns` roster automatically.
- **`0080_automation_run_action_sequence.sql`** — Phase 8 · Session 3 follow-up.
