Adds `automation_runs.action_sequence uuid[]` (NOT NULL, default `'{}'::uuid[]`) — the per-run snapshot of `automation_actions.id` values in position order, captured at run creation. The engine walks THIS array, so mid-run reorders / inserts / removals of the underlying actions only affect future runs. `current_action_position` is treated as a 1-indexed slot into the array. Backfill: every existing in-flight run (`status in ('running', 'paused')`) is populated with its automation's current ordered action ids; terminal-status runs are left empty (never walked again). An empty `action_sequence` is the engine's explicit backwards-compat signal — fall back to a live position query — so any pre-0080 run the backfill missed still executes correctly until it finishes. See the resolved "Mid-execution action reordering" decision above for the full contract.
- **`0079_platform_email_templates.sql`** — Phase 8 · Session 3 (V1.1 polish). Single-row-per-`template_key` table for `lead_notification` + `lead_digest` — the two operator-facing notification templates. **Platform-level**: one body for all clients (operator-facing copy is branded for the Webnua operator, not the customer's business — same body fires regardless of which client triggered it). The previous per-client rows in `email_templates` for these two keys are now legacy fallbacks. RLS: operator-only SELECT + UPDATE (the `users.role = 'admin'` check); INSERT/DELETE are service-role only — rows are seeded once and edited, never created or deleted from the app. Seeded with the same defaults as `DEFAULT_EMAIL_TEMPLATES` (which stays the code-level runtime fallback). The `send_lead_notification` + `batch_notification_digest` job handlers' `loadTemplate` reads platform-level FIRST for these keys, falling back to per-client `email_templates`, falling back to `DEFAULT_EMAIL_TEMPLATES`. Edited via the new operator-only `/settings/platform-templates` tab.
- **`0081_client_custom_domains.sql`** — Phase 9 custom-domain attachment. New `client_custom_domains` table — one row per attached domain, multi-domain per client. Status enum (`pending_dns | verifying | ssl_pending | live | failed | removed`); `is_primary` per client (partial-unique-index enforced); `dns_records_required` jsonb (A/CNAME + Vercel verification rows). RLS: operators read all accessible-client rows; clients read/insert/update on their own client's rows. DELETE is revoked from `authenticated` — the app uses a soft delete (`status='removed'` + `removed_at`). A `BEFORE INSERT` trigger stamps `added_by = auth.uid()` when omitted (attribution for audit). The legacy `websites.domain_primary` / `domain_aliases` stay populated for the pre-Phase-9 single-domain flow on `/website`; the public-site resolver reads both sources.
- **`0082_custom_domains_cron.sql`** — Phase 9 custom-domain attachment. Every-5-minutes `pg_cron` schedule enqueueing one `check_domain_verification` job per tick (the handler reads in-flight rows in one batched scan, batch size from `DOMAIN_CHECK_BATCH_SIZE`, default 50). Vercel's per-account rate limit is ~100 req/min and each row makes 2 calls (getDomain + getDomainConfig), so a 50-row batch sits well under the ceiling. Adds `client_custom_domains` to the `supabase_realtime` publication so client + operator UIs refresh when a status moves.
- **`0089_invite_tokens_and_accept.sql`** — Pattern B operator-invite session. Adds `token text unique not null` + `consumed_at timestamptz` to both `team_invites` + `client_user_invites` so the real magic-link accept flow has the columns it needs. Backfills any pre-existing rows with a random token + flips their status to `expired` (the previous fabricated `magic_link` strings never resolved to anything). Adds a daily `pg_cron` sweep at 02:00 UTC that flips pending invites past `expires_at` to `expired` — the UI uses the status flip to surface the "Expired · Resend" affordance correctly. RLS unchanged (operator-only for `team_invites`; operator-or-own-client for `client_user_invites`; the public accept route bypasses both via service-role). See the "Pattern B operator invite flow" parked-decision entry for the full architecture.
- **`0083_automation_suppression.sql`** — Phase 8 · Session 4 suppression layer. Adds `clients.quiet_hours_{start,end,timezone}` (nullable start/end = no quiet hours; timezone defaults `'UTC'`). Creates `automation_suppression_log` (one row per suppression decision: `(client_id, automation_id, automation_run_id, action_id, lead_id, channel, reason, deferred_until, context, suppressed_at)`) + the `automation_suppression_reason` enum (`frequency_cap_hourly` / `frequency_cap_daily` / `quiet_hours` / `priority_cancelled`). Indexed `(client_id, suppressed_at desc)` for per-client audit reads + `(automation_run_id)` for per-run trace + a partial index on `lead_id`. RLS: SELECT for `accessible_client_ids()` (operators + own-client users see their own audit); writes service-role only — the engine writes every row. Closes the long-deferred "Automation overlap / anti-spam suppression rules" parked decision.
- **`0090_lifecycle_status_cancelled_deleted.sql`** — Pattern B onboarding wizard · Session C. Adds `'cancelled'` and `'deleted'` to the `client_lifecycle` enum — the two new stages of the two-stage cancellation lifecycle. **Lands standalone** because Postgres requires `ALTER TYPE ... ADD VALUE` to commit before any other statement references the new value (migration 0091's cron references both).
- **`0091_onboarding_wizard_and_cancellation.sql`** — Pattern B onboarding wizard · Session C. Adds five columns to `clients`: `wizard_state` (jsonb, in-progress wizard data), `wizard_completed_at` (timestamptz, drives the dashboard redirect gate), `cancelled_at`, `data_deletion_scheduled_at` (= cancelled_at + 30 days, the cron's anchor), `hard_delete_warning_sent_at` (prevents double sends of the day-83 email). Creates the daily `webnua_cancellation_lifecycle` pg_cron (05:00 UTC) that runs three stages in one tick: day 30 = `cancelled` → `deleted`; day 83 = enqueue `send_cancellation_warning_email`; day 90 = hard DELETE via cascade FKs (with an `integration_call_log` audit row written first). RLS unchanged — the existing `clients_update` widening from 0087 covers the wizard's client-side writes; the cancellation timestamps are written exclusively via service-role from the Stripe webhook + the `/api/clients/[id]/cancel` route.
- **`0092_brand_design_bundle_and_palette.sql`** — Bundle C2b-1. Two nullable columns on `public.brands`: `design_bundle_id text` (one of the 4 closed-set bundle keys `sharp_direct` / `warm_established` / `clean_premium` / `bold_direct`; NULL = inherit from `industry-bundle-defaults.ts`; no CHECK constraint so a 5th bundle can land without a migration) and `derived_palette jsonb` (the resolved 8-stop palette the bundle + brand colours produce). Backfill-safe (NULL = legacy behaviour). Foundation for Bundle C2b-2's variant-narrowing pass.
- **`0093_variant_reassigned_fallback_reason.sql`** — Bundle C2b-2. Extends the `generation_fallback_reason` enum with `'variant-reassigned'` so the new bundle-aware variant-assignment pass (`assignBundleVariants` in `lib/website/generation-validation.ts`) can log when a section's variant key (e.g. `hero.layout`) is narrowed to a bundle-allowable subset. Distinct from `'invalid'` (AI emitted out-of-catalog) — here the AI picked a CATALOG-valid value and bundle policy steered it elsewhere. Pure-additive `ALTER TYPE`.
- **`0095_conversational_onboarding.sql`** — Session B. Replaces the wizard `/sign-up` with a chat surface; the wizard moves to `/sign-up/legacy`. Adds `clients.conversation_state jsonb` (sibling of `wizard_state`, NOT an extension — both columns coexist during the 30-day legacy keep-alive; shape `{ messages, capturedFacts, current_turn, verified }`) + a new `email_verification_codes` table for the 6-digit verification flow (10-min lifetime, SHA-256 hashed with email-as-salt). Magic-link infrastructure stays wired for password reset + operator invites + client teammate invites. App-code enforces the policy (5 attempts before 15-min lockout, 3 codes per email per hour).
- **`0096_brand_offer.sql`** — Session C.5. Promotes the four-field offer (`headline` / `promise` / `risk_reversal` / `cta_text`) from `funnels.funnel_offer` to a new `brands.offer jsonb` column so the offer becomes a single source of truth that flows to the website hero CTA, the dedicated offer section, AND the funnel hero. `funnel_offer` remains as a per-funnel override for the V1.1 multi-funnel case. Same snake_case key shape so the backfill is a direct copy; new clients write to `brands.offer` directly.
- **`0097_plain_text_customer_emails.sql`** — Two concerns: (1) customer-facing emails (`lead_acknowledgment_email`, `review_request_email`) ship plain-text only with the "Powered by Webnua" footer appended at send time in `src/lib/integrations/resend/job-handlers.ts` — strips `body_html` from the seeded rows so the stored shape matches the sending shape; (2) aligns the platform-level `lead_digest` row with the better `DEFAULT_EMAIL_TEMPLATES.lead_digest` TS body (adds the `{{digest.summary}}` line the 0079 seed missed).
- **`0098_operator_email_branded_chrome.sql`** — Rebrands the two platform operator emails (`lead_notification`, `lead_digest`) with the standard Webnua HTML chrome (paper bg, white card, rust eyebrow, mono footer) and a real card-list for digest summaries. Keeps the live `platform_email_templates` rows in lockstep with the in-code `lib/email/default-templates.ts` so the rebrand fires immediately without a redeploy gap on the platform-template resolver path.
- **`0099_email_logo_footer.sql`** — Swaps the brand footer on `lead_notification` + `lead_digest` rows from text-only "© Webnua · Perth" to the logo-image footer (`/webnua-logo.png` on `public/`) matching the rest of the operator-email family. All operator-facing emails share `EMAIL_BRAND_FOOTER` (`src/lib/email/footer.ts`); this brings the seeded DB rows in lockstep. **Operational note:** the logo PNGs were uploaded to the working branch (`dd8b5f8` apple-icon.png, `126232c` webnua-logo.png) — if the merge to main hasn't landed at deploy time, every branded email shows a broken image fallback.
- **`0101_delete_hardcoded_seed_clients.sql`** — Operator follow-up to 0100. The 4 hardcoded seed clients preserved by 0100 are TS-level reference data only (file-level constants in `lib/website/data-stub.tsx` + `lib/funnel/data-stub.tsx` + the `voltlinePassthrough` fallback in `generation-stub.ts`); no code path queries them by UUID at runtime, so the DB rows were operator-facing noise with no functional value. Same constraint-topology dance as 0100 (drop `users_client_id_fkey` + bypass `users_guard_identity_columns` for the transaction, then restore both); self-asserts `clients_remaining = 0`. Drops the 4 clients + the 3 seeded client users (mark@voltline, liam@voltline, anna@freshhome) from `public.users` + `auth.users`. Operator users (`role='admin'`, `client_id IS NULL`) untouched. `supabase/seed.sql:31-88` is deliberately NOT modified — a future fresh project setup via `supabase db reset` can still re-seed for platform reference work.
- **`0100_prelaunch_test_data_cleanup.sql`** — Pre-launch readiness session (2026-05-26). Operator-approved one-shot cleanup. Deletes every `clients` row EXCEPT the 4 hardcoded seeds (Voltline / FreshHome / KeyHero / NeatWorks UUIDs `c0000000-…-0001..0004`) plus their attached `public.users` + `auth.users`. **Superseded a few minutes later by 0101**, which removed the 4 preserved seeds too — kept here as the migration history of the cleanup-in-stages. Three constraint-topology steps inside one transaction: (1) `disable trigger users_guard_identity_columns` (0045's privilege-escalation guard, correct to bypass in a service-role migration); (2) `drop constraint users_client_id_fkey` (the RESTRICT FK that would block client deletion while client-role users still reference them); (3) `delete from public.clients` (cascades through ~40 child tables, clearing the 11 RESTRICT FKs INTO users on the way); (4) `delete from public.users` then `delete from auth.users` for the doomed user ids; (5) re-add the FK with identical semantics + re-enable the trigger. Self-asserts `clients_remaining = 4` and rolls back if any other count emerges. Reduces 59 clients → 4. Test/playground signups + Webnua-suffixed dupes + Pattern-B race residue + one off-mission gmail signup all removed. **Known gap:** Vault secrets referenced by `integration_connections.token_secret_id` on the doomed rows are NOT garbage-collected — the connection rows go but the Vault entries leak. Acceptable for V1 (production had zero connected integrations on the doomed rows). Subsequent migrations adding token-cleanup logic can sweep these via a `vault.secrets` audit query.

### Duplicate-numbered migration filenames

Two migration prefixes were inadvertently reused. Postgres' migration ordering is alphabetical-by-full-filename, so behaviour is stable today, but the duplicate numbering is a foot-gun if a future migration assumes monotonic numbering. Rename to `0079a_` / `0079b_` / `0089a_` / `0089b_` in a future housekeeping pass.

- **`0079_automation_inline_bodies.sql`** — Phase 8 Session 2. Moves SMS + email message bodies (and email subjects) from the per-client `sms_templates` / `email_templates` tables into `automation_actions.action_config`, so each comm action carries its own body. Three-pass migration (backfill → make `template_key` nullable → switch the runtime resolver to action_config first, table second). Closes the architectural decision from the Session 2 plan: "Templates live with the automation action that uses them" — no separate templates table the action references by key. The legacy tables stay in place as fallback.
- **`0079_platform_email_templates.sql`** — Phase 8 Session 3 (already documented above under its own entry). The second `0079` filename — applied after `0079_automation_inline_bodies` due to alphabetical ordering. Adds the operator-facing platform-level templates surface.
- **`0089_invite_tokens_and_accept.sql`** — Pattern B operator-invite session (already documented above under its own entry). Adds magic-link `token` + `consumed_at` columns to `team_invites` + `client_user_invites`.
- **`0089_websites_insert_update_for_owners.sql`** — Pattern B critical fixes Session 2 hotfix. Widens `websites_insert` + `websites_update` RLS from operator-only (`private.is_operator()`) to: a user with the `editPages` capability who belongs to the target client may insert + update the websites row. Same widening pattern as `0087` (`clients_update`) + `0088` (`funnels_update` / `brands_update`). Unblocks the sub-account `ScaffoldWebsiteButton` for client-role owners. `editPages` is in `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS` and matches the cap the UI gates the button on.

---

### `lib/domains/` — custom-domain attachment (Phase 9)

> Self-serve + operator-concierge custom domain attachment. Replaces the legacy single-domain `domain_primary` flow on `websites` (kept for back-compat); the new path is multi-domain per client, status-tracked, with a 5-minute polling job. Built on the Phase 7 integration spine — every Vercel call routes through `callExternal()`, the poller runs on `integration_jobs`. The `client_custom_domains` table is the row of record; UI reads via `lib/domains/queries.tsx`, writes go through `/api/domains/*` routes.

- **`types.ts`** — `CustomDomainStatus` (the six lifecycle values), `CustomDomainRow` (table shape), `DnsRecordRequirement`, `STATUS_LABEL` / `STATUS_DESCRIPTION` maps, `IN_FLIGHT_STATUSES` (`pending_dns | verifying | ssl_pending` — the poller's scan set).
- **`validation.ts`** — pure. `validateDomain(input)` → `{ valid, normalized, errors }`. Strips protocol / path / port / surrounding dots, lowercases, validates FQDN syntax (≥ 2 labels, ASCII letters/digits/hyphen, TLD ≥ 2 chars). Rejects Webnua-owned domains (`webnua.com` / `webnua.dev` / `webnua.app` and any subdomain) + bare public suffixes (`com`, `ie`, `co.uk`). `isApexDomain(domain)` is exported for the DNS-record builder. NOT a full PSL parse — a curated short list covers the common cases; add entries as real customers collide.
- **`manager.ts`** — SERVER-ONLY. The single business-logic entry point for every domain mutation. `attachDomain(clientId, domain, userId)` validates → uniqueness-check (a domain in any non-removed state on ANY client blocks a fresh add) → `vercel.addDomain` → persists the row. Returns a discriminated `AttachOutcome` (`ok | invalid_domain | already_attached | vercel_error | not_configured`) — the `not_configured` branch still creates the row (operator finishes in the Vercel dashboard). `checkDomainStatus(domainId)` reconciles one row against `vercel.getDomain` + `vercel.getDomainConfig` in parallel; `deriveStatus({ verified, misconfigured, previousStatus })` is the pure transition function. `removeDomain(domainId)` calls `vercel.removeDomain` then soft-deletes the row — refuses to remove the only-primary domain (caller must demote or add another first). `setPrimaryDomain(domainId)` demotes siblings then promotes. `listInFlightDomains(batchSize)` is the poller's read.
- **`queries.tsx`** — `'use client'`. RLS-scoped browser reads + POST mutations to the routes: `useClientDomains(clientId)`, `useAllDomains()` (operator cross-client roster), `useDomain(id)`; `useAttachDomain`, `useCheckDomain`, `useSetPrimaryDomain`, `useRemoveDomain`. Same `PGRST205`-tolerant pattern as the per-tenant integration hooks (treat missing-table as empty list so a deploy that has not applied migrations still renders the empty state).
- **`job-handlers.ts`** — registers `check_domain_verification` with the integration_jobs spine. Handler reads `listInFlightDomains` (batch from `DOMAIN_CHECK_BATCH_SIZE`), processes each row sequentially through `checkDomainStatus` (errors per-row are swallowed + logged so one bad row doesn't take down the batch), and on a `→ live` transition enqueues a `send_email` job with template key `domain_live_notification`. Registered via the `job-handler-manifest.ts` side-effect import.

### `lib/integrations/vercel/domains.ts` — typed Vercel domains adapter

> Phase 9. Sibling of the legacy `lib/website/vercel.ts` (which stays in place for the `ConnectDomainButton` single-domain flow). Five typed wrappers — `addDomain` / `getDomain` / `getDomainConfig` / `verifyDomain` / `removeDomain` — every call through `callExternal()`. Shapes live in `domains-types.ts`. SERVER-ONLY.

- **`addDomain(domain, clientId?)`** — POST `/v10/projects/{id}/domains`. Idempotent on 409 (re-fetches and returns the live record).
- **`getDomain(domain, clientId?)`** — GET `/v9/projects/{id}/domains/{domain}`. Returns null on 404 (the domain is not attached, distinct from a Vercel error).
- **`getDomainConfig(domain, clientId?)`** — GET `/v6/domains/{name}/config`. Vercel's DNS-side view (`misconfigured: true/false`) — independent of the per-project verification state.
- **`verifyDomain(domain, clientId?)`** — POST `/v9/projects/{id}/domains/{domain}/verify`. Re-trigger verification.
- **`removeDomain(domain, clientId?)`** — DELETE `/v9/projects/{id}/domains/{domain}`. 404 = already gone = success.
- **`classifyVercelError`** maps Vercel error codes onto the typed union (`domain_already_in_use | invalid_domain | forbidden | not_configured | rate_limited | unknown`).

### `app/api/domains/*` — Phase 9 routes

> The route handlers backing the UI. Auth is `requireClientAccess`-shaped via `_auth.ts` — operator on an accessible client OR a client-role user on their own client. The legacy `POST/DELETE /api/domains` with `{ domain }` only is preserved (operator-only direct Vercel call backing `ConnectDomainButton`).

- **`/api/domains` POST** — discriminated on body shape: `{ client_id, domain }` → Phase 9 `attachDomain`; `{ domain }` only → legacy direct Vercel call.
- **`/api/domains` GET** — `?client_id=...` returns active (non-removed) domains for one client. RLS-scoped via the auth check.
- **`/api/domains` DELETE** — legacy direct Vercel delete by domain string (operator-only); new soft-delete-by-id lives at `/api/domains/[id]`.
- **`/api/domains/[id]` GET / DELETE** — single domain row; DELETE is the soft-delete (rejects the only-primary case with 409 `cannot-remove-only-primary`).
- **`/api/domains/[id]/check` POST** — manually re-run the verification check + return the updated row.
- **`/api/domains/[id]/set-primary` POST** — promote one domain to primary, demote siblings.

### `components/shared/settings/{CustomDomainSection,AddDomainForm,DnsRecordsTable,DomainStatusCard}` + `components/admin/domains/AllDomainsTable`

> The UI primitives. `CustomDomainSection` is reused by both client + operator-sub-account surfaces (same shape — operator-vs-client divergence is the API authorisation, not the chrome). `DomainStatusCard` auto-refreshes every 30s while in-flight via `useCheckDomain`. `AllDomainsTable` is the operator cross-client roster — status + client filters, "Stuck" badge for in-flight > 24h, drill-in to the active client's sub-account view.

### `app/settings/domains/` — settings tab

> 2-way role dispatcher (`page.tsx`). Operator `_admin-content` dispatches a second time on workspace mode: agency mode → `AllDomainsTable` cross-client roster, sub-account → `_sub-account-content` (the same `CustomDomainSection` the client sees, scoped to the active client). Client `_client-content` renders the client's own domain management.

### Middleware — Phase 9 redirect

> `src/middleware.ts` extended: a request landing on `{slug}.webnua.dev` looks up the client's primary live custom domain (60s in-memory cache; PostgREST direct call, the edge runtime can't import the service-role client). If a primary is set AND differs from the current host, the middleware 301-redirects (SEO consolidation on the canonical host). Lookup failures fall through to the existing rewrite — a Supabase outage never breaks the visitor flow. `lib/public-site/resolve.ts` was extended to look up the new `client_custom_domains` table first (status=live), then fall back to the legacy `websites.domain_primary` / `domain_aliases` columns.

---

## Remaining build phases

> The roadmap to a finished platform. The frontend + the wired-data backend
> (Phases 1–6 / Clusters 1–9 + the form builder) are done. What is left:

- **Phase 7 — Integrations.** OAuth + API for GBP, Meta Ads, GA4, Google Ads
  (business) and Stripe, Resend, Twilio (platform). Makes the
  `/settings/integrations` connect flows real; unlocks review auto-pull,
  campaign metrics, email/SMS sending, real billing.
  **Session 1 (platform integration spine) — DONE.** The shared foundation is
  built: `lib/env.ts` (typed/boot-validated env), `callExternal()`, the
  retry helper, the `integration_jobs` queue + `pg_cron` poller + executor
  route, `integration_call_log`, the three client-assignment tables, and
  `notifications_outbound` (migrations `0047`–`0053`).
  **Session 2 (per-tenant OAuth foundation) — DONE.** Supabase Vault
  (token encryption), the `integration_connections` table, the OAuth provider
  registry (GBP fully implemented; Meta written but unverified — `TODO(meta)`),
  the connect / callback / disconnect routes, `callWithToken()`, the daily
  token-refresh job, and the operator connections UI (migrations `0054`–`0056`).
  See `reference/integration-foundation-audit.md`.
  **Stripe billing — DONE.** Subscription billing for clients: €299/month via
  Stripe Checkout, the webhook → `client_stripe_customers` sync, the
  payment-failed operator alert (on the jobs queue), and the operator billing
  UI on sub-account `/settings/billing`. See the "Stripe billing" inventory +
  the "Stripe billing — operator setup" steps above; migration `0057`.
  **Twilio SMS — DONE.** One-way alphanumeric SMS sending: the Twilio client
  wrapper, the SMS character validator + template renderer + cost estimator,
  the per-client sender registration + template editor UI on sub-account
  `/settings/sms`, the `send_sms` job handler, the status-callback webhook, and
  the lead-acknowledgment auto-trigger on the public form-submit flow. See the
  "Twilio SMS" inventory + the "Twilio SMS — operator setup" steps above;
  migrations `0058`–`0060`.
  **Resend email — DONE.** Two-way email integration with inbound reply
  routing: the Resend wrapper, HMAC-signed plus-addressed thread tokens
  (`{clientSlug}+lead-{token}@mail.webnua.com`), per-client sender slug
  + display name provisioning UI, the five seeded templates (`lead_followup`
  / `review_request` / `quote_followup` / `lead_notification` /
  `lead_digest`), the inbound webhook (signature-verified, cross-tenant-
  guarded, auto-responder-detecting, attachment-reuploading), the delivery
  webhook (status reconciliation by Resend message id), the operator-side
  reply flow from inside the lead inbox, and operator notification
  preferences with per-client recipients, per-event flags, and an
  immediate/hourly/daily digest model. The lead-followup customer email is
  enqueued from the public form-submit route when an email is captured;
  the operator new-lead notification fans automatically via the migration
  0063 trigger. See the "Resend email" inventory + the "Resend email —
  operator setup" steps above; migrations `0061`–`0064`. The remaining
  per-provider business logic — GBP review pull, Meta campaign metrics —
  follows.
  **Google Business Profile — DONE.** Per-tenant GBP integration end-to-end:
  the API client (`listAccounts` / `listLocations` / `getLocation` /
  `listReviews` / `replyToReview` through `callWithToken`), the
  post-OAuth location-picker modal (auto-opened from
  `/settings/integrations`), the daily review-pull cron with seen-state
  preserved across syncs, the booking-completion trigger that auto-fires
  a review request 2 hours later through SMS (preferred) or email
  (fallback), and the operator + client dashboard widgets. **UI
  consolidation (PR #100):** every GBP affordance lives on Webnua's
  established surfaces — reviews + inline reply on `/reviews` (both
  contexts), review-request audit on the lead timeline, manual "Send
  review request" on lead + booking detail, connection management on
  `/settings/integrations` with a GBP-only footer for location summary
  + Sync / Change. No dedicated GBP tab. SMS/email `{{review.link}}`
  substitution resolved via `getReviewLinkForClient`. GBP Posts +
  insights deferred to V1.1. See the "Google Business Profile (Phase 7)"
  inventory + "Google Business Profile — operator setup" steps;
  migrations `0066`–`0069`.
  **Meta Ads — DONE (FINAL Phase 7 session).** Per-tenant Meta Ads
  integration: the API client (`listAdAccounts` / `listPages` /
  `listCampaignsForAdAccount` / `listAdsForCampaign` / `getLeadForm` /
  `pause`+`activate` / `getCampaign` / `getCampaignInsights` /
  `getLeads`, all through `callWithToken` — the `create*` family is
  exported but un-called, kept for a future in-app launch path if one
  ever ships), the post-OAuth ad-account
  picker + customer-agreement capture (`MetaAdAccountPickerModal`),
  the **Open Meta Ads Manager →** deep-link button +
  **↻ Sync campaigns** trigger (`LaunchMetaCampaignButton`), the
  hourly `meta_sync_campaigns` ingest cron (minute 7 of every hour,
  migration `0075`) + daily insights cron + quarter-hour leads cron,
  and `lib/campaigns/queries.tsx` joined to `meta_campaigns` +
  `meta_ads_insights` so the previously-`—` per-row metrics and the
  4-week trend chart render real numbers. **V1 model**: Webnua does
  NOT build campaigns in-app — the customer's OAuth grant gives
  Webnua business-manager access, and the operator manages campaigns
  directly in Meta Ads Manager. The `meta_sync_campaigns` job pulls
  Ads-Manager-launched campaigns BACK into Webnua so they surface on
  `/campaigns` (auto-fires post-pick, hourly thereafter, manual
  trigger via the "↻ Sync campaigns" button). The in-app launch
  wizard + 9 trade templates + 5-step orchestrator were removed in a
  follow-up once that V1 model settled. **Lead-form discovery is
  wired** — the campaign-ingest handler walks `/{campaign_id}/ads` →
  each ad's `creative.form_id` (or the legacy
  `creative.object_story_spec.link_data.lead_gen_form_id`), fetches
  the form's detail (name / page id / question array), upserts into
  `meta_lead_forms`, and patches `meta_campaigns.meta_lead_form_id`.
  Once linked, `meta_sync_leads` (every 15 min) picks up the campaign
  on its next tick — the INNER JOIN on `meta_lead_form_id` matches.
  Skipped on subsequent syncs (campaigns rarely switch forms; the
  manual sync button re-runs the whole walk if needed). The **€200
  month-1 ad-credit funding transfer is a manual operator process**
  (V2 to automate via Meta's funding APIs). See the "Meta Ads (Phase 7
  — FINAL Phase 7 session)" inventory + "Meta Ads — operator setup"
  steps; migrations `0070`–`0075`. **Phase 7 — DONE.**
- **Phase 8 — Automation execution engine — DONE.** The engine + DB triggers
  + cron + dispatch (Sessions 1–2) shipped earlier; the action editor
  (Session 3) shipped; the in-flight run isolation via `action_sequence`
  snapshot (migration 0080) shipped; Session 4 closes the long-deferred
  suppression layer + the `LeadAutomationPanel` "View all runs" carve-out.
  **Session 4 deliverables:**
  • **Suppression layer** (`lib/automations/suppression.ts`, migration
    `0083`) — three dimensions evaluated before every comm action:
    frequency cap (1/channel/hr, 3/channel/24h, read against
    `sms_messages` / `email_messages`); quiet hours (per-client window on
    `clients.quiet_hours_*`; deferred to end-of-window, not dropped);
    priority cancellation (hardcoded by trigger type — transactional >
    nurture > reputation; new higher-priority runs cancel lower-priority
    running runs on the same lead). Every decision logs to
    `automation_suppression_log` for audit.
  • **Per-client quiet-hours UI** — `QuietHoursSection` mounted on
    sub-account `/settings/notifications` (operator-only) with start /
    end / IANA timezone picker (curated 9-entry shortlist).
  • **LeadAutomationPanel run history** — `GET /api/leads/[id]/runs`
    returns full run history; the panel's new collapsible "VIEW ALL RUNS"
    block fetches lazily on expand. Closes the Session 3 carve-out.
  • **NOT building `messaging_events`** — `sms_messages` + `email_messages`
    already log every send with `related_lead_id`; a separate normalised
    log would duplicate. Campaign metrics (Phase 7 Meta Ads) closed
    differently via `meta_ads_insights`.
- **Phase 9 — Realtime + notification writes — DONE.**
  Notification write path: `AFTER INSERT` triggers fan notifications to a
  client's users on new leads / one-off bookings / reviews / operator ticket
  replies (migration `0032`, all `SECURITY DEFINER`). Realtime:
  `notifications` / `tickets` / `ticket_messages` are in the
  `supabase_realtime` publication (migration `0032`) and `RealtimeProvider`
  invalidates query keys on `postgres_changes`. **Builder approval Realtime
  is wired (B1 → A3)** — B1 first added `website_approval_submissions` to the
  publication with targeted query-key invalidations; A3 unified all four
  builder tables (`website_approval_submissions` / `funnel_approval_submissions`
  / `website_versions` / `funnel_versions`, migration `0046`) under one
  `BUILDER_EVENT` fan, so the approval queue + the submitter's editor lock +
  the version surfaces react across tabs and users.
- **Phase 9b — Client context routing fix — DONE.** Every shared route follows
  the canonical `_admin-content/_sub-account-content/_client-content` pattern
  documented at `reference/client-context-pattern.md`. Sessions 1–3 brought
  `/tickets`, `/leads`, `/calendar`, `/search`, `/automations`, `/reviews`,
  `/campaigns`, and `/(admin)/websites` into line.
- **Phase 9 · Custom domains — IN PROGRESS.** Self-serve + operator-concierge
  custom domain attachment via the Vercel Domains API. New
  `client_custom_domains` table (migration `0081`), status lifecycle
  (`pending_dns | verifying | ssl_pending | live | failed | removed`),
  every-5-min polling job (cron `0082`), per-client UI on `/settings/domains`
  (client + operator sub-account modes), cross-client operator roster
  (`AllDomainsTable` on agency-mode `/settings/domains`), middleware-level
  301 redirect from `{slug}.webnua.dev` to the client's primary live domain.
  Env: `NEXT_PUBLIC_WEBNUA_CONCIERGE_CALENDAR_URL` (surfaced as a "Book a
  setup call" link in the DNS-pending UI), `WEBNUA_CONCIERGE_CALENDAR_URL`
  (server-only mirror), `DOMAIN_CHECK_BATCH_SIZE` (poller batch, default 50).
  End-to-end verification against the live Vercel API is the follow-up step
  (test domain under operator credentials).
- **Phase 10 — Production hardening.** Domain management (V2), deploy config,
  env/secrets, error monitoring, security review + Supabase advisors, live
  browser E2E.
- **Phase 11 — Proof Page prospecting tool.** The deferred admin feature
  (audit → proof-page → outreach) — see the section below. Build last.

**Additional gaps found in the May 2026 audit (not in the original 7–11 list):**
- **Public site rendering.** Generated websites / funnels / lead-capture forms
  have no public render or hosting pipeline — the editor builds them, nothing
  serves them. Its own workstream; Phase 10's domain management implies it but
  does not cover rendering.
- **Editor publish/approval layer — DONE (PR #41 / merge `534de96`).**
  `publish-stub.ts` + `draft-stub.ts` are deleted; the layer is
  Supabase-backed via `lib/website/queries.tsx` + `mutations.ts` +
  `content-drafts.ts` + `snapshot.ts` + `builder-events.ts` against
  `website_versions` / `website_approval_submissions` /
  `force_publish_audit_log` / `content_drafts`. `audit-stub.ts` and
  `website-approval-stub.ts` collapsed to type-only display modules.
  Hook surface (`use-autosave`, `use-publish-state`) preserved.
- **Funnel publish / preflight unbuilt** — see the parked decision.

## Deferred / out of scope until end

The admin **Proof Page / prospecting tool** (the audit → proof-page → outreach
pipeline, sourced from `reference/webnua-proof-page-tool.html` and
`reference/webnua-finding-library.json`) is a real platform feature **but is
deferred until the full platform — front and back end — is working.**

Until then:
- **Do not** scaffold routes, components, lib/types, or data for it.
- **Do not** add it to nav, sidebar, or any role's settings.
- **Do not** treat the prototype HTML or the finding-library JSON as current spec.
- The files stay in `/reference` — they are the spec for the future build, not for now.

If a session has a reason to touch this area, stop and confirm with the user
first.

## Open decisions / parked

> Things deliberately not decided yet. Don't silently resolve these — flag them.

- **PARKED — Conversational onboarding is the V1 primary signup path.** Wizard `/sign-up` survives as `/sign-up/legacy` fallback for 30+ days post-launch. Delete legacy in V1.1 if conversational is reliable. Magic links remain in use for password reset and operator invites.
- **PARKED — Conversation state schema and column.** Conversational onboarding uses a sibling `clients.conversation_state jsonb` column. **NOT** an extension of `wizard_state`. Reasons: clean separation during the 30-day legacy keep-alive, independent schema evolution, trivial to delete legacy when ready. Schema shape: `{ messages, capturedFacts, current_turn, verified }`. `capturedFacts` accumulates as the conversation progresses; `messages` is append-only history. Both columns coexist for 30 days. Migration ships in Session B.
- **PARKED — Code verification policy (conversational onboarding).** 6-digit codes via Resend. 10-minute code lifetime. One active code per email at a time (new request invalidates the prior). 5 attempts per code before a 15-minute lockout. 3 codes per email per hour. Storage: hashed (SHA-256 + email salt), never plaintext. Failure modes: expired → request new; locked-out → 15-min wait; max-codes-reached → 1-hour wait. Rate-limit budget separate from `signup_attempt` (per-email, not per-IP — register `verification_code_request` + `verification_code_attempt` in `RATE_LIMITS`). If Resend fails after a 30s wait, silent fallback to magic link with a visible UX message. Magic-link infrastructure preserved for password reset + operator invites + client teammate invites.
- **PARKED — Brand-level offer migration.** `brands.offer_headline` + `brands.offer_body` (or `brands.offer jsonb`) becomes the single source of truth. Read order: `brand.offer ?? funnel.funnel_offer ?? null`. Propagation to: hero CTA, dedicated offer section, funnel hero. Edit surface: `/settings/brand`. Backfill: `brand.offer = funnel.funnel_offer` where only the funnel has one. Migration ships in **Session C.5** (between Session B and Session C), to keep Session C from bloating past its line target.
- **PARKED — `/sign-up/legacy` retention conditions.** Conditions for retiring `/sign-up/legacy` (**all** must be met): (1) 30 days minimum since conversational launch; (2) conversational completion rate within 10 percentage points of legacy; (3) conversational code-verification success rate ≥ 95%; (4) no critical bugs unfixed for > 7 days on conversational; (5) drop-off rate at any single turn ≤ 25%. If any condition fails, keep legacy alive longer and investigate before deletion.
- **PARKED — Magic-link backward compatibility.** Magic links remain wired for: password reset, operator invite, client teammate invite. Conversational signup uses 6-digit codes. `provisionPendingSignup` still generates a magic link (unused by conversational, harmless overhead) for backward compat with `/sign-up/legacy` — do NOT refactor it out during Session B; ignore the return value in the conversational caller instead. Cleaner than two divergent provision paths.
- **PARKED — Offer becomes brand-level field.** `offer_headline` + `offer_body` columns on `brands` row. Customer edits in `/settings/brand` propagate to hero CTA, dedicated offer section, funnel hero. Single source of truth replaces section-level offer storage. Migration ships with conversational onboarding work. *(See "Brand-level offer migration" above for the full design + Session C.5 split.)*
- **PARKED — Code verification for conversational onboarding.** 6-digit codes via Resend, 10-minute lifetime, one active per email, 5 attempts before 15-minute lockout, 3 codes per email per hour. Replaces magic-link for in-chat verification. Magic link infrastructure preserved for password reset + operator invites. *(See "Code verification policy" above for the expanded policy including hashed storage + fallback behaviour.)*
- **PARKED — Scraper for existing tradie sites.** V1.1 work. "Paste your existing site URL, we'll extract services + about + testimonials + contact + brand colors." Launch motion: "We just made rebuilding your existing site automatic."

- **Pattern B onboarding wizard — RESOLVED (Session C; Phase 2 concierge-parity follow-up).** 7-step wizard at `/onboarding` (industry / business / target / brand / testimonials / integrations / done) replaces the previous "click Scaffold on /website" first-build path. Step 4 (brand) is the trigger point for background website + funnel generation, so the customer's site is ready by step 7. Persists state to `clients.wizard_state` (jsonb, migration 0091); resumes pick up at `current_step`. Skip is allowed on every step except 1 (industry — required). See the `lib/onboarding/` + `app/onboarding/` inventory section. **Funnel brief fields are DERIVED, not asked separately** (per the locked plan answer): `funnel.service ← step1.services[0]`, `funnel.customerPain ← step3.targetCustomer framed via the industry urgency mode`, `funnel.guarantee ← step3.usp OR template.objectionHandlers[0].response`. The decision to add an explicit step 3b for these was rejected in favour of derivation — keeps the wizard at 7 steps + the customer doesn't repeat themselves. **Industry primary colour defaults live in a separate wizard-only map** (`INDUSTRY_PRIMARY_COLORS` in `lib/onboarding/industry-colors.ts`), NOT on the industry templates. The customer overrides via step 4's colour picker, so it's a seed only — keeping it off `industry-templates.ts` avoids ~150 lines of edits for a value most customers tune. **Trigger to revisit**: if a future surface needs a per-industry default colour outside the wizard (e.g. the AI generator picking a palette automatically), promote the map onto `IndustryTemplate.defaultPrimaryColor` and remove the wizard's standalone module. **Phase 2 concierge-parity follow-up (`claude/concierge-parity-audit` branch)** closed five wizard↔concierge divergences: (1) **Voice axes now persist on Step 4** — the brand UPDATE writes `voice_formality / voice_urgency / voice_technicality` from the tone preset (previously the preset was captured in `wizard_state` but the brand row stayed at signup's 3/3/3 neutral seed regardless of pick). Both Step 4 and `derive-brief.ts` read `toneToVoice` / `NEUTRAL_VOICE` from a new shared `src/lib/onboarding/voice-presets.ts` so the locked map (`friendly={2,2,2}` / `professional={4,2,3}` / `casual={1,3,2}`) can't drift between caller and deriver. (2) **`derivePalette` industry hint** — Step 4's call now passes `industry: industryKey` matching `createWebsiteForClient`. (3) **Funnel-offer generator runs in the wizard** — `triggerGeneration` fires `generateFunnelOffer` in parallel with site generation, awaits the offer, re-derives the brief with `offerOverride`, then kicks off `generateFunnelStub`. The funnel generator threads `offer.headline / promise / risk_reversal / cta_text` through every section, and `funnels.funnel_offer` is populated via `offerToRow`. Offer failure is NON-BLOCKING — `setOfferWarning` surfaces an inline amber note on Step 7's BuildReady; site + funnel still publish. `deriveBriefFromWizard` gained an optional `offerOverride: FunnelOffer | null` param so the caller can re-derive once the offer settles. (4) **Step 2 mirrors to canonical `clients` columns** — `/api/clients/[id]/wizard-state` POST now copies `businessName / phone / serviceArea` onto `clients.name / primary_contact_phone / service_area` on every state write, so every surface reading the canonical columns (the hub, `/settings/profile`, the sidebar, the public-site resolver) sees Step 2's values rather than signup defaults. `hours` + `address` have no clients columns and stay in `wizard_state.step_data.step2` only. (5) **`wizard-assets` brand-seed parity** — the defensive brand-seed insert now writes the full column set (`design_bundle_id` + `derived_palette` + `brand_colors` + `tagline` + `heading_font='inter-tight'` + `body_font='inter-tight'`) matching `createWebsiteForClient` / `provisionPendingSignup` so the wizard's fallback brand row can't differ from the concierge path.
- **Pattern B two-stage cancellation — RESOLVED (Session C).** Cancellation is **NOT** a one-shot "delete on day 30" — it's two stages with explicit transitions. Stage 1 (`lifecycle_status='cancelled'`, day 0–30): customer can log in, sees a high-vis `CancellationBanner` with a Reactivate CTA; reactivate flow mints a fresh Stripe Checkout and the webhook flips back to `'active'`. Stage 2 (`lifecycle_status='deleted'`, day 30–90): customer locked out (`dashboardIsAccessible` returns false); operator-only recovery out-of-band (support call → manual restore script). Stage 3 (day 83): cron sends 7-day warning email. Stage 4 (day 90): cron HARD-deletes the row via cascade FKs (irreversible). Rationale: 30-day grace alone is too aggressive for real-world edge cases (sickness, travel, holiday); a two-stage flow gives effectively 90 days of recovery + multiple notices for GDPR + customer protection + legal-risk reduction. Auth: `requireClientAccess` on both `/api/clients/[id]/cancel` and `/reactivate` — customer for own client, operator concierge for either. **Trigger to revisit**: if support reports a high rate of "I missed the warning email" recoveries past day 90, extend the day-83 warning to a 2-email cadence (day 76 + day 83) before the hard delete. The cron's stage 2 is already gated on `hard_delete_warning_sent_at IS NULL`, so a second email needs a sibling column.
- **`lifecycle_status` enum extensions (Session C, migration 0090).** `'cancelled'` + `'deleted'` added to `client_lifecycle`. New helpers in `lib/auth/lifecycle.ts`: `isCancelled(value)` (Stage 1 surface — show banner), `isSoftDeleted(value)` (Stage 2 — locked out). `dashboardIsAccessible` returns false for `'deleted'` (locked out) but TRUE for `'cancelled'` (the grace surface is the whole point — customer needs UI access to reactivate). `publicSiteIsServable` returns false for both. **Adding the next lifecycle state**: same pattern — separate migration for the enum value commit, then a follow-up migration for any schema/cron that references it. Update `CLIENT_LIFECYCLE_VALUES` array, `LIFECYCLE_LABEL`, `lifecyclePhrase`, AND every helper's switch (TypeScript will catch missing cases — exhaustiveness check holds).

- **Websites one-per-client unique constraint — RESOLVED (Phase 2 concierge-parity follow-up; migration 0094).** `websites` carries `UNIQUE(client_id)` (constraint name: `websites_one_per_client`). The wizard-assets idempotency probe + the operator-concierge guard already make duplicate creation nearly impossible in flight, but three clients on the live DB had ended up with two websites each (Lucan Flooring / getSparkit / Cork Cleaning Co — all the residue of an early-Pattern-B race that pre-dated the idempotency probe). Remediation choice: **hard-delete the older row per client** (chosen over slug-rename / soft-archive) — none of the older rows were published, FKs CASCADE cleanly (`website_versions`, `content_drafts`, `capability_grants`, `force_publish_audit_log`, `website_approval_submissions` all `ON DELETE CASCADE`; `tickets.context_website_id` is `ON DELETE SET NULL`), and the migration's CTE picks "older row per client" generically so a future race that slips past the in-app probes self-heals at the next apply. Verified read-only pre-migration: 36 clients with websites, 3 to-delete, 36 to-keep. **Trigger to revisit (loosen the constraint):** if a real customer needs multiple websites under one client account (a multi-brand operator running e.g. two distinct sub-brands), drop the unique constraint and add a `primary boolean` flag — same V1 forcing-function shape as `client_gbp_locations` / `client_meta_ad_accounts`. Don't drop the constraint without that flag — every consumer (the public-site resolver, `/website` hub, ScaffoldWebsiteButton, the wizard's persistence probe) currently reads "one website per client" as an invariant.

- **Pattern B capability grants on signup — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes).** `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS` (`src/lib/auth/capabilities.ts`) is the full self-serve client-tier capability bundle (`viewBuilder + editCopy + editMedia + editSEO + editLayout + editSections + editTheme + editPages + editForms + useAI + publish + rollback + manageDomain` — `approve` deliberately excluded; admin-only governance). `signup-workspace.ts` `provisionPendingSignup` inserts a workspace-wide `capability_grants` row for the new owner via the service-role client (bypasses the operator-only `capability_grants_insert` policy). Migration `0087_client_owner_grants_and_review_request.sql` backfilled the same grant for every existing client-role user whose workspace was in `preview` / `active` / `live` / `onboarding` (5 of 6 user rows on the live DB — the 6th already held a workspace-wide grant and was skipped). The operator concierge path (`create-client.ts`) does NOT create an end-user — when the operator later invites the owner via the team-invite flow, the invite acceptance is where the grant should land; for now operators already hold `ADMIN_DEFAULTS` and edit on the customer's behalf. Migration `0087` also widened `clients_update` RLS so any user with the `publish` cap can update their own tenant's clients row (needed for `/settings/profile`'s save) — tenant-scoped via `accessible_client_ids()`. **Adding a new capability:** add it to the `Capability` union + `ALL_CAPABILITIES`, decide whether it belongs in `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS`, and **add a fresh migration that backfills the new cap onto existing owners' grant rows** if it should retro-apply (the `0087` backfill ran once — re-running it won't pick up new caps).
- **Client settings stubs (`/settings/profile|notifications|security|integrations|help`) — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes).** `/settings/profile` reads the live `clients` row + the signed-in `users` row (business name / industry / service area / primary contact / display name); writes persist via Supabase update (works because `clients_update` RLS widened in 0087). `/settings/notifications` client branch mounts `QuietHoursSection` (writable, against `clients.quiet_hours_*`) + a READ-ONLY display of `notification_preferences` ("recipients managed by your operator — open a ticket if you want one added"). The operator-only `notification_preferences` write path was NOT widened — letting clients add arbitrary recipients would let them disable operator notifications. `/settings/security` is a real password-change via `supabase.auth.updateUser` + a "sign out of every device" using `supabase.auth.signOut({ scope: 'global' })`; 2FA enrolment surface deferred (Supabase TOTP supports it but the QR + recovery-codes UX wasn't in scope). `/settings/integrations` client branch is the same `IntegrationConnectionsSection` operator sub-account view uses, scoped to the signed-in client. `/settings/help` reads support contact from `NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPPORT_NAME` / `_PHONE_DISPLAY` / `_PHONE_E164` / `_EMAIL` env vars (defaults to the prior Craig / 0411 234 567 values when env unset). **Session 2 deleted the unused stub data modules** (`lib/settings/client-profile.ts`, `client-security.ts`, `client-integrations.tsx`, `client-notifications.ts`); `client-help.tsx` was kept because `/settings/help` still consumes its FAQ + recent-support copy. Don't reintroduce the deleted files — every consumer is on live data now.
- **Brand editor — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes · Session 2).** `/settings/brand` (`src/app/settings/brand/page.tsx` + `_content.tsx`) is a real brand editor — palette (primary + 2 supporting brand colours + 3 inherited section defaults: heading / body / background), typography (heading + body font picked from `CURATED_FONTS`), logo upload (reuses `uploadSectionImage` against the `section-media` bucket), tagline, audience line, industry, voice tone (3 sliders). Reads + writes the `brands` row directly via the browser Supabase client; the cap gate is `editTheme` (in `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS`). Migration `0088` added the optional columns (`brand_colors text[]` / `heading_font` / `body_font` / `heading_color` / `body_color` / `background_color` / `tagline`) and widened `brands_update` RLS so an owner with `editTheme` can update their own brand row (previously operator-only). **The `brand-style-stub.ts` localStorage overlay is now SUNSET** (Session: Brand stub refit) — every section-editor color/font picker writes through the brands table via the new `brand-style.ts` mutation helper; see the inventory entry above. The brand editor's save path is unchanged. Read paths (`fetchBrandForClient` in `lib/website/queries.tsx`) now read all the new columns and fall back to undefined when NULL, so existing editor surfaces inherit brand-level defaults from the table the moment a customer saves. Listed in both `clientSettingsNav` and `subAccountSettingsNav`.
- **Operator concierge invite acceptance — RESOLVED via DB trigger (Session: Pattern B critical fixes · Session 2).** Migration `0088` added `private.grant_owner_caps_on_first_user()` — an `AFTER INSERT` trigger on `public.users` that auto-grants `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS` to the FIRST client-role user of a workspace. The "first" check is `not exists` against `public.users` filtered by the same `client_id` — every subsequent client user for that workspace stays at `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` (the teammate floor), as designed. The trigger covers BOTH Pattern B signup (where `signup-workspace.ts` also inserts the same grant explicitly — the `on conflict (user_id, website_id) do nothing` clause makes the two paths idempotent) AND the operator-concierge invite-accept flow (Pattern B operator invite — see below). New caps need a fresh migration to update both the trigger's array literal and the backfill seed. The signup-workspace explicit grant was left in place as defence in depth.
- **Pattern B operator invite flow — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B operator-invite).** Real magic-link invites are wired end-to-end. The previous client-side fabricated links (TeamInviteModal + ClientTeamInviteModal both produced `https://app.webnua.io/invite/wb_<random>` strings that resolved to nothing) are gone. Architecture:
  - **Migration `0089`** adds `token` (random URL-safe base64, 256 bits of entropy, UNIQUE-indexed) + `consumed_at` (timestamptz NULL) to both `team_invites` and `client_user_invites`. Existing rows are backfilled with a random token and their status flipped to `expired` (they were never emailable). A daily `pg_cron` sweep at 02:00 UTC flips pending invites past `expires_at` to `expired` so the UI's "Resend" affordance lights up correctly.
  - **`lib/invites/token.ts`** generates the opaque tokens (32 random bytes → base64url ≈ 43 chars). Not HMAC-signed — DB lookup is the source of truth; `consumed_at` + `expires_at` drive validity.
  - **`lib/invites/invite-email.ts`** sends the magic-link email via Resend (`callExternal` shape — sibling of `lib/auth/verification-email.ts` + `welcome-email.ts`). Two variants discriminated by `kind: 'team' | 'client'`; both share the same Suby/Sultanic voice. Skips honestly when `RESEND_API_KEY` is unset (the modal's confirmation step surfaces "email skipped — copy the link and send it directly" rather than misleadingly claiming delivery).
  - **`lib/invites/server.ts`** is the server-only business logic. `createTeamInvite` / `createClientUserInvite` (write the row + send the email; refuse duplicate pending invites per email; for client invites, re-check the seat limit server-side as a defence-in-depth guard against the in-memory modal check). `resolveInviteByToken` (probe both tables; returns redacted summary with state error when not actionable). `acceptInvite` (validate, refuse `emailAlreadyRegistered`, `supabase.auth.admin.createUser({ password, email_confirm: true, user_metadata: { role, client_id?, team_role?, display_name } })`, mark `consumed_at` + `status='accepted'`, copy `team_invite_clients` → `user_client_access` for junior team invites). `resendInvite` (re-mint token, extend expiry, re-send email — the OLD token becomes unresolvable because the UNIQUE-indexed column is overwritten). `cancelInvite` (flip to `revoked`). The 0088 auto-grant trigger fires when the new public.users row lands, so first-user-of-workspace gets CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS automatically.
  - **7 routes** under `src/app/api/invites/`: `POST /team` (operator-only), `POST /client` (operator OR client-role for that client), `GET /[token]` (public, redacted summary), `POST /[token]/accept` (public; password setup; rate-limited via `signup_attempt`), `POST /[id]/resend` + `POST /[id]/cancel` (auth shape mirrors the create route). All return JSON with consistent `{ ok, error, kind }` shapes.
  - **`/invite/[token]` page** (lives in the `(auth)` route group so it reuses the auth layout). Server-renders invite metadata via `resolveInviteByToken`; the `_form.tsx` client component does the two-stage submit (POST accept → `supabase.auth.signInWithPassword` → router.push to dashboard). Error states (expired / consumed / revoked / not_found) render friendly explainers with a "contact your operator" link or, for consumed, a "Sign in" CTA.
  - **Modal updates.** Both `TeamInviteModal` + `ClientTeamInviteModal` now AWAIT a real route call (`addTeamInvite` / `addClientInvite` in their respective stub modules — kept the original module names so the ~50 import sites are unchanged; the modules now wrap fetch instead of fabricating + writing direct to Supabase). The Send button shows a loading state; failures surface inline via `humaniseInviteError` (`lib/invites/error-text.ts`); the confirmation step shows the real magic link via `InviteCopyLinkRow` AND adapts copy based on `emailOutcome` ('sent' / 'failed' / 'skipped'). `addClientInvite` now takes a `{ clientId }` param (added to the draft) since operators-in-sub-account-mode now use this same modal — see next bullet.
  - **Operator-concierge launch surface.** Per the brief's locked Q3 answer, the entry point is sub-account `/settings/team`. The dispatcher `app/settings/team/page.tsx` already dispatched on role; `_admin-content.tsx` now also dispatches on workspace mode — agency mode → existing Webnua-team UI; sub-account mode → the new `_sub-account-content.tsx` mounting `InviteTeammateButton` (which itself was widened to accept operator-in-sub-account-mode by reading `useWorkspace().activeClientId`). When no client-role users exist yet for the workspace, the button label flips to "Invite the owner →" + a paper-2 explainer card explains the auto-grant.
  - **Pending invite list** is now real on both surfaces. The operator agency-team page surfaces every `pending` team_invites row with `Resend` + `Revoke` action chips; the client + sub-account team pages do the same for their `client_user_invites`. `TeamRow.actions[]` was extended with an optional `onClick` so action chips can be wired without changing existing call sites.
  - **Seat-limit accuracy.** `createClientUserInvite` re-reads the seat limit from `policy_overrides` + `agency_policy` directly via service-role (not via the in-memory hydrated stores, which are client-side) and refuses when the limit would be exceeded — the client-side `canInviteToClient` stays as the modal's pre-flight check.
  - **Token security model.** Opaque, DB-resolved, single-use. A token leak between resend cycles only burns the OLD token (UNIQUE constraint forces replacement); a leaked active token is single-use (the `consumed_at` UPDATE locks it). The accept route is rate-limited under the `signup_attempt` family (10/IP/hour) so brute-forcing tokens off the GET resolver is bounded.
- **`/settings/*` direct-URL guard widened for clients — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes · Session 2).** `app/settings/layout.tsx` previously only redirected operators away from wrong-mode tabs. Now also redirects client-role users off any operator-only surface: `AGENCY_ONLY` (`/settings/workspace|plans|defaults|seats|api|platform-templates`), `SUB_ACCOUNT_ONLY` (`/settings/email|sms`), AND the new `OPERATOR_ONLY` bucket (`/settings/access|danger` — operator governance regardless of mode). Universal routes (`/settings/integrations|domains|profile|brand|team|notifications|billing|security|help`) load for both roles via their existing per-role dispatch. The redirect target is `/settings`, which routes to a role-appropriate landing tab.
- **Funnel client-side unpublish — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes · Session 2).** `FunnelSlugEditor` previously gated the publish/unpublish row on `role === 'admin' && capabilities.has('publish')` — clients hold `publish` via `CLIENT_OWNER_DEFAULTS` (Session 1) but the role gate kept the button hidden. Flipped to a pure cap check (`capabilities.has('publish')`). The `funnels_update` RLS was widened in migration 0088 to allow `publish`-cap holders to update their own tenant's funnels row; the existing `funnels_update` policy was operator-only so the UI fix alone would have 403'd.
- **`/website` Scaffold button context — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes · Session 2).** The `/website` agency empty-state button used to flat-link to `/clients/new` regardless of context. Session 2's `ScaffoldWebsiteButton` (`src/components/shared/website/ScaffoldWebsiteButton.tsx`) dispatches on workspace mode: agency (no client picked) → still links to `/clients/new` (the create-NEW-client flow); sub-account (client picked, no website yet) → reads the existing client + brand row, builds a default `ClientBrief`, calls the new `createWebsiteForClient` helper (extracted from `createClientWithGeneration` so it can run standalone), routes to `/website`. Default brief: brand fields come from the live brand row; `primaryIntent: { kind: 'book' }`, `audience: 'mixed'`, empty funnel slot — the generator tolerates these.
- **Pattern B "request operator review before publishing" — RESOLVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes).** Optional secondary path on `PublishToGoLiveCTA` — a small inline "Or request operator review first →" button beside the primary Publish CTA. Clicking it POSTs `/api/clients/[id]/request-review` (`requireClientAccess`), which stamps `clients.review_requested_at` (column added by migration `0087`), fans an operator-notification email via Resend (`sendOperatorEmail` — `RESEND_API_KEY` unset → skipped, no fake), and returns. The button settles into a green mono "✓ Review requested · we'll be in touch within 24h" — it does NOT block direct publish; the client can still hit Publish if they change their mind. Operator side: `ReviewRequestsPanel` (`src/components/admin/dashboard/ReviewRequestsPanel.tsx`) mounts on the agency-mode admin dashboard and lists every client with a non-null `review_requested_at` (newest first; hidden when empty). Each row shows the request age + the client's phone/email + a "Drill in →" (switches workspace context) + "Mark handled" button which POSTs `/api/clients/[id]/clear-review-request` (operator-only, clears the column). Operators handle the actual review out-of-band (call / email / in-app messaging) — the request is a signal to the queue, NOT a state machine. Notification fan-out tries `notification_preferences` for the client first, falls back to every admin-role user's email.
- **`lifecycle_status` `as never` casts — REMOVED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes).** The Supabase TypeScript types were regenerated against the live DB (Pattern B migration `0084` added `pending_verification` / `preview` / `banned` / `active` to the `client_lifecycle` enum). The `as never` casts in `create-client.ts`, `signup-workspace.ts`, `clients-store.ts`, and `(admin)/signups/page.tsx` were removed — the values are now well-typed enum members. **When extending the lifecycle enum again**: add via migration (precedent: `0084` migration-only, `0085` references the new values one migration later because Postgres requires the `ADD VALUE` to commit first), then run `mcp__supabase__generate_typescript_types` and replace `src/lib/types/database.ts` — no in-code casts needed.
- **`/website` Scaffold button — FIXED (Session: Pattern B critical fixes).** The agency empty-state "Scaffold a new website" button is now `<Button asChild><Link href="/clients/new">…` — matches the sidebar `AdminClientPicker` "+ Add new client" and the `/(admin)/websites` matrix "Build →" entry points. The button stays behind `<CapabilityGate capability="editPages">` (operators hold the cap, clients don't — clients wouldn't hit the agency empty state anyway).
- **Pattern B onboarding — build-first, pay-to-publish (Session 2 refactor).** Session 1's Pattern A ("pay first, then onboard") has been replaced. The new flow: stranger → `/sign-up` (free, no Stripe at signup) → DB-backed IP rate-limit (10 attempts/IP/hour, 3 successes/IP/24h via `rate_limit_hits`, migration 0085) + disposable-domain check (`disposable-email-domains` npm) + duplicate-email refuse → `provisionPendingSignup` (`lib/auth/signup-workspace.ts`) inserts the clients row with `lifecycle_status='pending_verification'` (new default — migration 0085) + creates the auth user with `email_confirm: false` + generates the magic link → verification email sent via Resend (`lib/auth/verification-email.ts`) → user clicks magic link → Supabase confirms `email_confirmed_at` → the 0085 `on_auth_email_verified` trigger flips `lifecycle_status` from 'pending_verification' to 'preview' → user lands on `/dashboard` → IntegrationOnboarding mounts the wizard surface + the new `PublishToGoLiveCTA` at the top → customer hits Publish → Stripe Checkout (the EXISTING `/api/integrations/stripe/checkout` route, widened to `requireClientAccess` in Session 1) → on `subscription.created` the webhook calls `markClientActiveOnPublish` which flips `lifecycle_status` 'preview' → 'active' + fires the `welcome-email.ts` (refit to fire post-publish, not post-signup). **Migrations 0084 / 0085 / 0086** add the new enum values (`pending_verification`, `preview`, `banned`, `active`), the `rate_limit_hits` table, the `re_engagement_sent_at` column, the email-verification trigger, and three pg_cron jobs (pending-verification 7-day sweep, rate_limit_hits 7-day sweep, daily re-engagement-email scan). **Lifecycle SoT** is `lib/auth/lifecycle.ts` — every dispatcher (dashboard, public renderer, operator admin) reads the helpers (`publicSiteIsServable` / `publicSiteIsPreview` / `dashboardIsInPreOnboarding` / `isActivelyPaying`) — never raw string compares. The Session 1 'live' / 'onboarding' values stay valid; the helpers treat them as 'active' / 'preview' respectively, so Session 1's production clients keep working without a backfill.
- **Pattern B preview-site rendering — single URL, lifecycle-gated.** The locked Q2 was "use the existing {slug}.webnua.dev URL pattern; same URL serves preview content while lifecycle_status='preview' (with floating banner + disabled forms), then transitions to serving published content when 'active'". Implementation: the resolver (`lib/public-site/resolve.ts`) reads `clients.lifecycle_status`; returns 'not_found' for `pending_verification`/`banned`/`churned`; returns `isPreview: true` for `preview`/`onboarding`; normal for `active`/`live`/`paused`. **Preview falls back to the DRAFT version** (not just published) so a mid-wizard customer with no published version sees their generated site. The `PublicSiteRenderer` accepts `isPreview` + mounts `PreviewBanner` (floating bottom-center pill with "Publish to go live →" CTA) + injects `<meta robots="noindex,nofollow">` via the route's `generateMetadata`. **Forms on preview render but cannot submit** — `PublicFormSubmit.isPreview` rides the slot context, `FormBlock` disables the submit button + intercepts the form's onSubmit + renders a "Preview mode. This form is disabled until you publish — your leads stay in your inbox" note above the fields. No new DNS / cert / middleware work needed.
- **AI generation rate limits — site/funnel are workspace-scoped; section regen is IP-scoped (provisional).** `/api/generate-site` and `/api/generate-funnel` check `ai_site_gen` / `ai_funnel_gen` (3/client/24h) when a `clientId` is supplied — the dev preview surface (no clientId) stays unmetered. `/api/generate-seo` checks `ai_section_regen` (10/IP/hour) — the route doesn't carry a clientId today, so IP is the V1 key. **Trigger to revisit:** thread a `clientId` through the `seo-generate.ts` browser caller + accept it on the route → switch the section-regen key to `client_id` for per-workspace precision. Same applies to `enhance-field` + `enhance-offer` (left unmetered for now — they're called once per signup, low abuse risk). The 5 rate-limit configs live in `RATE_LIMITS` (`lib/rate-limit/index.ts`) — change there, not at call sites.
- **Re-engagement email — sends once per client lifetime (clients.re_engagement_sent_at).** The daily `webnua_re_engagement_scan` cron (migration 0086) enqueues `send_re_engagement_email` for clients in 'preview' state >7 days old whose `re_engagement_sent_at IS NULL`. The handler (`lib/auth/re-engagement-handler.ts`) stamps the timestamp on send so the next scan skips them. **A customer who lapses, publishes, then lapses to preview again does NOT get a second nudge** — the cron WHERE clause filters on `IS NULL`. Operator can NULL the column manually to force a resend.
- **Pattern A leftover in the Stripe webhook — kept defensively.** The webhook handler still recognises `kind=signup` metadata on `subscription.created` events (Session 1's stamp), logs a warning, and ACKs without provisioning. Any Pattern A Checkout that lands AFTER the Pattern B deploy (an in-flight session) is handled cleanly — Stripe creates the Customer + subscription, we record via `integration_call_log`, operator picks up + manually creates the workspace. Real production traffic on Pattern A has been verified live (Session 1 deployed + tested); the manual-pickup path is the safety net for the rare race.
- **Onboarding foundation — self-serve signup is wired (Session 1; superseded by Pattern B above).** Reference `reference/onboarding-flow-audit.md`. Session 1's "pay first, then onboard" flow: stranger → `/sign-up` (`src/app/(auth)/sign-up/page.tsx`, captures business name + email + category) → `POST /api/sign-up` (mints a Stripe Checkout session with `metadata.kind = 'signup'` + the captured details + the email pre-filled) → Stripe Checkout → `/sign-up/success` interstitial → Stripe fires `customer.subscription.created` → the webhook (`app/api/integrations/stripe/webhook/route.ts`) reads the `signup` metadata, called `provisionSignupWorkspace` to insert the clients row (the three AFTER INSERT triggers fan templates + automations), create the auth user with `email_confirm: true` (the 0017 trigger creates `public.users`), insert the `client_stripe_customers` mapping, generate a magic link, and email the link via `src/lib/auth/welcome-email.ts`. **Subscribe-before-workspace was locked** (Q2): no DB write happened before Stripe confirms payment. **Concierge path unchanged** — the operator `CreateClientModal` + `lib/clients/create-client.ts` still works (now writes `lifecycle_status='active'` explicitly so it bypasses Pattern B's verify+pay gates).
- **Stripe `/checkout` + `/portal` routes are client-or-operator now** (was operator-only). The Stripe billing infrastructure (Phase 7) was widened in the onboarding foundation session: both `app/api/integrations/stripe/checkout/route.ts` and `app/api/integrations/stripe/portal/route.ts` use `requireClientAccess` instead of `requireOperatorForClient`. A client subscribes themselves; a client manages their own card / invoices / cancellation via the Stripe Customer Portal. Client `/settings/billing` (`_client-content.tsx`) now mounts `StripeSubscriptionSection` — same component the operator sub-account view uses; the previous Voltline-keyed stub (`lib/settings/client-billing.tsx`) was deleted. **What this does NOT include:** a Webnua-side pre-cancellation warning (the audit asked for one). The data-retention behaviour on cancellation is undecided — Stripe's portal handles the actual cancel, but we don't yet have a defined "workspace lifecycle on subscription end" story. Defer a confirmation modal until that policy lands.
- **Client sidebar identity reads live (no constants).** `ClientSidebar.tsx` resolves identity from `useUser()` + `useAdminClients()`; status pill is a simple "Active" badge per locked Q6 (no computed "day N"). The previous hardcoded constants (`clientWorkspace`, `clientUser`, `clientSupport`) in `lib/nav/client-nav.ts` are gone; only `clientNav` (the nav-item list) and `clientSupportContact` (managed-by Webnua, a static cross-client constant) remain. `AdminSidebar.tsx` also reads `useUser()` for the operator's name (the `adminUser` constant in `lib/nav/admin-nav.ts` was dropped). The dead `clientSupportContact.ctaHref = '/support'` was retargeted to `/tickets/new` (the audit flagged `/support` as a 404). **Nav badge counts** (`'5'`/`'2'`/`'+2'` in the old client nav) were dropped along with the constants — they were stubs anyway; a future session wires real unread counts (audit's "honourable mentions").
- **Onboarding-screen Connect buttons are real OAuth now.** `IntegrationOnboarding` (`src/components/shared/onboarding/IntegrationOnboarding.tsx`) was rewritten to mount the real flows: `StripeSubscriptionSection` (billing setup), `IntegrationConnectionsSection` (GBP + Meta Ads — same component the sub-account `/settings/integrations` uses), and a link card to `/settings/domains` (custom domain). The previous 5 stub `IntegrationCard`s opening `ConnectIntegrationModal` are gone. **OAuth callback `returnTo`** — the connect / callback routes now accept an optional `returnTo` internal path (signed into the state token). The onboarding screen sets `returnTo='/dashboard'` so post-OAuth lands back on dashboard rather than `/settings/integrations`. The picker auto-open pattern was extracted into `IntegrationCallbackPickers` (`components/shared/settings/IntegrationCallbackPickers.tsx`) — both `IntegrationConnectionsSection` and any future surface mount this. **`ConnectIntegrationModal` + `ConnectIntegrationButton` were NOT deleted** — two other stub surfaces still consume them (`app/settings/integrations/_client-content.tsx` and `app/settings/api/page.tsx`'s "Manage" buttons). The brief's Q5 ("Delete onboarding stub modals") was scoped to the onboarding context; sunset the files in a future session that converts those two settings stubs to real surfaces. Until then, the `IntegrationCard.action.kind` prop remains.
- **`signup_submissions` table — orphan, deprecated, slated for removal.** The `signup_submissions` table appears in `src/lib/types/database.ts:2801` (the generated `Database` type) but has **NO migration in `supabase/migrations/`** and **zero references** in `src/lib` / `src/app` / `src/components`. The audit (§3 / RLS test suite §4) flagged this; it was a marketing-landing signup-capture surface that was either built and removed without a migration, or generated into the type without ever being migrated. With the self-serve signup flow now landed (subscribe-before-workspace via Stripe Checkout, not via `signup_submissions`), this table has **no future role** — the signup flow writes straight to `clients` + `auth.users` once payment confirms. **Future session — cleanup migration.** Before dropping, confirm the table actually exists in every environment that matters (Supabase dashboard SQL: `select * from pg_class where relname = 'signup_submissions'`). If it exists: a migration `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS public.signup_submissions CASCADE` + regenerating `database.ts` removes the orphan cleanly. If it does NOT exist: just regenerate `database.ts` — the type was a phantom and will drop out. **This session does not add a SQL migration** — without knowing the environment-level state, neither a `COMMENT ON` (would error if absent) nor a `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS` (irreversible without backup) is safe to ship blind.

- **Automation editor — client-vs-operator split (PR #106).** The automation editor at `/automations/[id]` honours role + plan invariants:
  - **Clients edit copy + cadence; operators own templates.** Clients see action cards with editable body/subject + per-action config knobs, no reorder/delete/add affordances. Operators see the full Session-3 editor — add/move/remove + clone + test-send + the trigger cadence editor.
  - **Filter checkboxes (`requires_phone` / `_email` / `_gbp_location`) are hidden in the UI for both roles** — they're system invariants the runtime engine enforces. The `trigger_filters` jsonb still persists and is preserved on every save (`buildTriggerFiltersPayloadFromEditor`) so unrelated cadence edits don't clobber the row's stored filters. **`to_status`** is hidden too (editing would silently change what the automation IS — clone to change).
  - **Trigger settings → cadence.** The trigger-editor section is now labelled `// CADENCE`; with only `delay_minutes` / `days_after_last_outbound` / `max_nudges` visible (and the section suppressed entirely when an automation has none). Frame as "How long to wait before this fires."
  - **5-action cap per automation.** `MAX_ACTIONS_PER_AUTOMATION = 5` — enforced server-side in `useAddAction` (throws `AppError.validation`, applies to operators too as an abuse guard) AND in `AutomationAddActionMenu` (disabled button with "Maximum 5 actions per automation" note). **Parked decision — upcharge tier:** the brief noted "we'll add upcharge in the future when we build this feature out more"; the cap stays global until a plan tier is built. Don't add a per-client override path until then — it's the same plan-resolver shape that already exists for seat limits.
  - **GBP prerequisite on toggle.** `useAutomationGbpGuard()` (`components/shared/automations/AutomationGbpGuard.tsx`) wraps every enable-toggle path (client roster, admin roster, editor footer). Before flipping a GBP-requiring automation to ON it runs a `client_gbp_locations` count probe (RLS-scoped, `head: true`); a missing row blocks the toggle and opens a Dialog with "Connect Google Business Profile to enable this automation" + CTA to `/settings/integrations`. Disabling never blocks. **`AutomationStatsCard` is now controlled** (not internal-state) so a GBP-blocked toggle reverts visually too. `AutomationStatsCard` + `AutomationFlowMini` carry `clientId` + `requiresGbpLocation` for the guard.
  - **Operator-notification body is read-only with a platform-template link.** `send_operator_notification` action cards render the current `platform_email_templates` body as a paper-2 preview + "Edit template at /settings/platform-templates →" link, NOT an editable textarea — edits in the per-action `body_text` would never reach the send-handler (which reads platform-level templates first).
  - **Test send is operator-only and wired.** `AutomationTestSendCard` mounts only when `role === 'admin'`. `POST /api/automations/test-send` (operator-only via `requireOperatorForClient`) resolves the picked action's `action_config.body` / `subject`, validates ownership cross-tenant, and enqueues `send_email` for email-channel tests (the modal switches channel when both SMS + email comm actions exist). **SMS test-send returns `no-test-phone`** because `public.users` carries no phone column — the modal surfaces "Add your phone in Settings to enable test SMS; switch to email to test now"; when a phone column lands, the route's SMS branch flips to enqueueing `send_sms` (no other changes needed). Sample-context substitution is curated in both the route AND the modal preview so the operator sees what actually sends. Recipient is the signed-in operator's auth email.
  - **`lead_created` group subtitle** spells out the per-channel split ("SMS to the lead (when phone is on file), email to the lead (when email is on file), and a notification to you — all fan from one trigger") so the three default automations no longer look like duplicates. `job_completed` carries a similar "SMS preferred, email fallback" line.
  - **Tier-1 deletions:** `AutomationVariableList.tsx` is gone (per-card chips are the only variable-insert path). The inert "Change trigger →" button on `AutomationTriggerBox` is gone — trigger type really is fixed (clone to change). The new structural API surface: `useAutomationGbpGuard` + the `clientId` / `actions` props on `AutomationTestSendCard` + the `readOnly` prop on `AutomationActionCard` + the `currentCount` prop on `AutomationAddActionMenu`.
- **`LeadAutomationPanel` + per-lead automation-run history — DONE (Phase 8 · Session 4).** Both Session 3 carve-outs are closed: (1) the "View all runs" expansion lives at the bottom of `LeadAutomationPanel` as a collapsible block, fetching `GET /api/leads/[id]/runs` lazily on expand (the route returns up to 200 runs ordered newest first); (2) the "Needs follow-up" inbox tab landed earlier with the cold-lead-scanner work.
