The panel itself is mounted on both `_admin-content.tsx` + `_client-content.tsx` for `/leads/[id]`. Closed history rows render with a status-keyed pill (`completed` = good, `cancelled` = quiet, `failed` = warn) + the start time + position progress.
- ~~**Mid-execution action reordering — runs see the snapshot at trigger time.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 8 · Session 3 follow-up · migration 0080). `automation_runs.action_sequence uuid[]` is the per-run snapshot of `automation_actions.id` values in position order, captured at run creation. The engine's `processNextAction` walks THIS array (`current_action_position` is treated as a 1-indexed slot — position N = `action_sequence[N - 1]`) via `resolveActionForRun(run, startPosition)` in `src/lib/automations/engine.ts`. **Reorder semantics:** an in-flight run continues with its original action ids in their original sequence. **Insert semantics:** newly added actions DO NOT appear in any in-flight run. **Delete semantics:** if an id in `action_sequence` no longer exists in `automation_actions`, the resolver silently skips it and lands on the next still-existing id (the only mid-run mutation that can affect a live run — and the run gracefully degrades rather than crashing). Backwards compat: a run whose `action_sequence` is empty (legacy / pre-0080) falls back to the live position query so the existing in-flight runs the migration backfill missed still execute. The same snapshot is read by `handoff.ts` `recordInboundOnLead` when deciding whether the run's CURRENT action is a comm-action (so a mid-run reorder can't misclassify the current step). Editor surfacing: `useAutomationActiveRuns(automationId)` (`lib/automations/queries.tsx`) returns the running + paused count; the editor mounts a mono pill above the trigger box when > 0 ("// N active runs — they'll finish with the previous sequence") so the operator knows their edit doesn't disrupt live work.
- **The 8-step onboarding wizard was sunset** (cleanup pass). Client creation is now the `CreateClientModal` quick-create flow (see the `admin/` create-client inventory section). The wizard routes, `lib/onboarding/`, `components/admin/onboarding/`, `WizardSectionEditor`, the wizard-only `AutomationCard`, and `BuilderLayout` / `PreviewPanelBar` were deleted. `builder-design.md §5` and `builder-generation-design.md §3` carry SUPERSEDED banners.
- **Lead-capture forms** — the form builder (the `editForms` capability, the `form` section type, the `Section.form` envelope config, `form_submitted` lead events) shipped after Cluster 9; the retroactive design doc is `reference/form-builder-design.md`. Files: `lib/website/form-config.ts`, `lib/website/sections/form.tsx`, `components/shared/website/{FormBlock,FormFieldTypePicker,SectionFormControls}.tsx`. Public-site rendering of forms is the remaining piece, deferred with the public-render pipeline.
- **Auth — DONE (real Supabase Auth, end to end).** `backend-schema-design.md §6` / `[JC-10]` called for real Supabase Auth; it is wired (`7ceda3c` Phase 2, `b07a79c` Phase 3 fix, `341d19f` Phase 5). `user-stub.tsx` (misnamed — kept for import stability) resolves the signed-in user from a real `supabase.auth` session; `(auth)/login` is a real `signInWithPassword` screen; `capability_grants` are live rows; `DataHydrationProvider` hydrates the in-memory stores from Supabase on every auth change. **A logged-out page load shows a wall of `401 permission denied` console warnings** — `DataHydrationProvider` fires `hydrateAll()` on mount before a session exists and the `anon` role is correctly refused; it re-hydrates after sign-in. That is expected noise, not a bug. **Still owed:** a deliberate cross-tenant RLS validation pass — the policies have not been systematically negative-tested with real `auth.uid()`s. **Never grant `anon` table access** — it would defeat every RLS policy.
- Backend wiring (Supabase) — **in progress.** Design ratified in `reference/backend-schema-design.md`; built in phases (cross-cutting locks → page-builder design pass → non-builder migrations → builder family → real auth → surface wiring → integrations).
- ~~Error-handling pattern — decide on first real use.~~ **Resolved** (Phase 0.5): `Result<T>` + discriminated `AppError` in `src/lib/errors.ts`. See the Code-conventions "Error handling" line + backend-schema-design.md §8.
- ~~**`SettingsPanel` — second-use trigger.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 5 session B): every settings tab page now uses the extracted `components/shared/settings/SettingsPanel`. Don't re-inline the `Card`+`CardContent` pattern in new tab pages — use `SettingsPanel`.
- **`InkHero` — evaluated at six instances (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · Session 1a); verdict: styling recipe, not a component.** Six ink-hero-style components exist (`IntegrationProgressHero`, `BillingPlanCard`, `TicketsHero`, `LeadsHero`, `IntegrationMatrixHero`, `FunnelHero`). The structure-vs-styling call: only **3 of 6** share the canonical `[tag][headline][subtitle] | [side]` structure (`TicketsHero` + `LeadsHero` are near-identical twins; `IntegrationMatrixHero` matches if its stat tiles are treated as a generic `right` payload). The other three are genuinely different shapes — a progress-bar row (`IntegrationProgressHero`), a plan-meta line + action (`BillingPlanCard`), a back-link + meta rows + version pill + `FunnelAggCard` + radial flourish (`FunnelHero`). A unified `InkHero` component would need optional slots for all of those — the grab-bag this decision exists to prevent. What IS broadly shared is *styling chrome*: the `bg-ink … text-paper` surface and especially the rust mono-pill tag (near-identical in 5 of 6). **So: consolidate as a `cn()` styling recipe (`inkHero*` helpers), NOT a component.** The recipe landed in **Session 1b** as `lib/ink-hero.ts` (`inkHeroSurface()` + `INK_HERO_TAG_CLASS`), first consumed by `ClientHubHero`; existing heroes adopt it opportunistically when next touched — no churn-migration of five shipped surfaces. **Separate still-open item:** `TicketsHero` + `LeadsHero` are true twins — collapsible to one component independently of this verdict; merge whenever one of them is next touched (not urgent, not bundled into Cluster 6).
- ~~**`LeadRailCard` vs `TicketSideCard` vs booking rail — third use of the white-card-rail pattern.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 6 · Cluster 6, first commit): `TicketSideCard` → `shared/RailCard`, `TicketPropertyRow` → `shared/RailPropertyRow`; `LeadRailCard` / `LeadRailRowItem` merged in (the `rows` shorthand + `tone`/`accent` row vocabulary absorbed). All four old files deleted, no re-export shims; tickets / leads / bookings detail rails migrated. `RailPropertyRow` carries a `labelStyle: 'plain' | 'mono'` knob to cover the divergent label styling (plain for tickets/bookings, mono for leads rows). See the `shared/` rail-primitives inventory entry.
- ~~**`CalendarClientFilterBar` vs `LeadFilterChips` — second use of the rust-active filter-chip recipe.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 5 · Cluster 3 · Session A): the third use landed (admin `/automations` client filter) and triggered the extraction. `shared/FilterChips.tsx` is the canonical implementation; both `LeadFilterChips` and `CalendarClientFilterBar` were deleted (no re-export shims) and the two callers (`/leads` admin, `/calendar` admin) were migrated to import `FilterChips` directly. The `LeadFilterChip` / `CalendarClientFilter` data types stay in their feature `types.ts` files — they're structurally `FilterChip`-compatible and TypeScript accepts them. Don't reintroduce per-feature wrappers — use `FilterChips` directly.
- ~~**`CalendarClientTone` vs `LeadClientTone` / `AdminTicketClientTone` — three separate client-tone vocabularies.**~~ **Resolved (Session 7).** Two distinct vocabularies, kept separate by design: leads/tickets pills use muted background tints (`bg-rust/[0.12]` etc. — a pill-tint vocabulary); calendar/booking/automations surfaces use solid per-client identity hex (`#4a7ba6` etc. — an identity-colour vocabulary). The solid-identity map was first extracted to `lib/calendar/tones.ts` (at the booking-detail surface), then **promoted to `lib/clients/tones.ts` in Session 7** when `AutomationFlowMini` became the fourth consumer — `lib/calendar/` was the wrong home for a map automations also needs. `CLIENT_TONE_BG` / `CLIENT_TONE_BORDER_L` are keyed on the superset `ClientTone`; feature modules keep their narrower tone unions (`CalendarClientTone`, `AutomationClientTone`) and index the wider record (the shared-types-with-aliases pattern). The muted pill-tint vocabularies (`LeadClientTone` / `AdminTicketClientTone`) were **deliberately NOT folded in** — same family, different vocabulary, build separately (the discipline the `InkHero` and `LeadTimeline` calls applied; this is the third clean application). Don't reopen — the two vocabularies staying separate is the decided outcome.
- **`BuilderFooterActions` + `EditorFooterActions` both exist — revisit for a shared core if a third footer-actions variant appears.** Built as siblings (not a single conditional component) because the interaction models genuinely differ — wizards do Back/Continue + step-count progress, editors do Back/Disable/Save + auto-save indicator. Same discipline that just paid off with `FilterChips`: extract on the third data point, not the second.
- **Three `1fr + fixed-rail` detail layouts now exist (`TicketDetailLayout` 320px, the inline lead-detail shape 320px, `AutomationEditorLayout` 340px) — revisit layout-shell consolidation.** Separate from the already-parked rail-card consolidation. The widths and surface treatments diverge slightly (the editor canvas is a white card; ticket/lead detail wrap the main col in their own surface), so this isn't a drop-in extraction. Don't act now — get it on the list for a future housekeeping pass (the `TicketSideCard` → `RailCard` rename it was bundled with is now done; this layout-shell item remains open).
- **Numbered-option-row pattern — `ConflictOptionRow` (booking conflict modal) + `NegativeReviewActionRow` (admin Screen 24) are visually adjacent (Phase 5 · Cluster 4 · Session A).** Both render a numbered ink/rust-light circle + title + sub + a recommended/selected state. The shapes diverge enough to sibling (the conflict row is 2-column with the recommended state colour-only; the negative-review row is 3-column with a visible "Recommended" pill), so they were intentionally not merged. **Third use → extract** a generic `NumberedOptionRow` in `shared/` with a `pill?: string` slot.
- ~~**`CampaignActivityCard` vs `LeadTimelineEventRow` — second activity-log pattern.**~~ **Resolved** (Phase 6 · Cluster 6 · Session 1a): evaluated at the third-surface trigger (the overview hub's activity feed). The flat-feed shape was extracted to `shared/ActivityFeed` + `shared/ActivityRow`; `CampaignActivityCard` became a thin adapter over it. `LeadTimeline` was **deliberately left a sibling** — a timeline (dot-spine, scheduled-future pending events, tinted snippet quotes, gapped rows) is a genuinely different structural concern from a flat feed, and folding it in would re-create the optional-slot grab-bag. Flat feeds consolidate; the timeline stays. Don't reopen this — `LeadTimeline` staying separate is the decided outcome, not an unfinished one.

- **GBP review-request delay = 2 hours after job-completion.** Hardcoded in migration `0069`'s booking-completion trigger (`run_after = now() + interval '2 hours'`). The brief reasoned: too soon and the SMS arrives while the tradie is walking back to the van (feels presumptuous, lower review-rate); too late and the experience has faded (also lower review-rate). Two hours is the "evening of the day the work happened" sweet spot for typical-hours residential trades. **Trigger to revisit:** if the conversion rate on the manual-send path (which is immediate) significantly beats the 2-hour auto path, the delay may be wrong for some industries; the `gbp_review_requests.sent_at` + `resulted_in_review_id` columns make the comparison queryable once volume warrants. Also revisit per-client: a 24/7 emergency electrician's job-completion at 3am should NOT fire an SMS at 5am; a quiet-hours guard (using the client's `notification_preferences` quiet hours, which doesn't exist as a per-client column today) would replace the flat 2 hours with "first daytime hour ≥ +2h". Out of scope V1; flag if a customer reports late-night SMS complaints.
- **GBP V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** (1) **One GBP location per client** — `client_gbp_locations` is UNIQUE on `client_id`. A multi-location electrician running two suburbs needs the unique loosened + a `primary` flag; defer until a real customer hits the constraint. (2) **No GBP Posts** — `createPost` is a fast-fail stub in `client.ts`. Local posts are a V1.1 add — useful for SEO once basic review automation is proven. (3) **No insights/analytics view** — `getInsights` stubbed too. The views/searches/actions numbers are a dashboard polish pass after V1 proves out. (4) **No auto-generated review replies** — every reply is human. AI-drafted replies could land in V1.1 but only behind explicit "Draft → operator approves → publish" UX (auto-publishing AI replies on customer reviews is a credibility footgun). (5) **Review pull is poll-only** — daily `pg_cron` at 06:00 UTC + on-demand "Sync now". GBP push notifications aren't reliable enough to depend on. (6) **Attribution window = 7 days** — review-request `resulted_in_review_id` link is set only when a review arrives within 7 days of a sent request; longer-window reviews are almost always unprompted. (7) **No "did the link get clicked" wiring yet** — `gbp_review_requests.clicked_at` is in the schema but unwritten in V1 (would need link-tracking through a redirect service). UI displays it as a sentinel when a future session wires it.

- **Wizard field enhancement — accept/reject preview, not auto-replace.** `components/shared/EnhanceableTextarea` shows the AI-enhanced version as a preview card with "Use this →" / "Keep mine" buttons; nothing replaces the user's wording until they explicitly accept. The earlier `CreateClientModal` offer enhance was auto-replace (the polished text overwrote the textarea immediately, with no preview gate); both the offer and the `funnel_customer_pain` fields now flow through the new component. Rationale: AI enhancement on a wizard brief field is **specificity drawing-out**, not blind rewriting — the operator's wording is the ground truth and the enhanced version is a suggestion they should be able to evaluate against the original. Auto-replace loses the operator's input the moment they click; even if they undo via the textarea's history, the recovery is friction-heavy and a hostile-to-trust UX for "I tried it once and the AI ate my words." Accept/reject costs one extra click on the happy path and preserves agency on the unhappy one. **Trigger to revisit:** if telemetry shows operators almost always accept (>90%) the cost of the extra click starts to outweigh the agency benefit — but telemetry like that doesn't exist yet, so the conservative default stands.

- **Two enhance routes (`/api/enhance-offer` + `/api/enhance-field`) — kept as siblings, not merged.** Both Sonnet-backed, same fallback contract. The offer route's system prompt is a direct-response copywriter polishing offer-paragraph copy for a conversion funnel (the Suby/Sultanic framing). The field route's system prompt is a research-grade copywriter interviewing the owner to draw out specificity (generic across freeform brief fields). The framings genuinely differ — the offer route would be too punchy for a thin pain-moment description, and the field route would be too tentative for an offer paragraph. **Trigger to revisit:** if both prompts converge as we tune them and the offer-specific bits collapse into the generic one, merge — but only after at least a third field shows the field-route framing fits universally. Until then, two routes is the honest answer.

- **Automation overlap / anti-spam suppression rules — DONE (Phase 8 · Session 4).** Shipped as `lib/automations/suppression.ts` + migration `0083`. Three dimensions, evaluated INSIDE `processNextAction` before every comm action dispatches:
  1. **Frequency cap** — hardcoded V1: `FREQUENCY_CAP_HOURLY=1`, `FREQUENCY_CAP_DAILY=3` per channel per recipient. Read directly against the existing `sms_messages` + `email_messages` send logs (filtered by `related_lead_id` + window + `status != 'failed'`; email also filters `direction=outbound`). Fail-open on count error — a mis-read must not silently drop a customer-facing message. No separate `messaging_events` table — the Phase 7 send logs are the source of truth.
  2. **Quiet hours** — per-client window on `clients.quiet_hours_{start,end,timezone}` (storage decision resolved per CLAUDE.md AskUserQuestion). Inside the window the action **defers** (re-enqueues at end-of-window via `enqueueJob` with `runAfter`) rather than skips — a quiet-hours customer never silently misses the message, just gets it at 08:00 instead of 03:00. Wrap-midnight windows supported (end < start). Pure helper `computeQuietHoursWindow` uses `Intl.DateTimeFormat` for IANA TZ resolution — no `tz`/`luxon` dep added. Operator UI: `QuietHoursSection` on sub-account `/settings/notifications`.
  3. **Priority cancellation** — hardcoded by `trigger_type` (resolved decision): 1=transactional (`payment_failed`, `job_completed`, `job_scheduled`, `job_status_changed`), 2=nurture (`lead_created`, `lead_inactive`), 3=reputation (detected by `automation_key.startsWith('review_request_')` since reputation rides on `job_completed`). When `onTrigger` creates a higher-priority run, `cancelLowerPriorityRuns` flips lower-priority running/paused runs on the same lead to `status='cancelled'`. Same-priority runs are NOT cancelled — they fall through to the frequency cap.
  Every decision writes to `automation_suppression_log` (`reason` enum: `frequency_cap_hourly` / `frequency_cap_daily` / `quiet_hours` / `priority_cancelled`; `deferred_until` populated for `quiet_hours`; `context` jsonb carries the why). Internal actions (`send_operator_notification`, `wait_for_duration`, `update_lead_field`, `create_followup_task`) are NEVER suppressed — they're internal system mechanics, not customer-facing. **Operator notification flooding** is controlled separately via `notification_preferences.digest_frequency` (per Phase 7 Resend) — that is the right knob, not the suppression layer.
  **Trigger to revisit:** if operators report customers complaining about messaging frequency, lower `FREQUENCY_CAP_DAILY`; if operators want per-client tuning, promote frequency caps to `agency_policy` keys (the `automationDefaults` slot in `PolicyValueMap` was reserved for this). Quiet hours could become an agency-policy default with per-client override too — same pattern as `defaultSeatLimit`. **Webnua-as-sub-account** (CLAUDE.md): no special-casing — the quiet-hours read is per-`clients.id`, indistinguishable across tenants.

- ~~**Booking creation / reschedule / recurring write flows — DEFERRED (Phase 3).**~~ **Resolved (Phase 3b).** All three booking-write flows are now wired to live writes (the booking *status* mutations were already done in Phase 3):
  - **Reschedule** — `useRescheduleBooking` (`lib/bookings/queries.tsx`) `UPDATE`s `starts_at`/`ends_at`; `RescheduleModal` carries native date/time inputs seeded from the booking, and the `was`/`now` compare cards are computed (was from the booking, now live from the form). The date/timestamp maths lives in `lib/bookings/time.ts` (`composeTimestamp` + siblings — wall-clock-in-UTC, matching the calendar's UTC accessors).
  - **New booking** — `useCreateBooking` resolves the picked customer (inserting a `customers` row for a quick-add) then INSERTs `bookings`. `NewBookingModal` is a controlled form (job title, `CustomerPicker`, native date/time, service, price, notes). `AddBookingButton` resolves the target client — a client books their own, an operator books the active sub-account, and agency mode disables the button until a client is picked.
  - **Recurring** — `useCreateRecurringSchedule` INSERTs one `recurring_booking_schedules` row + a rolling window of ~10 concrete `bookings`. `computeOccurrences` projects the visit window; `checkRecurringConflicts` overlap-checks it against existing bookings. `/recurring/new` is a controlled form with a live preview, and `ConflictModal` is data-driven from the real overlap result (skip the clashing visits, or cancel).
  - **Customer model** — `CustomerPicker` (`shared/bookings/`) + `useCustomerSearch` (`lib/customers/queries.tsx`, RLS- + per-client-scoped `ilike` lookup; filter-syntax chars stripped). The picker hands back a `SelectedCustomer` (existing id, or a new one the write flow inserts). `useClientId` (`lib/clients/queries.tsx`) resolves a client slug → UUID.
  - Removed in this pass: the `new-booking-modal.tsx` / `RecurringCustomerHeader` stubs; `recurring-setup.tsx` + `conflict-modal.tsx` trimmed to live shapes; `voltlineRecurring`/`voltlineConflict` deleted.
  - **Still a display stub:** the reschedule SMS preview (no messaging backend). **Still deferred:** a top-up job to extend the recurring window past the seeded ~10 bookings.


- **Funnel publish + approval lane — DONE (A3 + Session 4 unpublish).** The funnel publish lane is wired in parity with the website lane (`lib/funnel/mutations.ts` Lane A `publishFunnelDraft` + Lane B `submitFunnelForApproval` / `approveFunnelSubmission` / `rejectFunnelSubmission` / `recallFunnelSubmission` + Session-4 `unpublishFunnel`; `lib/funnel/queries.tsx` publish-state hooks; `lib/funnel/preflight.ts`; the `/funnels/[id]/review` surface; the operator approvals queue on `/tickets`; Realtime via migration 0046). **Session 4 added `unpublishFunnel(funnelId, actor)`** — pulls a live funnel offline by clearing `funnels.published_version_id` and archiving the previously-live `funnel_version` row (notes carry "Unpublished by X on Y" so the history still renders the row but marked archived). Refuses while a pending approval submission is in flight (returns `{ ok: false, reason: 'pending_submission' }` so the operator resolves the queue first). UI: a contextual button on the right side of `FunnelSlugEditor` (the Public URL row on `/funnels/[id]`) — "Unpublish" when live, "Publish →" (linking to `/funnels/[id]/review`) when draft-only. Operator-only (`role === 'admin'` + `publish` cap); the destructive `ConfirmDialog` lives inside `FunnelSlugEditor`. **Three deliberate divergences from the website lane** — each is a structural difference between websites and funnels, not an omission:
  1. **No force-publish.** The website `ForcePublishMenu` is admin break-glass to skip *preflight blockers*. `force_publish_audit_log` is website-keyed (`website_id NOT NULL`, FK to `websites`) — a funnel force-publish row can't be written without a schema change, which is adjacent to the A1-flagged tenant-check gap. And a funnel is operator-managed (the operator IS the content authority), so a funnel preflight blocker is the operator's own to fix. Funnel publish has no break-glass path. **Future session:** if funnels ever need force-publish, extend `force_publish_audit_log` (nullable `website_id` + a `funnel_id`) and generalise `ForcePublishMenu` to a target union.
  2. **The approval queue is one shared "Approvals" tab.** The `/tickets` approvals tab renders website submissions (`WebsiteApprovalRow`) then funnel submissions (`FunnelApprovalRow`); the count is the sum. Not a separate funnel queue page.
  3. **No commit-message / scheduled-publish fields.** The "publish modal" the A3 brief imagined doesn't exist for websites either — the website publish is a *review surface* (`/website/review`), not a modal, and captures no commit message or scheduled-publish time. The funnel review surface mirrors that: a preflight checklist + a Publish / Submit action, no extra fields.
- **Funnel autosave** was already wired in Session 7 (a funnel-keyed `DraftSlot`); A3 did not change it.

- ~~**Wizard preview (`FunnelLandingPreview`) ≠ funnel editor preview.**~~ **Resolved** — Session 7 (the wizard refactor): `FunnelLandingPreview` + `FunnelPreviewState` + the `previewAfter*` snapshots are deleted. The wizard's Step 5 (`/clients/new/draft`) is a wizard-frame `SectionEditor` walk (`WizardSectionEditor`) rendering the section registry's per-section `<Preview>` components — one preview implementation platform-wide. The wizard now produces an editable `Funnel`; steps 1-4 are single-column Q&A forms, the trust step triggers `generateFunnelStub`. See `builder-design.md §5`. **Still deferred:** the wizard does not yet fold its Q&A answers into a real `GenerationContext` (the stub generation ignores them — same as Session 6's specifics/avoid), and funnel publish/preflight is unbuilt (see the funnel-publish parked item above).

- **Agency vs sub-account two-tier model — `/settings/access`, `/website`, `/dashboard` are the references (Phase 6 · Cluster 5–6).** GoHighLevel-style. Workspace context driven by `lib/workspace/workspace-stub.tsx` and switched via `AdminClientPicker`. **Agency mode** = cross-client birds-eye for triage. **Sub-account mode** = drill into one client to make changes. `/settings/access` (Cluster 5 · Session 1b) and `/website` (Cluster 5 · Session 3) are built native against this — agency mode shows a cross-client overview; sub-account mode renders the active client's content. **Cluster 6 · Session 1a added the third reference: `/dashboard`** — `app/dashboard/page.tsx` dispatches on `useIsAgencyMode()`, agency mode → the cross-client roster (`AdminDashboardContent`), sub-account mode → the single-client overview hub. **The state-driven dispatch pattern (branch on `useIsAgencyMode()` inside the route, no URL change) now has three precedent points — it is the settled platform pattern; a future fourth surface adopts it, it does not get re-decided.** Their agency-level cross-client matrices live at `/settings/access` (agency view) and `/websites` (admin-only). **Surfaces still agency-only that need sub-account variants when next touched:** `/automations` (admin roster — inline groups don't scale past ~5 clients), `/campaigns` (admin roster — same), `/leads` (admin cross-client inbox is correct as triage; but editing/managing a specific lead should land you in sub-account), `/calendar` (cross-client overview correct as triage; booking-edit work should be sub-account), `/reviews` (per-client cards is OK as a hybrid). **Don't refactor the legacy agency-only roster surfaces now** — adopt the pattern surface-by-surface as scope reaches each one. **Cluster 8** formalised the model — see the `## Agency / sub-account model` section near the top: layered resolution, the closed policy-key union, and `/settings/*` joining the mode-dispatch pattern. **Cluster 9** added the plan layer: the `lib/billing/` plan catalog (Layer 2.5 of the resolution stack), the agency `/settings/plans` catalog editor, and `/settings/billing` sub-account mode (plan assignment + resolved bundle).

- **Auth + capability mechanism — real Supabase Auth (DONE).** User resolution, sign-in, and capability grants are all real Supabase: `user-stub.tsx` (misnamed — see its inventory entry) resolves from `supabase.auth` → `public.users` → `capability_grants`; `app/(auth)/login` is a real `signInWithPassword` screen; `<UserProvider>` in `app/layout.tsx` is the real provider. **`DevRoleSwitcher` is deleted**; view-as / user-switching / the four stub users are gone. The agency-policy + billing + invite + roster stores (`lib/agency/*`, `lib/billing/*`, `lib/invites/*`, `lib/auth/roster-store.ts`) hydrate from Supabase via `DataHydrationProvider` (`lib/data/DataHydrationProvider.tsx`, mounted in the root layout — `hydrateClients()` first, then the rest in parallel, re-run on every `onAuthStateChange`). `app/dev/` is down to just `/dev/sections`. The capability layer (`capabilities.ts` / `explainers.ts` / `resolver.ts`) is product code, unchanged. **Editor publish/draft/approval family — also Supabase-wired (PR #41).** `publish-stub.ts` + `draft-stub.ts` deleted; `audit-stub.ts` + `website-approval-stub.ts` collapsed to type-only display modules; `content-drafts.ts` + `queries.tsx` + `mutations.ts` + `snapshot.ts` + `builder-events.ts` are the live Supabase layer; `use-autosave.ts` upserts `content_drafts` rows; `use-publish-state.ts` is a re-export shim over `queries.tsx`. **Owed:** a deliberate cross-tenant RLS validation pass — the policies have not been systematically negative-tested with real `auth.uid()`s across tenants.
- **`app/dev/` convention — off-nav developer utilities.** Routes under `src/app/dev/*` are off-nav dev tools. Only **`/dev/sections`** remains (the section-registry × brand inspector); `/dev/capabilities`, `/dev/generation-preview`, and `/dev/agency-policy` were removed. Don't add user-facing pages here; don't link to `/dev/*` from production nav.

- **Explainer strings assume the Webnua managed-service relationship.** `src/lib/auth/explainers.ts` hardcodes "your operator" / "your account" in every `disable`-mode tooltip and `request`-mode label. Fine for V1 (single-operator platform). If multi-operator deploys land later (white-label, agency reseller, etc.), swap the hardcoded strings for an `{operatorLabel}` token resolved per workspace before the strings get embedded into hundreds of `<CapabilityGate>` calls downstream. Flag the moment a second deploy scenario shows up.

- **Workspace-governance capabilities (billing, team management, client deletion) are not in the 13-cap builder model.** The capability layer covers page-builder access only; org-governance actions live outside it. This is why the team-invite `PermissionPreview` shows owner and operator as identical — in the builder model they genuinely are; they diverge only on governance. Extending the cap model is **deferred**. When next revisited — likely with the backend pass or the first real billing surface — evaluate adding ~4 new caps (e.g. `manageBilling`, `manageTeam`, `deleteClient`, `viewFinancials`) and update `TEAM_ROLE_CAPABILITIES` in `lib/team/roles.ts` so owner/operator reflect their real divergence. The `PermissionPreview` parity note can then be dropped.

- **Per-client seat limit lives on `/settings/access` sub-account mode — provisional home.** The seat limit is a contract/plan axis (how many users a client's plan permits), distinct from the capability axis (`/settings/access`'s main job). It sits on `/settings/access` sub-account mode because that is the operator's only per-client management surface today — there is no standalone client-record edit surface, and inventing one was rejected as scope creep. It's rendered as a visually-distinct `SettingsSection`, separate from the capability grid, to keep the two axes from blurring. The data layer is home-agnostic: as of Cluster 8 · Session 4b the seat limit resolves through the `defaultSeatLimit` policy key (agency default + per-account override) — `lib/clients/seat-limit-stub.ts` is a thin facade over the resolver, and `AdminClient.seatLimit` has been retired. **Cluster 9 landed `/settings/billing` sub-account mode** — the seat-limit *editing control* (`ClientSeatLimitCard`) deliberately stayed on `/settings/access` (it's a per-account override, an Access concern); `/settings/billing` shows the seat limit *resolved, read-only* as part of the assigned plan's bundle. If a future revisit wants the per-account override editable from Billing too, that's a placement call to make then — not a forced move.

- **Client-internal hierarchy is flat for V1 — deferred.** Every client-invited user gets the `CLIENT_DEFAULTS` baseline; the client teammate-invite flow has no in-flow role pick (no co-owner vs member tier). The capability model doesn't currently distinguish a client-internal admin from a regular client user, and inventing a tier to match a UI shape would be the drift the operator-side Step-2 call correctly avoided. When workspace-governance caps land (see the item above), `inviteClientTeammate` becomes a real capability and the client-invite flow can gate it — at which point a client-internal role tier can be designed against a real cap, not a guessed one.

- **`funnel_testimonials` renders placeholders, never AI-generated testimonials.** The wizard captures 0–3 real customer testimonials per funnel; the AI funnel generator (wired in a later session) reads them straight onto the social-proof section. **When the list is empty, the funnel renders an explicit "Your customer reviews will appear here" placeholder** rather than asking Claude to invent quotes — fabricated testimonials are a credibility / consumer-protection foot-gun nothing else in the platform recovers from, and the placeholder is honest about what's missing. The deterministic funnel generator preserves the same behaviour. **Trigger to revisit:** when the GBP integration ships and the platform can auto-pull real Google reviews — empty `funnel_testimonials` can then resolve to real GBP entries at render time instead of a placeholder. Until then: empty = placeholder, full stop.

- **Phase 6 generation fallback policy.** On `/api/generate-site` `503` (key not configured), `site-generation-stub.ts` falls back to the deterministic stub silently — intentional for dev so the create flow works without an `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`. On `500` (real generation failure), the error is now thrown and surfaced in `CreateClientModal`'s error pane via the server's `{ name, status, detail }` body — no more invisible stub-degradation when Claude actually fails. Network throws still fall back (with a `console.warn`) so a transient connectivity blip doesn't hard-fail the flow. **Trigger to revisit:** if operators report seeing stub-quality copy in production, check `generation_log` for matching field-level fallback entries — every real generation writes one row per fallback field (see commit `feat(phase-6): write generation_log entries from generate-live.ts`).

- **Post-AI repair pipeline (Bundle A + B).** Both the website pipeline (`generation-stub.ts` `runValidationPipeline`) and the funnel pipeline (`generate-funnel-live.ts` `validateAndAssemble`) run a shared six-pass sequence on every AI-returned section before it lands in the editor: (A) theme-discard, (B) **enum validation** via `validateEnums` (substitutes invalid values with `SECTION_SHAPE_CATALOG`'s first listed value — audit caught `offer.layout='single'` in 12.5% of offers), (C) **hallucinated image-path strip** via `stripHallucinatedImages` (clears any URL that isn't `http(s)://` / `data:image/` / a known local prefix — audit found ~14-18% of image fields carrying invented `/images/x.jpg` paths), (D) **stock-image injection** via `injectStockImages` (fills empty slots from `industry-templates.ts` `stockImages` — was previously deterministic-fallback only, audit found 77.9% of heroes had empty `heroImageUrl` in production), (E) `reconcileColumns` (clamps `columns` down to `items.length` so the renderer doesn't pad an empty 4th column), (F) missing-field reporting (runs last so injected / substituted fields aren't double-flagged). Shared helpers live in `src/lib/website/generation-validation.ts` (server-safe, no `'use client'`). The strip must run BEFORE the injection so a fresh stock URL replaces the cleared hallucination, not the other way around. **`generation_log.reason` does NOT carry new enum values** — diagnostics use the existing `missing` / `invalid` plus the `modelValue` column: `invalid` + a value = substituted enum or stripped URL; `missing` + a non-null modelValue = injected stock image; `missing` + null modelValue = genuine hole. Adding a richer enum is deferred until volume warrants the migration churn. **Section module DEFAULTS are now honest** — every `withDefaults` array fallback returns `[]` (not the editor seed) so AI omissions don't leak Webnua agency pitch (offer), category-locked features ("Plumbing / HVAC / Electrical"), or fabricated stats ("500+ happy customers", "10+ years in business"). The editor's `defaultData()` still mounts representative placeholder rows (`EDITOR_SEED_*`) so an operator adding a fresh section sees the shape; only the generator's `withDefaults` path empties them. See `reference/bundle-a-b-audit.md` for the full audit with live SQL counts. **Bundle C1 extends Pass D with per-slot image diversity** — `resolveStockImage` + `injectStockImages` take an optional `{ slug, surface }` options bag. An FNV-1a hash of `${slug}:${surface}:${sectionType}:${fieldKey}` picks a stable per-slot gallery index, so a site's hero / cta / contact / about / offer slots resolve to DIFFERENT photos instead of all landing on the same fixed position (audit confirmed Lucan Landscaping's 3 about-image slots all pointing at the same hero URL, and 4 cta sections all pointing at the same `1558904541-efa843a96f01`). The `surface` token (`'site' | 'funnel'`) is the seed token that guarantees a customer's funnel hero never collides with their website hero — the funnel hero pool is gallery-only (excludes the template's headline `hero` URL), so the funnel never shows the same opener photo as the site for the same brand. Slug seed = `ctx.business?.name` for websites, `brief.businessName` for funnels; absent slug falls back to pre-C1 fixed positions (deterministic-fallback path remains unchanged when no slug is passed). The `slug:surface:section:field` hash is reference-stable across re-runs, so the same brand always picks the same photo for the same slot — no churn on re-generation. The 4-item gallery + 1 hero URL per industry remains the same; sparse-industry expansion is its own content session.

- **Phase 6 generation TypeError — RESOLVED (three commits).** Server-side `/api/generate-site` was crashing with `TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'includes')` on `def.allowedContainers` inside the registry filter. Root cause was structural: every section file under `sections/*.tsx` is `'use client'` (because it ships React Fields/Preview components), and Next's RSC bundler replaces all 'use client' exports with `registerClientReference` stubs in the server bundle — so the `SECTION_REGISTRY` array the server route imported was an array of stub functions, not real section definitions. PR #58 surfaced the masked 500 from the modal; the structural fix introduced `sections/registry-meta.ts` (no 'use client', SSOT for metadata) and switched `generation-prompt.ts` + `generation-stub.ts` to read `SECTION_REGISTRY_META`. The editor continues to read `SECTION_REGISTRY` (the full definition with Fields/Preview) — only the server consumers moved. **Round two (this commit)** caught the latent risk the first fix flagged: `fillHeaderSection` / `fillFooterSection` (the only other server-reachable functions in `generation-stub.ts`, called from the route handler to produce site chrome) were still calling `headerSection.defaultData()` / `footerSection.defaultData()` directly — same stub problem, different call site. The fix added an optional `defaultDataValues: Readonly<Record<string, unknown>>` field to `SectionMeta` (a static snapshot of the section's `defaultData()` output, populated only for `headerMeta` + `footerMeta` since they're the only server-reachable consumers today), and switched the two fill helpers to read from `getSectionMeta('header'/'footer')?.defaultDataValues`. The unused `headerSection` / `footerSection` imports in `generation-stub.ts` were removed. Three commits in total: `433d850` (introduce `SECTION_REGISTRY_META`), `c6ffaf0` (switch server consumers + section files re-import metadata), and this one (eliminate `defaultData()` call sites on the server path).

- **Section metadata server/client boundary.** Section files are `'use client'` because they ship React components. Server-side generation consumers MUST import from `sections/registry-meta.ts`, never from `sections/*.tsx` directly (or from `sections/index.ts`'s `SECTION_REGISTRY`, which transitively imports the `'use client'` modules). The `SECTION_REGISTRY_META` array is the source of truth for metadata; the full section definitions in `sections/index.ts` (`SECTION_REGISTRY` + `getSectionDefinition`) exist for the editor and other client-only consumers. **This applies to default DATA as well as metadata** — server code must never call `xxxSection.defaultData()` on a section import (those exports are client-reference stubs on the server). When a server-reachable path needs a section's defaults, populate `defaultDataValues` on that section's `*Meta` entry in `registry-meta.ts` and read from there (`getSectionMeta(type)?.defaultDataValues`). Today only `headerMeta` and `footerMeta` carry `defaultDataValues` because `fillHeaderSection` / `fillFooterSection` are the only server-reachable consumers; the other fillers (`fillHero`, `fillOffer`, etc.) live in `generation-stub.ts` but are only invoked from client-side fallback paths (`generateSync` reached from `/website/new` and the create-client modal). **Trigger to revisit:** (1) if section schemas grow large enough that the duplication-via-spread pattern (metadata in `registry-meta.ts`, `defaultData` function in the section module) becomes lossy — e.g. if the field-key list per section grows enough that drift between `defaultDataKeys` and a section's actual `DEFAULTS` becomes a maintenance problem, move the `DEFAULTS` data into `registry-meta.ts` too and have the section files import them; (2) if a new server-reachable code path needs another section's defaults, add `defaultDataValues` to that section's `*Meta` first — do NOT add `defaultData()` calls to server code.

- **Funnel-offer generator — Sonnet 4.6 (not Opus), editable after generation.** The four-field funnel offer (`/api/generate-offer`) uses Sonnet rather than Opus: the task is short, structured, well-prompt-able copy — `headline ≤12 words`, `promise ≤25`, `risk-reversal ≤15`, `cta ≤6` — Sonnet handles this fluently and Opus pricing is not justified for ~150 output tokens. **Trigger to revisit:** if operators report Sonnet drafts losing the brief's specifics (treating "burst pipe at 9pm" as generic), or repeatedly using banned filler ("comprehensive", "leverage", etc.) the prompt explicitly forbids, escalate to Opus and keep the same prompt. The 13-rule prompt + the explicit ban list should make Sonnet competent here; Opus is a fallback, not a default. **Editable-after-generation UX:** the wizard renders the four fields as editable inputs the moment the call returns — user can accept, edit any field, or regenerate. The justification is recovery: if Sonnet drifts on any single field, edit takes seconds; if we made the offer non-editable, the only recovery would be regenerating the entire thing or fixing it later in the editor. **Trigger to revisit:** if telemetry shows operators rarely edit (≤10% touch any field), reconsider making it non-editable to reduce decision fatigue — but that requires telemetry we do not yet collect. Until then, editable is the safe default.

- **Funnel vs offer generator model choice — Opus on funnel, Sonnet on offer.** The two AI-generation entry points the wizard runs split deliberately on model. **Offer** (`/api/generate-offer`) uses **Sonnet 4.6**: four short structured strings (~150 output tokens total) — Opus is overkill, and the field-level editable-after-generation UX means a drift is recoverable in-flow. **Funnel** (`/api/generate-funnel`) uses **Opus 4.7**: seven full sections of conversion copy in one structured response, the section copy lands directly into the published draft (no field-by-field accept gate), and the funnel is the actual money-conversion surface — quality matters more than per-call cost. Same `503` → deterministic-fallback shape; same `500` → `AppError` unmasking; same `generation_log` observability. **Trigger to revisit:** if Opus latency on the funnel call exceeds operator tolerance during the in-modal generation phase (sustained > 60s P95), or if Sonnet starts handling extended-thinking conversion copy at the same quality bar Opus does today, evaluate dropping the funnel to Sonnet — but keep the model id behind a single `MODEL` const in `generate-funnel-live.ts`, not behind a feature flag. **Anthropic constraints — two different thinking shapes:** Opus 4.7 only accepts `thinking: { type: 'adaptive' }` (no `budget_tokens`); passing `{ type: 'enabled', budget_tokens: N }` returns a 400 `"thinking.type.enabled" is not supported for this model. Use \"thinking.type.adaptive\"…`. Sonnet 4.6 still supports `{ type: 'enabled', budget_tokens }` — and when used, requires `max_tokens > budget_tokens` or returns a 400 `invalid_request_error` (the offer route's original `max_tokens: 2000 / budget: 2000` hit this; fix was `max_tokens: 4000`). New routes must match the constraint to the model: adaptive on Opus, enabled+budget (with `max_tokens > budget`) on Sonnet.

- **Prompt-content fixes for reported symptoms — applied directly to website + funnel prompts.** Three reported generation-quality symptoms — (1) funnel copy mostly blank except headlines, (2) `headlineAccent` / `titleAccent` duplicated with the headline rather than treated as a second-line accent, (3) layout drift (left-align when center expected; missing icons) — were addressed in `src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts` + `src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts` by adding three pieces of content: a per-section `SECTION_SHAPE_CATALOG` that documents variant-key enum values + item-array element object shapes; a `SHARED_FIELD_NOTES` block emitted in both prompts that explains the heading-accent semantic, lists the 74 curated icon ids, declares the item-id rule, and explains the `theme` object shape; and reinforcing bullets in each prompt's "Rules:" list. The semantic for `headlineAccent` is **an optional SECOND LINE in the accent colour beneath the headline**, NOT a substring of the headline (the section modules' in-editor helper "Optional second line — rendered in the brand accent colour." is the source of truth; the original task brief had this wrong). The offer (`/api/generate-offer`) and enhance (`/api/enhance-field` + `/api/enhance-offer`) prompts were NOT touched — none of the three symptoms implicated them. **Trigger to revisit:** if the same three symptoms recur after this fix, the next step is worked-example shots (a fully-populated section JSON inline in the system prompt) — the catalog approach taken here is the lighter-weight option. Subsequent prompt-quality sessions should address the other audit findings (banned-word consolidation, copy-vs-layout via `capabilityHints`, voice on offer/enhance, shared base persona).

- **Offer pricing — model cannot invent prices; runtime safeguard retries once on detection.** Two layers in `src/app/api/generate-offer/route.ts`: (1) the system prompt carries explicit guidance — when the brief carries no price, use qualitative language ("honest upfront pricing", "free quote, no obligation", "fixed-price quote on the spot") instead of inventing a number; a specific dollar / euro / pound figure may appear ONLY if the operator's brief contains that exact figure; (2) after the first Claude call returns, a `PRICE_PATTERN` regex (currency symbols next to a digit, or a number followed by a currency word — "dollars", "euros", "GBP", etc.) scans all four returned fields. If a price appears in the output AND no price was in the brief, the route retries ONCE with a stronger no-pricing instruction prepended to the user message. Cap is one retry per call — no retry storms. If the retry also invents a price, the retry result is shipped with a `console.warn` (no better option; the user can edit any field in the wizard). **Observability is console-only** — the `generation_log` table requires `client_id` (NOT NULL), but offer generation runs BEFORE the client row exists, so the route can't write there (matches the existing `generate-seo` / `enhance-offer` / `enhance-field` precedent). **Trigger to revisit:** if retries fail repeatedly across operators (visible only via the second `console.warn` in production logs), escalate to surfacing `AppError` in the wizard so the operator sees what happened, or wire a separate observability sink (e.g. a `generation_diagnostics` table without the `client_id` constraint).

- **Section themes — brand defaults apply via renderer; model does not output theme.** Sections occasionally rendered with text colour matching the background, making content invisible. Root cause: the model picked `theme` values per section that didn't have guaranteed contrast against the section's text colour. Three layers of fix: (1) the model is explicitly told NOT to emit a `theme` field — `SHARED_FIELD_NOTES` (`src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`) opens with a "Section themes" appendix explaining themes are applied automatically by the renderer from the brand palette; the website + funnel system prompts each carry an explicit "Do NOT output a `theme` field" rule in their "Rules:" lists; the previous "Theme objects" appendix is removed and `theme` no longer appears in the variant-keys hint list; (2) the funnel system prompts' "Populate only `theme`, `eyebrow`, `heading`" form-section rule is now "Populate only `eyebrow`, `heading`" (the renderer themes the form section too); (3) defence in depth — the validation pipeline (`runValidationPipeline` in `generation-stub.ts` and `validateAndAssemble` in `generate-funnel-live.ts`) discards any model-emitted `theme` value before the section lands in the editor. The discard is logged as a `FallbackLogEntry` with `reason: 'invalid'` and `fieldName: 'theme'` so the website route's `generation_log` writer can track whether the model is still emitting theme after the prompt change. **Trigger to revisit:** if `generation_log` entries with `field_name='theme'` and `reason='invalid'` show the model still emitting theme at meaningful rates, harden the prompt further (worked-example shots showing a section JSON without a `theme` key). If branded sections feel visually monotonous because every section uses the same brand-default colours, introduce a small per-section variant enum (e.g. `surface: 'primary' | 'secondary' | 'neutral' | 'dark'`) the model can choose from instead of restoring full theme freedom — the renderer would still map each enum value to a known-contrast pair from the brand palette.

- **Worked examples — all four AI generation prompts use the same fictional anchor business (Voltline Electrical, residential electrical contractor in Perth coastal suburbs — Cottesloe, Mosman Park, Claremont; owner Mark, 15 years on the tools; differentiators are fixed-quote pricing and same-day emergency response).** The website prompt (`src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`) carries a six-section home page; the funnel step-1 system prompt (`src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts`) carries an eight-section lead-capture page in the Suby/Sultanic + FAQ order; the funnel step-2 system prompt carries a four-section qualification page; the offer prompt (`src/app/api/generate-offer/route.ts`) carries a complete four-field offer; the enhance-field prompt (`src/app/api/enhance-field/route.ts`) carries a before/after pair for the `funnel_customer_pain` field. The example is shared deliberately so the model sees a consistent standard across the whole generation pipeline, and each example carries an explicit "do NOT copy these specifics" guard at the end. Every JSON example was validated against the section-type registry (`SECTION_REGISTRY_META`) + the curated 74-icon vocabulary (`section-icons.ts`) before commit — section types, icon ids, and variant enum values all resolve cleanly. **Trigger to revisit:** if generated output starts to resemble Voltline's specifics (Perth coastal suburbs, electrician, 2-hour response, "Mark", EC10437, named suburbs) for non-electrician briefs, the model is over-indexing on the example and the examples should be diversified across multiple trades (e.g. a plumber example for the funnel step-2 prompt, a cleaner example for the website prompt). Until that telemetry appears, a single shared anchor is the higher-leverage choice — it teaches the quality bar once rather than diluting it across five mediocre examples.

- **Copy vs layout field separation in generation prompts.** The website + funnel prompts split each section's `defaultDataKeys` into a COPY bucket and a LAYOUT bucket using `SectionMeta.capabilityHints.copyFields` as the authoritative source (with a name-based heuristic fallback for any future section type that ships without hints — see `partitionFields` in `src/lib/website/generation-prompt.ts`). The per-section catalog entry lists copy fields first under "Copy fields (populate with specific, on-brand content):" and layout fields second under "Layout fields (omit unless the brief specifically requires a variation — defaults apply):". The main rules in both the cached website system prompt (`src/lib/website/generate-live.ts`) and both funnel system prompts (`src/lib/website/generate-funnel-live.ts`) were reworded to match: populate every COPY field; do NOT specify a LAYOUT field unless the brief justifies a variation. Also: both funnel system prompts now carry an explicit "do NOT output a `fields` array on the form section" instruction in the form section's section-plan brief (the form's `fields[]` is built deterministically in code and was already discarded by `validateAndAssemble`, but the prompt now says so up front so the model doesn't waste tokens drafting an array that will be thrown away). **Trigger to revisit:** if the model consistently fails to specify a layout variation that would improve a page (operators reporting consistently centred or consistently left-aligned output when the page wanted the other), soften the omit-unless-required language or let the model choose for specific sections — but only after telemetry, not by guess. The opposite failure (model invents layout variations the brief doesn't justify) was the symptom this change targets; the change should make that strictly less likely. Cross-check with `generation_log` "missing" entries on layout keys — a sharp rise after this change is the expected signature; a sharp rise on copy keys would mean the partition is mis-classifying and would justify reopening.

- **Funnel lead threading uses ?lead=<id> URL parameter from step 1 to step 2.** `/api/forms/submit` returns `{ ok: true, leadId }` on a new-lead insert. `FormBlock`'s `handlePublicSubmit` reads `leadId` off the response and — when `form.afterSubmit.kind === 'nextStep'` — appends `?lead=<leadId>` to `publicSubmit.nextStepHref` before redirecting. On step 2's mount the same `FormBlock` reads `?lead=` from `window.location.search` (UUID-validated against `UUID_RE`) and posts it as `existingLeadId` on the next submit. The route validates: must be a syntactic UUID (malformed → 400); must resolve to a lead with the same `clientId` posted in the body (cross-tenant guard — wrong-client and not-found collapse to one 400 message so neither leaks lead existence). **C3 V1 — per-funnel guard tightened (FIX D)**: the existing-lead select now reads `source_funnel_id`; when the request carries a funnel id AND the lead already carries one, the two must match (mismatch → same generic 400). When the lead's `source_funnel_id` is NULL the route heals forward (sets it to the current request's funnel id) — a one-time write that closes the previous gap where a website lead could be appended to from any funnel. The cross-tenant `client_id` check is unchanged. **Trigger to revisit:** if users complain about lost step-2 data, check whether the URL parameter is being stripped — likely culprits are an aggressive referrer policy on the funnel domain, a browser extension stripping query params, or a custom step-2 redirect rule between step 1's submit and step 2's render. The parameter is **the only** mechanism stitching the two submissions; nothing else (cookie / localStorage / server session) carries the link today. A more robust alternative — a short-lived signed cookie set at the submit endpoint — is the next step if the URL approach breaks in practice. The `?lead=` value is a server-generated UUID and is rate-limited at 8 submits/IP/min, but it does ride the URL bar; treat it as a low-secrecy session token, not a stable identifier.
- **Funnel analytics gaps that remain after lead threading — RESOLVED for the rollup + filter shape, partly deferred for attribution and reconciliation.** This was the original audit punchlist; the resolved-vs-deferred split is:
  - **Rollup step-granularity — RESOLVED (migration 0042).** `analytics_funnel_daily` now keys on `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label, page_ref)`; step-1 and step-2 `page_view` / `form_start` / `form_submit` rows are distinct. `fetchFunnelStepBreakdown(surfaceId, pageRefs)` reads the per-step axis; surfaced on `/funnels/[id]` per prototype Screen 23.
  - **`lead_status` enum stays as it is — deliberately.** Adding a `partial` / `qualified` value was the original proposed close; it was rejected once the operator-facing framing landed ("every lead is a lead — completion is a filter axis, not a quality grade"). Completion is derived at read time from `lead_events` (`deriveCompletion` in `lib/leads/queries.tsx`); the `LeadCompletion` field is surfaced on the row records for the future automation engine's read but is not exposed as a user-facing inbox filter (the user-facing axis is `source_kind` instead — see below). Persisting completion as a column was considered and rejected — the derivation is cheap, lead_events is already in the inbox select, and the column would need a refresh path on every `form_submitted` insert. Revisit only if query cost becomes a problem (e.g. operator dashboards filter on completion at scale).
  - **Inbox source column — RESOLVED (different axis than originally planned).** The original Session B plan added a `LeadCompletionFilter` (in-progress vs completed) to the inbox; that filter was sunset on operator feedback ("Google Analytics isn't the framing — we track in-app — and the operator cares about *where the lead came from*, not how far through the funnel they got"). The replacement is a categorical Source column on every inbox row (website / funnel / meta) backed by the new `leads.source_kind` column (migration 0043) — surfaced via `LeadSourcePill`. `meta` is reserved for the Meta lead-ads integration. The `LeadCompletion` derivation stays in code for the automation engine; the inbox just doesn't filter on it. `LeadCompletionFilter.tsx` was deleted.
  - **Drop-off detection — partly resolved (the read-time signal), execution worker still deferred.** `isLeadDroppedOff(events)` returns true for a lead with only one `form_submitted` older than `LEAD_DROP_OFF_HOURS` (24h V1). This is what the future automation engine reads to decide whether to fire a follow-up nudge — but no scheduled worker currently calls it. The hook is here; the cron is Phase 8 work (automation execution engine — see the "Automation overlap / anti-spam suppression rules" parked decision).
  - **Funnel-to-lead attribution — RESOLVED (migration 0044).** `leads.source_funnel_id` (nullable FK to `funnels`, set-null on delete) is now written by `/api/forms/submit` for every funnel submission — the public renderer threads the funnel UUID through `PublicFormSubmit.funnelId` → POST body → cross-tenant-guarded insert. `getBookedFromFunnelCount` runs a real count (`source_funnel_id = funnelId` + `status in ('booked', 'completed')` + capture window) and the funnel-detail hero "booked from this funnel" tile renders live numbers instead of `—`. See "Funnel-to-lead attribution" below for the resolved entry.
  - **Editor test-submit attribution — RESOLVED (C3 V1 · FIX E).** `FormTestSubmitContext` + `CreateLeadInput` now carry an optional `funnelId`; `SectionEditor` passes `mode.funnel.id` when the editor mode is `funnelStep`; `submitLead` writes `source_funnel_id` for funnel test-submits. Test leads now attribute to their funnel rather than landing as `source_funnel_id = NULL`, so the funnel-detail "booked from this funnel" count is not polluted by editor-driven test data.
  - **`leads.submission_id`** is written but never read — same as before; reconciliation job is still deferred. Not blocking anything visible today.
- **Website-side analytics aggregation closed (migrations 0040 + 0041); funnel rollup step-granularity closed by migration 0042.** Migrations 0040 + 0041 close the analytics-audit §3 / §4 website-side gaps: `form_abandon` rolls into `form_abandoned`, scroll thresholds at 25 / 50 / 75 / 90 each roll into a distinct stage (50% kept as the canonical `engaged` label so existing read-layer + dashboard surfaces stay wired with zero migration on the consumer side), and per-CTA click distinction is preserved via an `element_label` column on `analytics_funnel_daily` extending the PK to `(surface_id, day, stage, element_label)`. Two implementation-shape decisions: **(1) scroll-stage naming** — `engaged` (50%) deliberately keeps its existing name rather than being renamed to `scrolled_50`, because every existing consumer of `SurfaceFunnelTotals.engaged` (dashboard conversion funnel, hub funnel bars) already trusts that stage; the new thresholds are `scrolled_25 / scrolled_75 / scrolled_90` and pair cleanly. Re-evaluate the naming inconsistency only if a third surface needs to iterate every threshold from a single key list. **(2) per-element click rollup approach** — Option A (extend the rollup PK with `element_label`; non-click stages write `''`) over Option B (separate per-element rollup table). One table, one read path; `fetchSurfaceFunnelTotals` keeps working because summing across element_label rows produces the same per-stage count when consumers don't care about the label, and the new `fetchSurfaceClickBreakdown` reads the same table filtered to `stage = 'cta_click'` for the top-N. **§2.2 funnel rollup step-granularity — RESOLVED (migration 0042).** Same chosen shape as the element_label approach: extend the existing rollup PK with `page_ref` (empty-string sentinel matches the element_label convention), rather than introduce a separate per-step rollup table. The pre-aggregation read paths (`fetchSurfaceFunnelTotals`) continue to work — summing across `page_ref` rows reproduces the pre-migration per-stage totals, so "total form submits across the funnel" surfaces don't break; the new per-step read uses `fetchFunnelStepBreakdown(surfaceId, pageRefs)`. The dashboard's conversion-funnel and hub bars stay as-is (per-client aggregate, not per-step); per-step rendering lives on `/funnels/[id]` per prototype Screen 23. **Trigger to revisit:** the prototype's step-3 footer rows (SMS SENT / SHOWED UP / NO-SHOW) are not funnel-tracker data — they need a bookings-side read keyed to a thanks-step `page_ref` lookup that doesn't exist yet. Adding them is its own follow-up, not blocked on schema.

- **Funnel-to-lead attribution — RESOLVED (migration 0044).** `leads.source_funnel_id uuid` (nullable, FK to `public.funnels`, `on delete set null`) is now the attribution column. Written at lead creation in `/api/forms/submit` when `surfaceKind === 'funnel'` and a `funnelId` body field is present (cross-tenant guard: the funnel must belong to the posted `clientId`); website submissions leave it NULL. The public renderer threads it through cleanly — `PublicSiteRenderer` takes a `funnelId` prop on the `funnel` case (sourced from `resolveSite`'s `tracking.surfaceId`), which lands on the `publicSubmit` context's `funnelId` field; `FormBlock` includes it in the POST body. `getBookedFromFunnelCount` (`lib/analytics/queries.tsx`) runs the real query: one count over `leads` filtered by `source_funnel_id = funnelId` + `status in ('booked', 'completed')` + `created_at` within the window (default 7-day matching the funnel hero's "Funnel performance · 7 days"; the optional `dateRange` parameter overrides). The funnel-detail hero "booked from this funnel" tile renders live numbers. Leads created before this migration carry NULL and are correctly excluded. **Editor test-submit attribution is wired (C3 V1 · FIX E)** — `FormTestSubmitContext` + `CreateLeadInput` carry an optional `funnelId`; `SectionEditor` passes `mode.funnel.id` when the editor mode is `funnelStep`; `submitLead` writes `source_funnel_id` on funnel test-submits. Test leads from a funnel preview now record `source_kind = 'funnel'` AND `source_funnel_id = <the-funnel-uuid>` so the funnel-detail "booked from this funnel" count attributes correctly.

- **Funnel lead completion state — derived at read time, not persisted.** `LeadCompletion` (`'in_progress' | 'completed'`) is derived in `lib/leads/queries.tsx#deriveCompletion` by counting `form_submitted` events on a lead's `lead_events` timeline (≥2 → completed, else in-progress). NOT a persisted column on `leads` — the derivation is cheap, `lead_events` is already in the inbox select, and a persisted column would need a refresh path on every `form_submitted` insert. NOT a user-facing lead label / quality grade either — operators see "Leads captured: N" as the headline metric (analytics-audit §5.1); the completion field is for the inbox filter ("Show only leads still in progress" → still actionable for a follow-up nudge) and for the future automation engine's read. **Trigger to revisit:** if a dashboard surface needs to filter by completion at high cardinality (≥10k leads) and the per-row derivation becomes a query-cost concern, persist it as a column and refresh from a `lead_events` `AFTER INSERT` trigger. Not warranted today.

- **24-hour drop-off threshold for funnel runs is a V1 choice.** `LEAD_DROP_OFF_HOURS = 24` in `lib/leads/queries.tsx` is the threshold `isLeadDroppedOff(events)` uses to classify a single-`form_submitted` lead as "dropped" rather than "still in progress" — read by future automation logic (the "send a follow-up nudge" decision; Phase 8). The inbox filter does NOT use this threshold (a step-1-only lead is "in progress" regardless of age — the filter is about operator action, not lead quality, so age doesn't change the framing). **Trigger to revisit:** raise if operators report leads being marked dropped when they're actually still in-progress; lower or remove if leads sit in-progress indefinitely. The 24-hour pick is an even split between "give the visitor time to come back later that day" and "don't wait so long the nudge is creepy" — re-evaluate once Phase 8's automation execution engine lands and the actual nudge cadence is calibrated.

- **Branch-name vs scope drift — discipline-restoration rule.** During the Phase 4–6 build window (PRs #41–#55, audited in `reference/drift-recovery/pr-deep-audit.md`), branch names frequently failed to describe the shipped work — most notably `debug-admin-access` shipping the entire form-builder feature (PR #46) and `review-dev-plan` shipping the Phase 6 Claude wiring (PR #47). Going forward: if work scope changes meaningfully during a session, **rename the branch** or **state the actual shipped scope in the first line of the PR description**. Merge commit titles are the authoritative record; branch names are advisory only. **Trigger to revisit:** if a future audit shows the pattern recurring, escalate to mandatory PR-description-first-line scope statements.

- **RLS test coverage is mandatory for new RLS policies.** Section A's cross-tenant validation pass built a permanent negative-test harness (`tests/rls/`, `pnpm test:rls`, doc: `reference/rls-test-suite.md`) and closed three holes (migration `0045`). Going forward: **any PR that adds or changes an RLS-protected resource MUST add or update the corresponding tests in `tests/rls/` in the same PR.** A new tenant-scoped table → seed a disposable row in `context.mjs` + a `clientScoped`/`childCrossTenant` call; a new operator-only / per-viewer / capability-gated policy → explicit suite tests. The harness is a negative-test harness — verify persisted state through a verifier client, never trust the attacker's error code (an `INSERT...RETURNING` can raise `42501` while the row was written; see migration `0028`). **Two structural items deferred to a future session** (see `reference/rls-test-suite.md` §4): `force_publish_audit_log_insert` has no website/tenant check (operator-internal, low severity — a junior operator could write an audit row for an out-of-scope website); and `signup_submissions` exists in the DB with RLS policies but has **no migration in `supabase/migrations/`** (migration drift — its policies are safe, but the table should be captured in a migration). **Cross-agency isolation** is not testable on the current single-agency deployment — the operative boundaries are client tenant isolation and junior-operator workspace scoping, both covered.

- **Twilio SMS — V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** The Twilio SMS session shipped one-way alphanumeric SMS sending; each stop-short below is a conscious V1 call. (1) **Per-segment cost is a single flat constant** — `SMS_SEGMENT_COST_EUR = 0.05` (`lib/sms/pricing.ts`), a representative IE/UK transactional rate, NOT a real per-country rate table. The estimate ("~€0.05/send") and the `sms_messages.cost_eur` column are good-enough operator-facing approximations. **Trigger to revisit:** when volume or multi-country destinations matter, replace the constant with a per-country rate lookup. (2) **No two-way SMS** — alphanumeric senders are one-way by nature; there is no inbound webhook, no SMS inbox. Two-way is WhatsApp / a direct call, deferred. (3) **No per-customer phone numbers** — one alphanumeric sender per client; long-code/short-code numbers are not modelled. (4) **Sender registration** — `registerSenderID()` adds the alphanumeric string to the Messaging Service AlphaSender pool (instant, usable in non-regulated countries). The regulated-country Sender ID *registration* (the genuine "1–3 business days" carrier process) is completed by the operator in the Twilio Console — the app does not drive it; "Refresh status" polls Twilio and flips the row to `approved` once the AlphaSender resolves. (5) **Webhook status updates are last-write-wins** — not ordering-aware; an out-of-order older callback could in theory overwrite a newer status. Transactional SMS statuses arrive in order in practice; revisit with a status-rank guard only if operators report a row reverting. (6) **The lead-acknowledgment SMS fires only from the public `/api/forms/submit` flow**, not from the editor test-submit (`submitLead`) — a test submission must not fire a real customer SMS. (7) **`{{client.responseTime}}`** has no schema column — the `send_sms` handler defaults it to `'1 hour'`; override per-send via the job payload's `contextOverrides`. (8) **`sms_messages` / `sms_templates` / `client_sms_senders` have no `tests/rls/` coverage** — the "new RLS resource → new RLS test" rule (above) is triggered by `0059`/`0060`'s new tables; a follow-up RLS-harness pass should add `clientScoped` probes for all three (all are operator-SELECT-or-own-client + service-role-write, low risk, but the rule stands). (9) **Verification gap:** this session could not run the live test SMS / webhook round-trip the brief asks for — no Twilio credentials, no deployed app in the build environment. The pure modules (validator / renderer / estimator) are fully exercisable offline; the Twilio-dependent paths need a deployment with credentials.

- **Meta Ads — V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** V1 shipped the per-tenant Meta Ads integration with a deliberate division of labour: **Webnua handles connection + ingest + observability**; **the operator builds campaigns directly in Meta Ads Manager** (the customer's OAuth grant gives Webnua business-manager access). (1) **No in-app campaign builder** — `LaunchMetaCampaignButton` deep-links to `business.facebook.com/adsmanager/manage/campaigns?act={id}` for the connected ad account. The previous in-app wizard (template picker + Page picker + budget + privacy + landing URL) + the 5-step orchestrator + the 9 trade templates + the `launch` route action were removed once this V1 model settled. The `create*` API functions in `client.ts` are kept exported (un-called) for a future in-app launch path if one ever ships. (2) **Campaign + lead-form ingest are both wired.** `meta_sync_campaigns` (server: `meta-ads/job-handlers.ts`; cron: migration `0075`, hourly at minute 7; immediate trigger after ad-account pick + the "↻ Sync campaigns" button) discovers campaigns built in Ads Manager, upserts both `public.campaigns` + `meta_campaigns`, AND walks each new campaign's ads to resolve its `lead_gen_form_id` (either modern `creative.form_id` or legacy `creative.object_story_spec.link_data.lead_gen_form_id`). The form is then fetched via `GET /{form_id}` and upserted into `meta_lead_forms` with its questions array, and `meta_campaigns.meta_lead_form_id` is patched. After that the existing `meta_sync_leads` cron (every 15 min) attaches automatically — its INNER JOIN on `meta_lead_form_id` now matches. The walk is skipped on subsequent syncs once the form is linked (campaigns rarely switch forms; a manual sync button or a future "clear form" affordance can force a re-resolve). Auxiliary references (`meta_ad_set_id` / `meta_ad_id` / `meta_creative_id`) are still null on ingest — no consumer reads them today. (3) **One ad account per client** — `client_meta_ad_accounts` is UNIQUE on `client_id`. An agency client managing multiple ad accounts needs the unique loosened + a `primary` flag (same forcing function as GBP); defer until the first real customer hits the constraint. (4) **€200 month-1 ad-credit funding is manual** — the `meta_campaigns.created_via` tagging (`webnua_month_1` / `webnua_ongoing` / `external`) is set to `external` on every ingest (Webnua didn't launch them); manual operator accounting drives the €200 transfer from Webnua to the customer's ad account out-of-band (Stripe Transfer / SEPA + the customer manually tops up their Meta funding source). V2 will automate via Meta's funding APIs (which themselves require additional App Review). (5) **Per-row sparkline = lead counts, not spend** — the admin `/campaigns` row sparkline shows the last 14 days of daily lead counts. Spend trends live on the client deep-dive's 4-week chart only. (6) **`client_meta_ad_accounts` / `meta_campaigns` / `meta_ads_insights` / `meta_lead_forms` have no `tests/rls/` coverage** — the "new RLS resource → new RLS test" rule (above) is triggered by migrations `0070`–`0073`; a follow-up RLS-harness pass should add `clientScoped` probes for all four. (7) **Verification gap:** this session could not run the live test (connect a real customer's Meta ad account, verify insights + leads syncing) — Meta business verification + App Review for the sensitive scopes (`ads_management`, `business_management`, `pages_manage_ads`, `leads_retrieval`) is the operator's responsibility and takes weeks. Until App Review approves Webnua for Advanced Access on each scope, only test users added on the Developer dashboard can connect. The pure modules (status mapping, lead-data extraction) work offline; every Meta-dependent path needs the App approved + a customer's real ad account.
- **Stripe billing — V1 scope + minimal-on-purpose choices.** The Stripe billing session shipped subscription billing (€299/month) and deliberately stopped short in several places; each is a conscious V1 call, not an omission. (1) **The €99 + €200 month-1 split is UI copy, not Stripe.** Stripe charges a flat €299 every month; the "€99 platform fee + €200 Meta ad credit" framing lives only in `StripeSubscriptionSection`'s description, and the ad credit is applied OUTSIDE Stripe by the Meta ads integration. There is no month-1 discount Price, Coupon, or column. **Trigger to revisit:** if finance wants the month-1 split to actually appear on the Stripe invoice, that needs a one-off €99 Price + a €200 negative-amount line or a Coupon — a real model change. **Follow-up (dynamic plan info):** the displayed PRICE is no longer hardcoded — `usePlanInfo()` resolves name/amount/currency/interval live from the Stripe Price object (`lib/integrations/stripe/plan-info.ts`, 5-min cache). The €99/€200 month-1 sentence is the ONE remaining hardcoded plan figure — it is sanctioned marketing prose (Stripe never had €99 or €200, so it cannot drift *from Stripe*), but it assumes a €299 total: if the Stripe Price ever changes, that sentence needs a manual copy edit. Move it to a Stripe Price `metadata` key if it should become dynamic too. (2) **Webhook events are applied idempotently but NOT ordering-aware.** Each `customer.subscription.*` event carries the full subscription object, so applying any one gives correct state — but a delayed/out-of-order older `.updated` arriving after a newer one would write stale state. No event-dedup table, no `created`-timestamp compare. **Trigger:** if operators report a status flickering or going stale, add an event-sequence guard. (3) **The payment-failed alert emails every admin-role user**, not operators scoped to that client's `accessible_client_ids` — fine for the single-operator V1; revisit when junior-operator scoping matters. (4) **The Resend send in `notify.ts` is a minimal inline send**, not the full Resend integration (a later session) — when `RESEND_API_KEY` is unset the alert job records `skipped` and the operator sees nothing. (5) **`client_stripe_customers` has no `tests/rls/` coverage** — this session added columns to it but no new table and no new policy (the existing operator-SELECT / service-role-write policy is column-agnostic), so the "new RLS resource → new RLS test" rule above is not triggered. The pre-existing gap (the table got no RLS test when migration `0052` created it) should be closed in a future RLS-harness pass — it is operator-only + service-role-write, low risk. (6) **Pricing is env config** (`STRIPE_PRICE_ID_STANDARD`), not a `stripe_prices` table — promote to a table when there is more than one tier (migration `0057`'s comment carries the plan).

- **Concierge + Pattern B onboarding flow alignment — RESOLVED (two parity audits).** The original parked decision called for a behavioural-parity audit of the two onboarding paths. It has now run twice. **(1) PR #139 (concierge vs wizard).** Audited the operator concierge `CreateClientModal` against the Pattern B wizard at `/onboarding`. Closed five wizard↔concierge divergences: voice axes persistence on Step 4, `derivePalette` industry hint, funnel-offer generation in the wizard, Step 2 mirroring to canonical `clients` columns, and `wizard-assets` brand-seed parity. See the "Pattern B onboarding wizard — RESOLVED" entry above for the full list. **(2) Second audit (conversational vs concierge).** Once conversational onboarding shipped and replaced the wizard as the primary `/sign-up` path (wizard moved to `/sign-up/legacy`), a second audit ran the same parity discipline against the conversational shell. Closed two material gaps: **(a) Concierge now fires `industry-knowledge`.** The conversational path resolves industry knowledge (services, pain points, trust signals, desired outcomes, voice recommendation) after the business-name turn and threads it into every downstream prompt (site/funnel/offer). The concierge path didn't — so for unmapped industries (anything outside the 10 mapped trades), concierge generated against template defaults only. `CreateClientModal` now kicks off `resolveIndustryKnowledge` on the business-step Continue click and holds the in-flight promise on a ref; `runGeneration` awaits with an 8s ceiling fallback.
